1601 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Kramer v. Clark County


No. 34058-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2112



September 26, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Kramer v. Clark County, 135 Wn. App. 1005, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2606 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant developer challenged a decision of the Superior Court (Washington) that denied his petition under the Land Use Petition Act, challenging respondent county's approval of the preliminary plat of respondent neighbor on the ground that the developer had sufficient notice of the public hearing on the neighbor's plat approval but did not have standing to appeal the hearing examiner's decision because he was not a party of record.


OVERVIEW: The developer claimed that the public notice of the hearing was misleading, and thus defective, because it included a plan that showed a road connecting to his property that was later deleted. The developer also argued that the county should have required his neighbor to build a cross-circulation road allowing access to the developer's property as a condition for approval, and additional frontage improvements on an access street. The court held that the developer had standing to appeal the hearing examiner's decision because the developer became a party of record when he signed a sign-in sheet that was titled with the general subject matter. The court also found that the county provided sufficient notice of the hearing because any defect in the initial notice was cured when the county provided the amended plat proposal at the first public hearing. The court held that hearing examiner did not err by not requiring the neighbor to build a cross-circulation road because the road would not serve a public purpose, thus the county could not constitutionally require it as a condition for approving the plat. The court found that the developer waived the issue of the frontage requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the superior court decision.

 

1602 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Smissaert


NO. 54483-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2104



September 25, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Smissaert, 135 Wn. App. 1001, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2588 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendant's motions to sever offenses, the trial court of the State of Washing convicted defendant of raping his five year old neighbor but acquitted him of raping his six year old son. Defendant was given an indeterminate sentence of 108 months to life in prison. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended the trial court's refusal to sever the offenses required a new trial. The appellate court disagreed, finding that the trial court's conscientious evaluation of the relevant factors and subsequent ruling was not an abuse of discretion. Further, the trial court expressly reserved Wash. R. Evid. 404(b) rulings and came to the conclusion that severance should be denied even if much of the evidence was not cross-admissible. Defendant pointed to no portion of the record at which the trial court told the jury which evidence related to which count. Defendant's statement that he may have accidentally touched the neighbor did not change defendant's defense of general denial. The jury persuasively demonstrated that it could put aside propensity inferences by acquitting defendant of raping his son. There was no reasonable probability that the jury would have acquitted defendant on the count regarding the neighbor had the trial court granted the motion to sever; thus, any such error was harmless.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1603 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Annyas


No. 55512-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2106



September 25, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Annyas, 135 Wn. App. 1001, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2590 (2006)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Annyas v. Cole, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 115461 (W.D. Wash., Sept. 8, 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Bartholomew, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 832 (Wash. Ct. App., Apr. 25, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of a Washington trial court convicting her of first-degree kidnapping and second-degree attempted murder.


OVERVIEW: The victim, defendant's mother, told her rescuers that defendant and defendant's boyfriend beat her up, forced her into a vehicle, tied her up with jumper cables, and left her in the woods lying in a puddle of water. The victim did not testify at trial. On appeal, the court held that the trial court did not violate defendant's Sixth Amendment rights by admitting into evidence the victim's hearsay statements to her rescuers as excited utterances because the statements were not testimonial. The victim's statements were made while she was under the stress of the recent kidnapping and assault, the rescuers were not involved in law enforcement, and there was no indication that the victim made the statements for prosecutorial purposes, especially in light of her refusal to involve law enforcement. Even though the trial court violated defendant's Sixth Amendment rights by admitting into evidence the victim's statements to medical treatment providers, as those statements were testimonial, the error was harmless because they were almost entirely cumulative of the more detailed and properly admitted statements to the rescuers.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

 

1604 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Leonard


No. 33717-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2088



September 19, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Leonard, 134 Wn. App. 1069, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2585 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of a trial court (Washington), which sentenced him following his conviction of attempted first degree burglary. Defendant argued that the trial court lacked statutory authority to empanel a jury to determine whether he was armed with a firearm at the time of that crime, a fact that resulted in the imposition of a sentencing enhancement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the firearm enhancement was completely invalid because the trial court submitted the special verdict question to the jury without specific legislative authority. On appeal, the court noted that defendant did not object to the trial court's special verdict procedure below. Because defendant's claim was statutory error, not constitutional error, defendant failed to preserve the issue as set forth in Wash. R. App. P. 2.5(a) and waived any claim of error. The court next agreed that the sentencing court improperly imposed a 60-month instead of a 36-month enhancement. The required firearm enhancement for a class B felony was 36 months pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.533(3)(b). The trial court erred when it instead imposed the 60-month enhancement required for class A felonies pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.533(3)(a). Attempted first degree burglary was a class B felony, not a class A felony, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.28.020(3)(b), 52.020(2). The court then determined that the trial court erred by adding a period of community custody to his sentence in an ex parte procedure without notice a day after the contested sentencing hearing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the firearm enhancement special verdict and remanded the case for imposition of the correct firearm sentence enhancement of 36 months and for an adversarial hearing on the State's proposed sentence modifications, including community custody.

 

1605 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Wahleithner v. Thompson


No. 57101-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


134 Wn. App. 931; 143 P.3d 321; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2065



September 18, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed the denial of his petition for writ of habeas corpus by the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) after his suspended sentences for driving under the influence (DUI) and drug charges were revoked.


OVERVIEW: Finding that the inmate had made no attempt to comply with the treatment requirements for the three years of probation, the trial court revoked the suspended sentences on all cause numbers, imposed all remaining time, and ordered that the terms be served consecutively. The remaining time totaled approximately 44 months. The inmate argued that his total sentence constituted cruel punishment in violation of Wash. Const. art. I, § 14. The court of appeals disagreed. Among other specifics of the inmate's extensive history of noncompliance, he had attended a probation interview while intoxicated. The inmate's crimes included three DUIs and hit and run. Those were offenses that threatened or caused injury to persons or property. The inmate's repeated failure to complete substance abuse treatment also related to public safety, given that he seemed determined to drive while intoxicated. The inmate served consecutive time only because he consistently failed to take steps that might have lessened the threat he posed to persons and property. Therefore, the sentences were not grossly disproportionate to the offenses.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1606 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



KMS Fin. Servs., Inc. v. City of Seattle


No. 56808-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


135 Wn. App. 489; 146 P.3d 1195; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2075



September 18, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Order Granting Motion to Publish dated October 30, 2006.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at KMS Fin. Servs. v. City of Seattle, 134 Wn. App. 1067, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2575 (2006)
Review denied by KMS Fin. Servs., Inc. v. City of Seattle, 161 Wn.2d 1011, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 617 (Wash., Sept. 6, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city challenged a judgment of the trial court (Washington) that denied the city's motion and granted respondent business taxpayer's motion for summary judgment in the taxpayer's action seeking a refund of business and occupation (B&O) taxes imposed under Seattle, Wash., Mun. Code § 5.45.050 on the entire gross income of the taxpayer, which included income generated outside the city.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer claimed the city had improperly attempted to tax income derived from activities outside the city's borders; and that the city's different treatment of the commissions for stockbrokers and real estate brokers violated the federal and state equal protection clauses. The court found that although the taxpayer did not maintain "offices" outside the city, it was undisputed that some of its registered representatives generated sales outside the city and the state. The court held that the city's attribution of the entire proceeds of the taxpayer's registered representatives to the taxpayer's city office merely because that was the taxpayer's sole office violated the external consistency requirement of federal commerce clause jurisprudence. Rather, the taxpayer was entitled to apportionment to ensure that the city taxed only its fair share of income generated within the city. The court rejected the taxpayer's claim that the city's tax violated equal protection, holding that a classification based solely on a difference in the method of operation of a particular kind of business was permissible. The court found that neither party had correctly identified the measure of the tax.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the trial court's order granting the taxpayer's motion and denying the city's motion, and remanded the case for calculation of the correct tax amount because either party had correctly identified the measure of the tax.

 

1607 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Thomas


No. 55556-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


135 Wn. App. 474; 144 P.3d 1178; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2077



September 18, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals October 16, 2006.   [***1] Order Granting Appellant's Motion to Publish dated October 16, 2006


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Thomas, 161 Wn.2d 1009, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 627 (2007)
Appeal after remand at State v. Thomas, 2009 Wash. App. LEXIS 2789 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 9, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Thomas, 134 Wn. App. 1065, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2568 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant contended that the decision by the trial court, Washington, to include out-of-state convictions in the calculation of his offender score violated his constitutional and due process rights to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the sentencing court's decision to include out-of-state convictions in the calculation of his offender score violated his constitutional and due process rights to a jury trial. In the alternative, defendant argued that the State failed to prove the out-of-state California convictions for burglary and receiving stolen property were comparable to a Washington crime. The appellate court held that the trial court did not deprive defendant of his constitutional and due process rights to a jury trial by engaging in a limited fact finding to determine comparability between an out-of-state conviction and the in-state convictions. However, the appellate court did vacate defendant's sentence and remanded the matter for resentencing because based on the record before it, the appellate court could not tell if defendant stipulated or admitted to an unlawful entry for his California convictions pursuant to Cal. Penal Code § 459. Thus, the State did not meet its burden that the 1980 or 1982 California burglary convictions were factually comparable to Washington's burglary statute. Thus, the matter was remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was vacated and remanded for resentencing.

 

1608 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Stacey v. Florendo


No. 31767-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1969



September 12, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Stacey v. Florendo, 134 Wn. App. 1060, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2550 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court denied appellant mother's motion to dismiss respondent possible father's petition to establish paternity because it found that Wash. Rev. Code § 26.26.530 was unconstitutional. The mother appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that the two-year statute of limitations of Wash. Rev. Code § 26.26.530 began to run on June 13, 2002, and the possible father's petition on October 21, 2003, was timely filed. Although the appellate court affirmed the trial court's ruling denying the motion to dismiss because it was not barred by the statute of limitations, the trial court had to determine whether it was in the best interests of the child for the parentage action to continue. The appellate court did not decide whether Wash. Rev. Code § 26.26.530 was unconstitutional for another day when the issue was properly before it. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in appointing a guardian ad litem for the child, Wash. Rev. Code § 26.26.555(2). The trial court acted within its discretion in not awarding attorney fees to the mother.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1609 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Nguyen


No. 55443-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


134 Wn. App. 863; 142 P.3d 1117; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1952



September 11, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review pending at State v. Nguyen, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 102 (Wash., Jan. 30, 2007)
Review denied by State v. Troung V. Nguyen, 163 Wn.2d 1053, 187 P.3d 752, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 721 (2008)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Nguyen v. Washington, 555 U.S. 1055, 129 S. Ct. 644, 172 L. Ed. 2d 626, 2008 U.S. LEXIS 8551 (2008)
Related proceeding at In re Pers. Restraint of Truong V. Nguyen, 152 Wn. App. 1032, 2009 Wash. App. LEXIS 2549 (2009)
Habeas corpus proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Nguyen v. Glebe, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 186079 (W.D. Wash., Dec. 13, 2012)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicting him of three counts of burglary in the first degree, five counts of robbery in the first degree and two counts of assault of a child in the second degree, and imposing a standard range sentence of 135 months, together with consecutive firearm enhancements totaling 492 months, for a total term of 627 months.


OVERVIEW: Defendant participated in three home invasion robberies. In each instance, an accomplice was armed with a firearm. Defendant argued that the trial court was without authority to impose the enhancement, because there was no authorized procedure for submitting the firearm question to the jury. The appellate court overruled defendant's argument that there was no procedure in place for the imposition of a firearm enhancement and none could be judicially created, finding that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.602 amply authorized the firearm finding. To the extent express authority was required, the deadly weapon special verdict statute supplied it. Also, the appellate court overruled defendant's assertion that under the U.S. Supreme Court Blakely decision, imposition of multiple firearm enhancements violated double jeopardy. A jury found defendant guilty on each count and entered a special verdict finding that defendant or an accomplice was armed with a firearm at the time of the crimes. This procedure complied fully with the U.S. Supreme Court Blakely decision.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1610 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Adams


No. 55539-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1953



September 11, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Adams, 134 Wn. App. 1059, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2543 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the trial court (Washington), which convicted defendant of two counts of first-degree rape of a child, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.073. Defendant challenged certain evidentiary decisions related to the hearsay statements made by the alleged victim, defendant's five-year-old nephew.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of first-degree rape of his five-year old nephew. After a pre-trial determination was made, the court allowed into evidence out-of-court statements made by the nephew to his mother, his grandmother, and a child interview specialist, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.120. Additionally, the nephew, who was six at the time of trial, testified about the alleged incident, but claimed that he had forgotten about specifics. The court held that defendant's rights under the Confrontation Clause, as set forth in U.S. Const. amend. VI and Wash. Const. art. I, § 22, were not violated. The nephew's testimony about the alleged sexual contact and his hearsay statements to the three other witnesses adequately met the requirements of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.120 and the Confrontation Clause. The court held that the prosecutor's statements during closing, even if based on impermissible hearsay, were not so flagrant that they could not have been neutralized through an admonition. It was not error for the trial court to replay the DVD to the jury on one occasion at their request. Defendant's sentence as a persistent offender was appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the district court.

 

1611 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fields


No. 32738-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1936



September 6, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Fields, 134 Wn. App. 1055, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2527 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 97-1-01054-1. Hon. Amma M Laurie.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the revocation by the Superior Court of Kitsap County, Washington of his special sex offender sentencing alternative (SSOSA) under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(8)(a)(ii) (1997) and reinstatement of his 97.5-month standard range sentence after his community corrections officer (CCO) discovered a marijuana-growing operation in defendant's backyard.


OVERVIEW: When the CCO was visiting defendant where he lived with his mother, the CCO looked into a tool shed with defendant's permission and discovered the operation. When police searched the residence, they found pornographic materials. The court affirmed and held that any error in admitting testimony of the CCO from an incident report that the officers found pornography in the laundry room was clearly harmless because defendant admitted that he violated the conditions of his SSOSA by possessing triple X videos. Defendant's admission verified the hearsay statement, and the trial court did not rely on unverified evidence in making its decision to revoke his SSOSA. Further, defendant's due process rights to adequate notice and an opportunity to be heard were protected. The court also held that the applicable revocation standard, former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(8)(a)(vi), did not require the court to consider the violating offender's best interests. Because defendant was on SSOSA, his sentence was suspended under § 9.94A.120(8)(a)(ii), and § 9.94A.120(8)(a)(vi) required that he receive credit for "confinement time" upon revocation, not for the time he spent in community custody.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

1612 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Theel


No. 33703-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1940



September 6, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Theel, 134 Wn. App. 1056, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2533 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for misdemeanor harassment by the trial court, Washington.


OVERVIEW: The facts revealed that after defendant started dating the victim, he sprayed "Oust" air freshener into her eyes. The next day, he threw hot coffee on her back. When she tried to call the police to report his abuse, he told her, "You're done, you're going to die," and he ran his finger across his throat. Defendant was charged with fourth degree felony harassment--threats to kill (domestic violence) contrary to Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.020(1)(a)(i) and .020(2)(b). Despite charging defendant with harassment contrary only to § 9A.46.020(1)(a)(i), the court instructed the jury that a person committed the crime of harassment when he or she violated § 9A.46.020(1)(a)(i) or § 9A.46.020(1)(a)(iv). Thus, the trial court's "to convict" instruction included § 9A.46.020(1)(a)(iv) as an alternative means for convicting defendant. The appellate court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded for a new trial because § 9A.46.020(1)(a)(iv) was not a lesser included offense of § 9A.46.020(1)(a)(i) as it contained elements that were not necessary for § 9A.46.020(1)(a)(i). As the State offered no evidence that the instructional error was not harmless, it was presumed to be prejudicial.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed, and the matter was remanded for a new trial.

 

1613 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Stannard


No. 33227-2-II (Consolidated with 33229-9-II & 33230-2-II)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


134 Wn. App. 828; 142 P.3d 641; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1921



August 29, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted in the Jefferson County Superior Court, Washington, of illegally hunting black bear using bait, contrary to Wash. Rev. Code § 77.15.245. Defendants appealed their convictions.


OVERVIEW: In 1996, Washington voters approved Initiative 655, which made it a gross misdemeanor to take, hunt, or attract black bears with bait, or to hunt bears, cougars, bobcat or lynx with dogs. The legislature codified Initiative 655 at Wash. Rev. Code § 77.15.245. Defendants argued that the initiative violated Wash. Const. art. II, § 19, by embracing more than one subject and by failing to express the initiative's subject in its title. The court concluded that the initiative's title was general. The initiative's incidental subjects banned different specific methods of hunting different animals; they differed only in the specific prohibited hunting methods and the targeted animals. Thus, the incidental subjects were sufficiently related to satisfy the single subject rule of Wash. Const. art. II, § 19. The court also concluded that the initiative did not violate the subject-in-title rule of Wash. Const. art. II, § 19. A voter would understand from the initiative's title that penalties, including license suspensions, would likely follow from hunting black bear with bait or hunting bear, cougar, bobcat, or lynx using dogs.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

 

1614 of 2278 DOCUMENTS




Mitchell v. PEMCO Mut. Ins. Co.


No. 55834-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


134 Wn. App. 723; 142 P.3d 623; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1860



August 28, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Mitchell v. Pemco Mut. Ins. Co., 2007 Wash. LEXIS 443 (Wash., June 6, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant class representative challenged a decision from the Superior Court in King County (Washington), which entered judgment in favor of appellee employer in a wage and salary dispute under the Washington Minimum Wage Act (MWA).


OVERVIEW: The employer contended that adjusters were exempt from overtime pay. The trial court determined that two classes were not exempt. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the payment of overtime was required under Wash. Rev. Code § 49.46.010(5)(c) unless the employees worked in an bona fide executive, administrative, or professional capacity. Next, the employer met the two tests to show that the two classes of adjusters were exempt from the MWA's overtime exemptions. Under the duties test, the adjusters were administrative under Wash. Admin. Code § 296-128-520(1), (3) because they performed office work directly related to business operations, and they customarily and regularly exercised discretion and independent judgment. As to the salary basis test, the adjusters were salaried employees, despite the contention that certain deductions were taken. Further, the reclassification of other adjusters was not relevant to the case. Finally, the trial court did not err by clarifying the class because of the three-year statute of limitations under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.16.130 since the first lawsuit had been dismissed.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.


 

1615 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Chavez


No. 33240-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


134 Wn. App. 657; 142 P.3d 1110; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1849



August 22, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at State v. Chavez, 163 P.3d 795, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 455 (Wash., 2007)
Review granted by State v. Chavez, 160 Wn.2d 1021, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 480 (2007)
Affirmed by State v. Chavez, 163 Wn.2d 262, 180 P.3d 1250, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 262 (Wash., Mar. 20, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a juvenile, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Clallam County (Washington), which convicted him of second-degree assault in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.021.


OVERVIEW: The juvenile appealed his conviction for second-degree assault, and the juvenile argued that his right to a jury trial was violated. The court disagreed and affirmed, stating that the Juvenile Justice Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 13.04, did not violate Wash. Const. art. I, §§ 21 and 22, or U.S. Const. amend. VI. He did not have a right to a jury trial in juvenile proceedings. Additionally, the second-degree assault statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.021(1)(c), stated that a defendant was guilty of assault if he assaulted another with a deadly weapon. Because the statute did not define assault, courts supplied the common law definition. Consistent with their history, the legislative and judicial branches cooperated in defining the offense of assault. The juvenile presented no authority to show that the established practice was unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1616 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stinson


No. 23540-8-III (consolidated with No. 24630-2-III)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1797



August 15, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Stinson, 134 Wn. App. 1041, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2246 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 04-1-01109-5. Judge signing: GREGORY D. SYPOLT (Suppression Hearing), SALVATORE F. COZZA (Trial). Date filed: August 11, 2004 (Suppression Hearing), October 29, 2004 (Trial).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, convicted defendant of possession of cocaine and heroin. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the deputies did not have a specific, articulable reason to justify his warrantless detention. He also argued that his arrest was unlawful. The appellate court noted that the deputies did not stop the vehicle due to suspicions directed at defendant. The deputies testified that they thought the bubble van had been used for illicit drug deliveries and that another person was the driver. The deputies based their suspicions on tips from a confidential informant, the complaints of neighbors, and their own surveillance. The deputies' suspicion that the other person was driving the van and that he had been or was currently engaged in criminal conduct was reasonable. This suspicion justified a stop of the van to identify the driver and conduct a brief investigation. For defendant to argue that his arrest for driving while license suspended in the third degree was invalid, he had to show that his license was suspended for the one reason under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1) that could be unconstitutional under Moore, but defendant did not do so. The fact that defendant was driving while his license was suspended was sufficient to establish probable cause for his arrest.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1617 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Young


No. 23700-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1798



August 15, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Young, 134 Wn. App. 1041, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2247 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: ADAMS. Docket No(s): 04-1-00068-8. Judge signing: RICHARD W. MILLER. Date filed: December 13, 2004.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Adams County (Washington), which convicted him of possession of heroin and possession of drug paraphernalia.


OVERVIEW: A trooper stopped defendant's vehicle for speeding. Defendant was riding in the vehicle as a passenger at the time, and both defendant and the driver of the vehicle had suspended licenses. The trooper impounded the vehicle, and an inventory search of the vehicle prior to impoundment uncovered heroin and used drug paraphernalia. Defendant was subsequently convicted of possession of heroin and possession of drug paraphernalia, and the court affirmed on appeal, concluding that the search prior to impoundment was lawful. Defendant was initially arrested for violating Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342, which was one of the traffic offenses where impoundment was authorized under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.55.113. The trooper had the authority to arrest defendant pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 10.31.100(3)(e) and had the authority to impound defendant's car as part of the enforcement of traffic regulations. It followed then that the impoundment of defendant's vehicle was lawful.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1618 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Kern


No. 23781-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1799



August 15, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Kern, 134 Wn. App. 1042, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2248 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: WALLA WALLA. Docket No(s): 03-1-00350-3. Judge signing: ROBERT L. ZAGELOW. Date filed: January 3, 2005.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Walla Walla County, Washington, convicted defendant of first-degree criminal mistreatment and failure to report. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court abused its discretion in denying her new trial motion where she contended that she received ineffective assistance of counsel. The appellate court found that defendant's counsel's strategic and tactical decisions did not support an ineffective assistance claim. Defendant did not show either deficient performance or prejudice. Defendant waived her due process argument that she did not receive a written copy of the amended information by failing to request one. Defendant did not show the second trial occurred outside the speedy trial period applicable to the initial charge. The two offenses were not the "same conduct" for purposes of mandatory joinder. Sufficient evidence showed that defendant failed to provide the victim with contractually required basic hygiene, a basic necessity of life under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.42.010(1). The jury could find that defendant knew the victim was being neglected and failed to report it. The trial court merely restated the prior instructions and did not suggest to the jury the decision it ought to reach. Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.42.010 was not unconstitutional as the terms of defendant's contract were clear.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1619 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Dependency of V.R.R.


No. 55954-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


134 Wn. App. 573; 141 P.3d 85; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1786



August 14, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a decision from the Superior Court in Skagit County (Washington), which entered an order in favor of respondent Washington Department of Social and Health Services (DSHS) by terminating his parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The day prior to trial on a termination case, an attorney was appointed to represent the father. Although DSHS agreed to a continuance, it opposed the request when the father failed to appear at trial. The trial court denied the continuance, and the father's rights were terminated based on the grounds under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.34.180. Thereafter, he sought review. In reversing, the appellate court found that the father did not forfeit his right to counsel by not seeking a more timely appointment of counsel and by failing to appear at trial. The father had a right to counsel in the termination proceedings under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.34.090(2) based on his fundamental liberty interest in the care and custody of his children under Wash. Const. art. I, § 3 and the Fourteenth Amendment. A forfeiture of this right was only found in cases involving serious misconduct or extremely dilatory conduct. Next, the father had the right to effective representation under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.101.005. The attorney was unable to provide effective assistance of counsel without additional time to prepare, despite having represented the father in a prior dependency proceeding.


OUTCOME: The decision was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

 

1620 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


In re Det. of Lee


No. 31900-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1775



August 11, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Det. of Lee, 134 Wn. App. 1031, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2207 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a committed individual (appellant), sought review of the decision of the trial court (Washington), which found that he was a sexually violent predator and ordered him committed.


OVERVIEW: Appellant had pled guilty to first-degree rape. That rape was his only conviction for a sex offense. He served 96 months for that offense, and just before his release, the State petitioned to commit him under Wash. Rev. Code ch. 71.09 as a sexually violent predator. The jury found that he was a sexually violent predator, and the trial court ordered him committed. The court affirmed on appeal, stating that although it was error to admit a doctor's hypothetical under Wash. R. Evid. 702 and 703, the error was harmless. There was more than sufficient evidence to support the State's burden of proving, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.020(16), beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant was likely to engage in predatory acts of sexual violence if not confined to a security facility. Using the proper scoring rules, the three actuarial tests that the doctor used predicted that the likelihood appellant would reoffend was 52 percent, 73 percent, and 75 percent. Those percentages were more than enough to prove that he was likely to reoffend. The altered scores only raised the later two scores by 15 percent and 25 percent respectively. The hypothetical was redundant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1621 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Plemmons v. Pierce County


No. 33072-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


134 Wn. App. 449; 140 P.3d 601; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1689



August 8, 2006, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Corrected by, Reconsideration granted by Plemmons v. Pierce County, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2380 (Wash. Ct. App., Oct. 31, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent sued appellant county for federal constitutional and state statutory civil rights violations based on the county's post-arraignment strip search performed while respondent was in custody awaiting release on bail. The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, granted summary judgment in favor of respondent. The county appealed, and discretionary review was granted.


OVERVIEW: The State of Washington charged respondent with felony forgery, and she was taken into custody during a traffic stop in Montana, her state of residence. Respondent posted bail and traveled to Washington to appear for arraignment and a bail hearing. In Washington, respondent asked for release on her personal recognizance because she was a victim of identity theft, and had already posted $ 10,000 bail when arrested on the charge in Montana. The superior court denied the request, imposed bail of $ 5,000, and ordered that she be taken into custody. The county conducted an automatic strip search in accordance with its policy based on Wash. Rev. Code ch. 10.79. After determining that respondent was the innocent victim of identity theft, and not a forger, the county dropped the forgery charges against her. The appellate court ruled that respondent did not meet the statutory criteria for a warrantless strip search, and therefore, the county acted without authorization in strip searching her under its automatic strip search policy. A person in custody pending release on bail was entitled to the protections of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 10.79.130 through 10.79.160.


OUTCOME: Summary judgment was affirmed, and the portion of the superior court's judgment that there was no statutory violation by the county was vacated.

 

1622 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Marriage of Anderson


No. 33507-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


134 Wn. App. 506; 141 P.3d 80; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1691



August 8, 2006, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The parties were divorced and appellant father was awarded custody of the child he had with respondent mother, and visitation rights with his stepdaughter, who was in the custody of the mother's parents. When the mother's parents disallowed the father to see the other child, he petitioned for enforcement of his visitation rights with his stepdaughter. The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, denied the father's petition, and he appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the father contended the trial court erred in deciding that he had no visitation rights with his stepdaughter based on a ruling from a prior supreme court ruling. The appellate court agreed, finding that the father already had an order allowing visitation, the one issued in the dissolution action. That is, without running awry of the prior ruling in question, the father could enforce the original parenting plan order because it had not been amended or vacated, and because he had exercised his visitation rights since the parenting plan was ordered. Furthermore, given the important role the father played during his stepdaughter's formative years and his exercise of his visitation rights since the dissolution, the appellate court could not terminate his visitation rights without good reason. Such an abrupt severance of a familial relationship would only entail inequitable consequences. Accordingly, the prior ruling in question did not retroactively revoke the father's visitation rights under his parenting plan. Absent finding that it was no longer in the stepdaughter's best interest, the father should have been allowed to exercise his visitation rights.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and the case was remanded for further proceedings to enforce the father's visitation rights under the prior parenting plan.

 

1623 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. David


No. 33403-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


134 Wn. App. 470; 141 P.3d 646; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1705



August 8, 2006 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. David, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 437 (Wash., June 5, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Clallam County (Washington) that convicted him for vehicular homicide under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.520, resulting from his speeding vehicle's collision with another vehicle while driving with his blood alcohol level at twice the legal limit in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.502. An enhanced sentence was imposed based on defendant's 4 prior driving under the influence (DUI) convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the vehicular homicide statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.520, violated the separation of powers doctrine. The court held that the vehicular homicide statute did not violate the separation of powers doctrine because in enacting Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.04.060, the Legislature indicated its intent to continue the then-existing practice of judicially defining proximate causation; therefore, incorporating the common law definition of "proximate causation" into the vehicular homicide statute was not an improper judicial encroachment on legislative powers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment that convicted and sentenced defendant for vehicular homicide.

 

1624 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Welfare of C.B.


No. 32948-4-II (consolidated with, No. 32951-4-II and No. 32958-1-II)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


134 Wn. App. 336; 139 P.3d 1119; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1653



August 1, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Kitsap County, Washington, terminating her parental rights to her three children.


OVERVIEW: The father was murdered in February 1997, and since July 1994, there have been six referrals to State authorities on behalf of the children in Washington and two referrals in Texas alleging physical abuse and neglect, medical neglect, sexual abuse, and drug use. The mother argued Wash. Rev. Code §§ 13.34.180 and 13.34.190, were facially unconstitutional. The appellate court ruled that because Wash. Rev. Code §§ 13.34.180 and 13.34.190 required the State to prove in every instance that its request to terminate parental rights was based on prevention of harm or risk of harm to children, they survived strict scrutiny and were constitutional. Also, the trial court did not err in terminating the mother's parental rights. The uncertainty of the mother's success and the considerable time necessary to complete the necessary services were significant obstacles that clearly diminish the children's prospects for long-term integration and permanence. There was little likelihood that conditions would be remedied so that the children could be returned to the mother in the near future.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1625 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nord


No. 55606-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1640



July 31, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Nord, 134 Wn. App. 1015, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2036 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a Washington trial court convicted defendant of malicious mischief in the second degree, defendant moved for a new trial and arrest of judgment. The trial court denied defendant's motion, reiterating that the State met its burden of proving that defendant was not legally justified in cutting down his neighbors' gate and that he acted maliciously in doing so. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence of malice to support the conviction, that pursuant to his easement he had a right to enter on his neighbors' property and cut the gate down, and that he attempted to gain access by other means by cutting the lock off the gate, but this attempt proved futile. Thus, defendant claimed he was acting within his legal rights when he cut down the locked gate because it was an unreasonable burden upon the easement. The appellate court agreed, finding that while the neighbors owned the land on which the easement was located, they did not have the right to unreasonably interfere with defendant's use of the easement. By locking the gate, the neighbors unreasonably interfered with the easement and defendant had a right to gain access. There was no requirement that defendant had to resort to other legal process before attempting to gain access to his easement. Further, substantial evidence did not exist to support the finding that defendant threw or tossed the gate against the neighbors' house after cutting it down. Thus, the conclusion that defendant acted with malice was unsupported by the evidence.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was reversed.

 

1626 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



TR Camano, Inc. v. Island County


No. 56692-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1666



July 31, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at TR Camano, Inc. v. Island County, 134 Wn. App. 1020, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2055 (2006)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county sought review of a decision of the Skagit County Superior Court (Washington), which reversed and remanded to the County Planning Department a decision, affirmed by the hearing officer, that rejected an application filed by respondent developer for the placement of hotels on an island and which further rejected the developer's request for a zoning code interpretation to permit the plan to go forward.


OVERVIEW: The developer sought to build two small free-standing hotels on island property that was zoned rural village. The developer submitted a site plan application and requested a zoning code interpretation to permit the plan to go forward. The county planning department rejected both, and the hearing examiner affirmed. A second interpretation request was also rejected. The lower court reversed and remanded for further interpretations. The court agreed with the county that the decision of the lower court needed to be overturned and the decision of the hearing officer reinstated, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C.130(1)(a). The hearing officer properly applied the doctrine of res judicata to the matters that were before him, because the second code interpretation request was the same as the first that had been rejected. The court also found that the developer's constitutional claim should not have been remanded because the agency was without authority to rule on a constitutional question. There was no violation of Wash. Const. art. I, § 12, because an earlier "spot zoning" decision on another island did not justify additional spot rezoning in favor of the developer.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the superior court.

Huckleberry Trust v. City of Medina


No. 55937-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1523



July 24, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 04-2-10447-5. Date filed: 02/25/2005. Judge signing: Hon Mary I Yu.
Huckleberry Trust v. City of Medina, 134 Wn. App. 1007, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2007 (2006)



DISPOSITION: We affirm. Fees and costs are granted to the City of Medina and the Burnsteads pursuant to RAP 18.1.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant realty trust sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of King County, (Washington), which upheld the decision of respondent city to deny a variance and a building permit for a playhouse structure placed by the residents on the trust's property, pursuant to the review procedure under Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70C.130.


OVERVIEW: The residents lived on property that was owned by the trust. The residents placed a child's playhouse on the property. Respondent abutting landowners complained to the city, and the city found that the residents and the trust had violated building permit and setback violations and had exceeded the structural coverage limits for the property. The city subsequently denied the request for variances filed by the trust and the residents, and the lower court upheld the denial. Affirming, the court held that the playhouse was subject to the city's zoning code because it met the definition of a structural coverage under Medina, Wash. Code § 17.12.010(B), and did not fall within one of the seven specifically enumerated exceptions for a structure. The trust was not entitled to a variance because the seven conditions enumerated in Medina, Wash. Code § 2.78.065(A) were not met. The court also rejected the trust's arguments that others in the vicinity enjoyed greater property rights over the trust or that the public welfare required the variance. The court found that the zoning codes did not violate the trust's due process or equal protection rights.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the variance.

State v. Didier


No. 33376-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1452



July 11, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Didier, 133 Wn. App. 1046, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1904 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions for residential burglary and violation of a restraining order by the trial court, Washington.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's estranged wife obtained a restraining order against defendant, and defendant was ordered to vacate the family home by January 2. Defendant did vacate the home, and while defendant was away, the wife, accompanied by relatives and friends, re-entered the home and hired a locksmith to change the locks. Before the locksmith could do so, however, defendant returned. Seeing his car, the wife hid in the bathroom while her friends locked the doors. Defendant entered through a window, telling the others present to leave his home and demanding to speak to his wife. He asserted that the restraining order barring him from the home after January 2nd was invalid because of his "revision." The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction as the trial court's instruction using the text of Pierce County, Wash., Super. Ct. R. 7(g)(2) was not a comment on the evidence in violation of Wash. Const. art. IV, § 16. Additionally, the instruction did not obstruct or comment upon defendant's theory of the case. The appellate court also held that there was no prosecutorial misconduct by using an analogy involving physical spousal abuse when it drew attention to his possession of guns.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

State v. Warren


No. 54032-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


134 Wn. App. 44; 138 P.3d 1081; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1438



July 10, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Warren, 161 Wn.2d 1001, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 591 (2007)
Affirmed by State v. Warren, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 1053 (Wash., Nov. 20, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him, in two trials, of one count of child molestation in the first degree of his 8-year-old stepdaughter and three counts of rape of his 14-year-old stepdaughter.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his molestation and rape convictions, but the court affirmed. Because the child interview specialist and the police detective did not explicitly say they believed the younger victim, any error in admitting their testimony was not manifest constitutional error that could be raised for the first time on appeal. Additionally, the trial court's evidentiary rulings were not an abuse of discretion; there was not a substantial likelihood the outcome of the two trials was affected by improper arguments of the prosecutor, and defendant was not denied his constitutional right to a fair trial. The trial court's decision to prohibit contact with his wife, the victim's mother, as a condition of his sentence, was not an unconstitutional restriction. The detective was permitted to testify under Wash. R. Evid. 701 based on her observations of the wife. Testimony about the wife's reaction of being more protective of defendant than concerned about the younger victim's allegations offered an alternative explanation about the timing of the disclosures and why the younger victim did not tell her mother about the abuse.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1630 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gilbert


No. 24100-9-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1436



July 6, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Gilbert, 133 Wn. App. 1045, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1898 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Benton County. Docket No: 05-1-00276-3. Date filed: 05/03/2005. Judge signing: Hon. Craig J Matheson.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with (1) unlawful possession of payment instruments under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.56.320(2)(a)(i), and (2) identity theft under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.35.020(3) and convicted of both counts in a bench trial in the Superior Court of Benton County, Washington.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was initially arrested as there was an outstanding warrant against him. In a search incident to the arrest, the police found several blank checks bearing the name of someone other than defendant. A subsequent search of defendant's home also revealed tax documents belonging to other persons. Defendant claimed on appeal that Wash. Rev. Code § 9.35.020 was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The appellate court affirmed defendant's convictions as the definitions in Wash. Rev. Code § 9.35.005 provided police and prosecutors with adequate standards for enforcement. Here, defendant was found to be in possession of tax documents. He was not a tax preparer, and police investigation revealed he was not authorized to possess those documents. The statute provided police with enough guidance to enforce the law in a fair and just manner. The appellate court also held Wash. Rev. Code § 9.35.020 was not overbroad as the legislature had a had a reasonable basis in not seeking to distinguish between persons with consent or permission, and those without because the statute sought to include persons with consent to be in possession, who nonetheless used the documents fraudulently.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

 

1631 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Wade


No. 22904-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


133 Wn. App. 855; 138 P.3d 168; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1420



July 5, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Wade, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 370 (Wash., May 1, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Cowlitz County. Superior Court Docket No. 97-1-00547-4. Date Filed In Superior Court: February 3, 1998. Superior Court Judge Signing: Don McCulloch.
State v. Wade, 125 Wn. App. 1016, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 773 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington) of first degree robbery and second degree assault. After the judgment was affirmed on direct appeal, defendant again appealed, contending that he was entitled to another direct appeal because counsel had erroneously filed an Anders brief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that he was entitled to a new direct appeal because the appellate court erroneously accepted counsel's Anders brief and permitted counsel to withdraw. The court of appeals disagreed. Defendant was not denied his right to counsel on direct appeal. Appointed counsel and the appellate court followed the Anders procedure -- counsel was permitted to withdraw only after counsel and the appellate court reviewed the trial record, counsel and defendant each filed briefing, the appellate court reviewed those briefs, and the appellate court affirmed the convictions. The failure of the appellate court and counsel to notice a ministerial error in the judgment and sentence did not vitiate the procedural safeguards that were followed or render the appeal otherwise unreliable. Defendant received all the procedural protection that the Constitution required. If defendant was to obtain relief, he had to do so through a claim of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel.


OUTCOME: The mandate was recalled. The judgment was affirmed.

 

1632 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Savage


No. 33291-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1435



July 5, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Savage, 133 Wn. App. 1044, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1893 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from a trial court in Washington, which convicted him of second degree assault and third degree theft.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was accused of stealing items from a victim that lived nearby. When he was confronted, defendant allegedly threatened to kill the victim. He was convicted of second degree assault and third degree theft. Thereafter, defendant sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the State was not required to allege in the indictment that defendant committed theft not exceeding two hundred and fifty dollars in value. Although value was stated in Wash. Rev. Stat. § 9A.56.050, it was not an essential element of a crime unless it represented a minimum threshold value that the State was required to prove. Next, there was sufficient evidence to support the convictions. As to the assault charge under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.021, the jury was instructed that the crime could have been committed in three ways: by a battery, an attempted battery, or intentional infliction of imminent fear of bodily injury. The undisputed evidence showed that defendant raised a bowling pin over the victim in a threatening manner. Finally, the evidence showed that defendant wrongfully obtained the property from the victim because he did not have permission to enter his home.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

State v. Minor


No. 33193-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


133 Wn. App. 636; 137 P.3d 872; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1323



June 27, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Minor, 160 Wn.2d 1001, 158 P.3d 614, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 311 (2007)
Reversed by State v. Minor, 2008 Wash. LEXIS 47 (Wash., Jan. 17, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Grays Harbor County (Washington), which adjudicated a charge of first degree unlawful possession of a firearm.


OVERVIEW: Several witnesses told police that defendant was in possession of a gun. He was charged with a violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.040(1)(a) due to a previous conviction for residential burglary. However, defendant contended that he was not told of his firearm possession rights. After the trial court imposed a manifest injustice disposition, defendant sought review. In affirming, the appellate court determined that there was a failure to comply with Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.047 when the original trial court did not check the box on the judgment and sentence indicating that defendant was prohibited from possessing a firearm. But defendant did not show that he looked at or relied on the judgment and sentence to determine whether he could possess a firearm. Further, the original trial court did not give any misleading affirmative information. Next, the sentence imposed under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.160(2) was justified due to defendant's extensive prior criminal history and his failure to comply with prior dispositions and paroles; moreover, it was not excessive. Finally, Blakely did not prohibit a juvenile judge from imposing a manifest injustice sentence.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1634 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Quintero Morelos


No. 22234-9-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


133 Wn. App. 591; 137 P.3d 114; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1301



June 22, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Morelos, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 244 (Wash., Apr. 4, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1]
State v. Morelos, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2802 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 16, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order of the Grant County Superior Court, Washington, amending defendant's sentence for fourth degree assault to 364 days of jail confinement with 330 days suspended for two years on good behavior.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of fourth degree assault (domestic violence) for pushing a family member. The trial court sentenced defendant to 365 days with 330 days suspended for two years on good behavior, and defense counsel did not object to the length of the sentence. A second lawyer informed defense counsel of the implications of such a sentence in an assault case, that a sentence of 365 days prompted federal immigration authorities to begin deportation proceedings, while a sentence of even one day less, 364 days, did not. Defense counsel moved to modify the sentence to 364 days to avoid deportation, and the trial court readily agreed that the amendment was appropriate. The appellate court ruled that defense counsel's failure to inform the trial court of defendant's alien status was excusable neglect under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8. The trial court reconsidered its sentence one day after its entry, and armed with information supplied by more experienced counsel ordered an amendment to the sentence that had minimal practical impact on the State but had critical consequences to defendant. The trial court properly exercised its discretion.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

 

1635 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Myers v. City of Cheney


No. 23372-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1303



June 22, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 01-2-03076-5. Judge signing: SALVATORE F. COZZA. Date filed: September 13, 2004.
Myers v. City of Cheney, 133 Wn. App. 1029, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1733 (2006)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed/Reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, granted summary judgment in favor of respondent city by deciding that the city fire code authorized the city fire chief to require appellant mobile home park owner to install fire hydrants. The trial court granted the city attorney fees but denied a motion by the city for Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 11 sanctions against the owner. The owner appealed; the city cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owner argued that he did not have to install fire hydrants in the mobile home park. The appellate court noted that a mobile home was a building for the purposes of the fire code. And homes were constructed or moved into or within the park after 1989, when the Uniform Fire Code for all counties and cities was adopted by the State, Wash. Rev. Code § 19.27.031. Some homes were more than 150 feet from a public street water main. The pertinent portions of the city's fire code were calculated to protect life and limb. Even if Wash. Rev. Code § 4.84.370 did not preclude administrative boards from awarding fees, no authority existed for the Fire Code Board of Appeals to award fees. The Uniform Fire Code § 103.1.4 said nothing about awarding attorney fees to the prevailing party. The trial judge did not abuse its discretion in determining that Wash. Super. Ct. Civ. R. 11 was not violated where the argument was not frivolous, was offered in good faith, and was properly before the court. The appellate court denied the city's motion to strike the appendix from the owner's brief.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as to the second order of correction and to the denial of sanctions. The judgment was reversed as to the attorney fee award and the city's motion to strike the appendix from the owner's appellate brief was denied.

State v. Borunda


No. 23664-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1304



June 22, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Borunda, 133 Wn. App. 1029, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1734 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 04-1-03985-2. Judge signing: SALVATORE F. COZZA. Date filed: November 15, 2004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Spokane County Court, Washington, convicting him of third degree theft and possession of a controlled substance-methamphetamine, and sentencing him to 18 months.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was observed by police as leaving a convenience store without paying for gas. Defendant was arrested for theft, and a search incident to arrest revealed a baggie containing a white substance in his truck. The substance tested positive for methamphetamine. On appeal, defendant argued that he was denied his constitutional right to confrontation, the prosecutor committed misconduct, and his sentence constituted cruel and unusual punishment. The appellate court ruled that the trial court properly admitted the convenience store clerk's testimony regarding her fellow cashier's statement, as the statement was not testimonial in nature and the confrontation clause did not apply. Also, defendant failed to show prosecutorial misconduct, as he could not show a substantial likelihood that the disputed line of questioning affected the verdict. Furthermore, defendant's sentence was not cruel and unusual punishment. Defendant failed to address the factors in his arguments on appeal, and in the absence of an argument specifically addressing the relevant factors, it could not be said that defendant's sentence was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

More v. Dep't of Ret. Sys.


No. 33035-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


133 Wn. App. 581; 137 P.3d 73; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1292



June 20, 2006, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington, denied appellant employee's benefits claim in favor of respondent, Washington State Department of Retirement (DRS), by finding that as a vessel crew member excluded from coverage under Wash. Rev. Code tit. 51, she was ineligible for retirement under Wash. Rev. Code § 41.40.200(1). The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The employee argued that Wash. Rev. Code § 41.40.200(1) violated her right to equal protection by excluding her profession from retirement benefits for total incapacitation due to an occupational disease. The trial court found that the legislature amended the statute to establish new potential pension benefits that did not significantly increase DRS's administrative costs. The appellate court agreed with the superior court that in amending the statute to create pension benefits for occupational diseases, the legislature could have intended to create a convenient means for DRS to determine coverage without the necessity of making costly individual eligibility determinations. The statute was rationally related to the legitimate governmental interest in creating new benefits that did not create significant administrative costs. Wash. Rev. Code § 41.40.200(1) did not violate the principle of equal protection.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Dukes


No. 55521-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1276



June 19, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Dukes, 133 Wn. App. 1023, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1711 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by a trial court, Washington, for possession of cocaine and possession of less than forty grams of marijuana.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendant's car after witnessing him make an illegal lane change and observing that the license plates for the car had expired. After stopping the car, the officer learned that defendant was driving with a suspended license. The officer arrested defendant for the criminal traffic infraction of third degree driving while license suspended and searched both defendant and the vehicle incident to arrest. The officer discovered cocaine and marijuana in the car. The State charged defendant with possession of cocaine and possession of less than forty grams of marijuana. At a Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 3.6 hearing, defendant argued that the arrest was a pretext to search for narcotics and violated Wash. Const. art. I, § 7. The motion was denied. The appellate court affirmed the motion to suppress and defendant's conviction as the evidence clearly established that the traffic stop was not pretextual as defendant made an illegal lane change and had expired plates. When the officer learned that defendant was driving with a suspended license after the stop, the arrest and subsequent search of the car was lawful.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

1639 of 2278 DOCUMENTS




Locke v. City of Seattle


No. 55256-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


133 Wn. App. 696; 137 P.3d 52; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1285



June 19, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Locke v. City of Seattle, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1621 (Wash. Ct. App., July 31, 2006)
Review granted by Locke v. City of Seattle, 152 P.3d 347, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 13 (Wash., 2007)
Affirmed by, Remanded by Locke v. City of Seattle, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 948 (Wash., Dec. 13, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee city fire fighter trainee was injured during a training exercise. The trainee, a law enforcement officer and fire fighter retirement system (LEOFF) member, sued appellee city for negligence pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 41.26.281. A jury in the Superior Court for King County (Washington) found the city negligent and returned a verdict in the trainee's favor of $1,513,663, after a remittitur. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The city challenged the basis for the trainee's suit on constitutional and statutory grounds and assigned error to numerous trial court rulings. The appellate court first addressed the city's claim that it was entitled to sovereign immunity from its LEOFF-member employees' tort claims. The city relied on Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96.010(1). Although the statute generally waived a municipality's sovereign immunity, the city contended that the phrase, "to the same extent as if they were a private person or corporation," operated to provide the city with sovereign immunity from claims under LEOFF because a private person or corporation was not required to pay into a worker's compensation fund and still be subject to an employee's tort suit. Wash. Rev. Code § 41.26.281 placed a statutory duty on municipal corporations not to injure employee fire fighters or police officers by negligent acts or omissions. That satisfied the public duty doctrine and established a cause of action that was in turn permitted by Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96.010. The city's sovereign immunity from claims brought under the LEOFF statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 41.26.281, was waived by Wash. Rev. Code § 4.96.010.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


 

1640 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Voshell


No. 32968-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1146



June 14, 2006, Decided  
June 14, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Marriage of Voshell, 133 Wn. App. 1021, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1604 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Marriage of Voshell, 131 Wn. App. 1058, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 749 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court set aside an attorney lien appellant attorney filed against the real property respondent client was awarded in a marital dissolution proceeding. The trial court found that the attorney was not entitled to an attorney lien on real property. The attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: The client moved the court to dismiss the appeal because the attorney filed it as a notice of appeal instead of as a notice for discretionary review. The appellate court found that the attorney's appeal was proper as the order from which the attorney appealed was effectively a final order as to his attorney lien. The attorney claimed that because he filed his attorney lien before judgment, he had rights to funds held by both his client and the client's ex-wife and any proceeds from the sale of marital assets to third parties. The appellate court noted that the attorney did not have any claim on funds in the ex-wife's hands unless they were funds she had to pay his client in judgment. The attorney had priority in any monetary judgment the client received; however, because the client's judgment awarded him real property, the attorney may not claim a lien on it. An attorney had no lien if the recovery his client obtained was real property. This interpretation was not an unconstitutional application of the lien statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 60.40.010. Because the decision was affirmed in the client's favor, he was the prevailing party and was entitled to attorney fees on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
