Peste v. Mason County


No. 33437-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


133 Wn. App. 456; 136 P.3d 140; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1150



June 14, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Request denied by Peste v. Mason County, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 196 (Wash., Mar. 7, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, three individuals and a trust, sought review of a judgment of the Superior Court of Mason County (Washington), which affirmed a decision of the board of commissioners of respondent county denying appellants' request for a rezoning of their property. Appellants had appealed the board's decision under the Washington Land Use Petition Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 36.70C.


OVERVIEW: The subject property was large, undeveloped, and surrounded by other similar properties with identical zoning designations to the east, west, and south. The board determined that rezoning the property, an undeveloped rural parcel, would contravene its comprehensive plan (CP), development regulations (DRs), and the goals of the Growth Management Act (GMA), Wash. Rev. Code §§ 36.70A.010-.902. The court first determined that appellants waived their right to argue that the county did not comply with the GMA's notice and public participation procedures. Appellants should have first presented that argument to the Western Washington Growth Management Hearings Board, not the court. The court next decided that appellants' takings claim was reviewable, but it determined that appellants' facial challenge to the validity of the county's CP and DRs failed and that its "as applied" challenge was not yet ripe. The court next held that the county's designation of rural areas and densities was not unduly oppressive and thus did not violate substantive due process. Finally, the court found that substantial evidence supported the board's findings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.


 

1642 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Seattle Mortg. v. Unknown Heirs of Gray


No. 33664-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


133 Wn. App. 479; 136 P.3d 776; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1160



June 14, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants city public utilities department (PUD) sought review of a decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, which granted summary judgment to respondent mortgage company in the company's foreclosure action, which extinguished the PUD's lien against the real property.


OVERVIEW: The company held a mortgage on the decedent's property, and the PUD had a lien on the property due to a loan by the PUD for energy conservation improvements to the home. The decedent died and the company initiated foreclosure proceedings. Wash. Const. art. VIII, § 10 authorized the PUD to establish a lien against the structure and entitled the PUD to traditional lien law protections. The court held that Wash. Const. art. VIII, § 7 did not mandate repayment. The PUD demonstrated a lack of donated intent because it received the benefit of saved electricity with the improvements. Also, provisions allowing the PUD to establish a lien did not expressly enable it to shut off power to a subsequent owner where the previous owner defaulted on a conservation loan. As a lender, the PUD was required to abide by lien and contract laws applicable to other lenders. Further, when acting as a lender, the PUD was not acting solely as a utility service provider and thus it could not extend benefits the legislature bestowed on it as a utility service provider to itself in the lender role. The PUD had other remedies s a junior lien holder, such as foreclosing at the time of default.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Baja v. Lehman


No. 55773-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1124



June 12, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Baja v. Lehman, 133 Wn. App. 1015, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1581 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate, who was a military veteran, sued respondent prison officials, challenging deductions taken from his military pension as required by Wash. Rev. Code § 72.09.480(2). A Washington superior court upheld the deductions. The inmate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The inmate predicated his appeal upon the Veteran's Administration benefits anti-alienation statute, 38 U.S.C.S. § 5301, and rested his argument entirely upon a ruling by a federal district judge in Wright v. Riveland, in which a class of Washington inmates challenged the same statutory deductions on a variety of constitutional bases. He argued that the federal judge's ruling in Wright constituted controlling precedent establishing that Wash. Rev. Code § 72.09.480(2) conflicted with 38 U.S.C.S. § 5301 and was void to the extent it permitted seizure of federal pension funds. However, the instant court noted that the inmate did not make the argument below. Although the inmate's counsel made one reference to the Wright case at the summary judgment hearing, counsel did not advance the argument. Thus, the argument was not preserved for review. Even if the instant court were inclined to review the argument, it was unable to do so because the inmate provided neither an adequate record nor a legal foundation. Even if the instant court had the district court ruling before it and were persuaded by it, the inmate could not establish that he would be governed by it.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Ocak


No. 56006-9-I (consol. No. 56019-1-I)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1126



June 12, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, two juvenile defendants challenged sentences imposed by a Washington trial court following their convictions for several felonies.


OVERVIEW: The first defendant and the second defendant argued that their prosecutions should have been transferred to juvenile court once they were acquitted on the charges that triggered adult court jurisdiction. Both defendants acknowledged that the auto-decline statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 13.04.030(1)(e)(v), granted adult courts exclusive jurisdiction based on the charges, not the conviction. They argued, however, that the auto-decline statute violated due process, equal protection, and separation of powers principles. The instant court concluded that defendants' sentencing claims were controlled and defeated by existing case law. The second defendant challenged his two convictions for unlawful display of a weapon on double jeopardy grounds. The State conceded that the second defendant's convictions for two counts of unlawful display of a weapon violated double jeopardy. The instant court accepted the State's concession of error. The instant court rejected defendants' argument that the sentencing court violated their rights to due process and a jury trial because it included prior juvenile adjudications in their offender scores.


OUTCOME: The first defendant's sentence was affirmed. The second defendant's judgment and sentence was reversed and remanded for further proceedings.

State v. Lott


No. 56279-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1132



June 12, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Lott, 133 Wn. App. 1016, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1587 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Washington trial court convicting her of one count of second degree rape of a child, and one count of third degree rape of a child.


OVERVIEW: The twelve-year-old victim and his fourteen-year-old cousin often visited defendant's apartment, where they could drink alcohol and smoke marijuana. Defendant was thirty nine years old. The victim later told his mother and a doctor that he had oral and vaginal sex with defendant. The victim's cousin also reported he had oral sex with defendant. Defendant's children each testified that they entered defendant's bedroom and observed the victim on top of defendant, moving up and down and that defendant had her eyes closed and appeared to be asleep or passed out. The appellate court ruled that the trial court erred by rejecting defendant's proposed jury instruction on her defense to the second degree child rape count. Drawing reasonable inferences from the evidence in favor of defendant, a finder of fact could have reached the conclusion the victim had intercourse with defendant without her consent, knowledge, or awareness, and defendant was thus not guilty of rape of a child. Defendant's son went to defendant's bedroom and observed the victim moving up and down on top of defendant, who he believed was still passed out drunk and gave no indication of being aware what was happening.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction of second degree rape of a child was reversed, the case was remanded for retrial of the second degree child rape charge and resentencing of the third degree child rape conviction.

State v. Monschke


No. 31847-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


133 Wn. App. 313; 135 P.3d 966; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1104



June 1, 2006, Filed


NOTICE: PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at State v. Pillatos, 159 Wn.2d 459, 150 P.3d 1130, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 62 (2007)
Review denied by State v. Monschke, 159 Wn.2d 1010, 154 P.3d 918, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 171 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Monschke v. Washington, 552 U.S. 841, 128 S. Ct. 83, 169 L. Ed. 2d 64, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 9614 (2007)
Post-conviction relief denied at In re Pers. Restraint of Monschke, 160 Wn. App. 479, 251 P.3d 884, 2010 Wash. App. LEXIS 2809 (2010)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Monschke v. Cross, 2011 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 51332 (W.D. Wash., Apr. 19, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No. 03-1-01464-0. Date Filed: June 4, 2004. Judge Signing: Hon. Lisa R Worswick.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) convicting him of aggravated first-degree murder in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.32.030, 10.95.020(6).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for murdering the victim, a homeless man, to advance his status as a white supremacist. On appeal, the court held that white supremacy fell within the meaning of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.95.020(6) because under the statute's plain language, white supremacy was an "identifiable group" with a "hierarchy." The court held that § 10.95.020(6) was neither overbroad nor vague. The evidence was sufficient such that a rational trier of fact could find that defendant murdered the victim to advance his position as a white supremacist because: (1) defendant was the member of a white supremacist subgroup; (2) defendant wanted to advance his position in the subgroup and open his own local chapter; (3) acts of violence elevated a member's status in many white supremacist subgroups; (4) defendant and his co-defendants were underneath an interstate looking to "do" someone inferior; (5) the victim was viewed as inferior by defendant and his co-defendants; (6) the victim's murder elevated a co-defendant's status; and (7) defendant wondered aloud whether the victim's murder would elevate his status with God.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


133 Wn. App. 156; 135 P.3d 946; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1061



May 25, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant junior lienholder sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Spokane County (Washington), which entered judgment in favor of respondent judgment creditors and dismissed a complaint brought by the lienholder seeking to quiet title in property and to set aside a sheriff's deed and sale for which the lienholder received no notice.


OVERVIEW: The creditors notified the judgment debtors of the sale and of their right of redemption. They did not, however, provide direct notice to the lienholder, although the sale was properly posted and published. Days before the one-year redemption period expired, the lienholder learned of the sale, but a sheriff's deed was issued and recorded. In response to the creditors' motion for summary judgment, the lienholder raised a challenge to the constitutionality of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 6.21.030(1) and 6.23.030(1), but the court affirmed the trial court's judgment of dismissal. Finding that the statutes were unambiguous and had been fully satisfied, the court next found that the constitutional challenge was never before the trial court because a complaint could not be amended in arguments in a response brief. Noting that the statutory period set forth in Wash. Rev. Code § 4.56.190 had not yet expired, the court next found that a challenge based on lack of court confirmation was not ripe for review. Finally, the court declined to address alleged sale irregularities because the lienholder did not object to the sheriff's return within the 20-day period set forth in Wash. Rev. Code § 6.21.110(2).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment of summary dismissal of the lienholder's complaint.

State v. Flemming


No. 31812-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1050



May 23, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Flemming, 133 Wn. App. 1001, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1454 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to one count of unlawful possession of pseudoephedrine and/or ephedrine with intent to manufacture methamphetamine, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 69.50.401(2)(b) and 69.50.440, and a Washington trial court denied defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea, convicted him of the charge, and sentenced him to 42 months of confinement and 42 months of community custody. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: One month after he pled guilty to violating Wash. Rev. Code §§ 69.50.401 and 69.50.440, defendant informed the trial court that he wanted to withdraw his plea. The court questioned defendant about his request before he was sentenced, but denied the request and sentenced defendant to confinement and community custody. One month after he was sentenced, defendant moved to withdraw his plea. The court of appeals held, inter alia, that (1) although a form that was given to defendant before he pled guilty did not inform him that he would have to provide a DNA sample if he were convicted, that omission did not affect the validity of his guilty plea; (2) defendant provided no evidence that he was incapacitated at the time he entered his plea because he had taken drugs, and his bear assertion that he was intoxicated was not enough to invalidate his plea (3) defendant's general assertions, unsupported by affidavits, that his counsel failed to provide proper advice and failed to investigate his reasons for wanting to withdraw his plea were insufficient to show that he was denied effective assistance of counsel; and (4) the State's sentencing guidelines were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's judgment.

State v. Reyes


No. 32481-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 976



May 16, 2006, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Reyes, 132 Wn. App. 1060, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1362 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A Washington trial court convicted defendant of first degree unlawful possession of a firearm and unlawful possession of a controlled substance while armed with a firearm. Defendant appealed his convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, who had been a passenger in a car that was stopped for not having its license plate properly illuminated, argued that the trial court erred when it: (1) failed to enter written findings and conclusions following a suppression hearing held pursuant to Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 3.6, and (2) improperly admitted evidence from an unlawful search. The instant court concluded that the trial court did submit findings and conclusions. It rejected defendant's contention that he was unlawfully seized under Wash. Const. art. I, § 7, when the officer requested him and the other passengers to remain in the car. Defendant failed to provide any evidence in the record that his movement or freedom were restrained. However, even if the officer did order defendant to remain in the car, the officer was entitled to do so in order to ensure his safety. The instant court also concluded that the evidence in defendant's backpack was admissible as product of a warrantless search for officer safety. Its discovery was inevitable in the ordinary course of an officer taking reasonable safety precautions in response to seeing bullets near the backpack.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1650 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Whitfield


No. 32655-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


132 Wn. App. 878; 134 P.3d 1203; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 981



May 16, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] PUBLISHED PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Whitfield, 159 Wn.2d 1012, 154 P.3d 919, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 195 (2007)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Whitfield v. Frakes, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 104602 (W.D. Wash., Oct. 26, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from his conviction in the Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington of 17 counts of first-degree assault with sexual motivation, 2 counts of witness tampering, and 3 counts of no-contact order violations. Defendant was sentenced to 2,137 months' confinement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was diagnosed as HIV positive, then had sexual contact with more than a thousand persons without wearing a condom. When a doctor learned that a third individual diagnosed with AIDS named defendant as a sex partner, defendant was served with a cease and desist order under Wash. Rev. Code § 70.24.024. The court affirmed, and held that nothing required the State to exhaust civil measures under ch. 70.24 before enforcing a criminal statute. Defendant's equal protection rights were not violated because the classification under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.011(1)(b) had a reasonable relationship to a legitimate state objective--to stop the transmission of a deadly disease. Further, § 9A.36.011(1)(b) did not grant unconstitutional immunity by not including other sexually transmitted diseases. There was evidence that defendant knew that he was HIV-positive when he engaged in unprotected sexual activities while concealing his HIV status. Thus, there was sufficient evidence that defendant intentionally exposed the victims to the disease. Also, the trial court properly refused to consider a consent defense because defendant did not disclose his HIV status to any of the victims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

 

1651 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Det. of Taylor


No. 32413-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


132 Wn. App. 827; 134 P.3d 254; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 921



May 9, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by In re Det. of Taylor, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 120 (Wash., Jan. 31, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an order of the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington committing him as a sexually violent predator (SVP) under Wash. Rev. Code ch. 71.09.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was incarcerated for the rape and stabbing of two women and he admitted to committing several other rapes since he was 12 years old. Appellant participated in every available sex offender treatment program and his therapist testified that appellant's risk level for reoffense was high because he continued to have fantasies about rape and he incurred prison infractions for impermissible touching of female corrections officers. The court affirmed the decision and held that appellant's substantive due process rights were not violated because the "about to be released" language of Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.030 showed that the legislature intended to allow the State to file at the end of an incarceration and the State did not abuse its authority by filing two days before appellant was schedule for release. The court also held that actuarial determinations of future dangerousness satisfied Frye. Furthermore, appellant's counsel was not ineffective for not presenting an expert opinion on a theory that concerned elderly sex offenders as appellant was 38 at the time. And, counsel presented expert testimony criticizing the State's actuarial expert.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1652 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Cork v. Wash. State Liquor Control Bd.


No. 23228-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 903



May 4, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Cork v. Wash. State Liquor Control Bd., 132 Wn. App. 1052, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1261 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of SPOKANE COUNTY. Docket No: 04-2-00418-1. Date filed: July 27, 2004. Judge signing: KATHLEEN M. O'CONNOR.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a man and a woman, challenged a judgment of the Spokane County Superior Court, Washington, which dismissed on summary judgment their petition for return of tobacco products and certain personal property seized by the State as contraband.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to a search warrant, respondent Washington State Liquor Control Board found 30,600 assorted packs of unstamped, untaxed cigarettes in a van driven by the man. The van was owned by the woman. The Board seized the van and cigarettes, and notified appellants that the seized property would be forfeited. Appellants argued that the property was not contraband because the statutory scheme did not apply to the woman, who was a member of an Indian tribe and had an American Indian business license. The court concluded that the woman's Indian status did not prevent the State from imposing an excise tax on her activities off-reservation. It rejected appellants' contention that the excise tax violated the Commerce Clause, U.S. Const. art. I, § 8, cl. 3. The statute authorizing the excise tax, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 82.24, did not openly discriminate against interstate commerce in favor of Washington state interests. Appellants failed to persuade the court that Washington's tax scheme was invalid as applied to Indians generally. Appellants also failed to qualify for an exemption to Washington's excise tax scheme. The seized cigarettes were contraband subject to forfeiture.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1653 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Giles


No. 33027-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


132 Wn. App. 738; 132 P.3d 1151; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 830



May 2, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at State v. Giles, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 47 (Wash., Jan. 3, 2007)
Review denied by State v. Giles, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 375 (Wash., May 2, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Mason County (Washington) sentencing him to concurrent standard-range sentences for methamphetamine and first-degree unlawful firearm possession.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his sentences, arguing that the trial court improperly increased his sentencing ranges based on a judicial finding that he was subject to community placement when he committed the crimes in violation of the Sixth Amendment. The court held that the trial court did not violate defendant's right to a jury trial when it added a point to his offender score because of his community placement status, and affirmed his sentences. Pursuant to the Hunt decision, the court held that: (1) whether a defendant was on community placement for another crime when he committed the crime for which he was being sentenced was not an aggravating factor increasing defendant's sentence beyond the standard sentencing range for the current crime; (2) therefore, the additional offender point based on defendant's community placement status did not implicate Blakely or require a factual determination by a jury; and (3) defendant's standard-range sentence did not violate any Blakely principles.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentences were affirmed.

 

1654 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Aaro Med. Supplies v. Revenue


No. 32486-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


132 Wn. App. 709; 132 P.3d 1143; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 832



May 2, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Aaro Med. Supplies, Inc., 2007 Wash. LEXIS 198 (Wash., Mar. 7, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant durable medical equipment vendors sued respondent Washington State Department of Revenue for a refund of sales taxes on medical products they had sold to federal Medicare beneficiaries and for which the federal government paid them on assignment. The Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) summarily dismissed the action. The vendors appealed.


OVERVIEW: For purposes of Wash. Rev. Code § 82.08.050, the Medicare beneficiaries were the buyers of the medical products as they were the ones who identified the product, ordered it from the vendor, incurred the primary obligation to pay for it, took possession of it, became the owner of it, and used it. Thus, the state sales tax applied to the vendors' sales of medical products. Although the vendors had standing to seek the sales tax refunds, they were not entitled to such refunds because the vendors were liable to the Department to remit taxes on taxable sales, whether or not they collected from the buyers. Moreover, the transactions at issue were taxable sales. Thus, the vendors were required to remit sales taxes from their own pockets.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1655 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stearns


NO. 55562-6-1


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 803



May 1, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Stearns, 132 Wn. App. 1044, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1231 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the trial court (Washington) convicting him for possessing depictions of a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant rented a room from landlords who had a six-year-old daughter. Defendant downloaded pornography onto the family computer; the child told the parents, and defendant was evicted. Defendant was found at a homeless shelter and arrested. Computer discs containing child pornography were found in his bag. The court held that the affidavit supporting the search warrant was sufficient in that it did not merely rely on an informant's tip that defendant had pornography in his bags; it explained that pedophiles habitually keep pornography for long periods of time. Further, the information was not stale because it showed a likelihood of continuous presence of child pornography. The trial court properly admitted anime drawings that resembled images found on the landlords' computer. However, the court vacated the consecutive sentences imposed under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.589(1)(a) because the "too lenient" conclusion made by the trial court implicated Blakely. Also, the condition of community placement that defendant should not "possess or access pornographic materials" was unconstitutionally vague under Sansone.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions, but remanded for resentencing.

 

1656 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. George


No. 55312-7-I (consolidated with No. 55313-5-I)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


132 Wn. App. 654; 133 P.3d 487; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 816



May 1, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, in part, Review denied by, in part State v. George, 153 P.3d 196, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 64 (Wash., 2007)
Affirmed by State v. George, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 562 (Wash., Aug. 9, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants advertised a truck for sale. Police thought their ad sounded too good to be true. After a sting operation, defendants were convicted in the Superior Court of King County (Washington) of attempted first degree theft by deception. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: The putative buyer of the truck did not get what he bargained for. Defendants repeatedly claimed the truck had been driven only 70,000 miles by its only owner and had always been garaged. None of that was true. To induce the sale, defendants falsely described the truck in the significant matter of mileage, if nothing else. The evidence was sufficient to establish the deprivation necessary to prove an unlawful taking. Also, the legislature did not intend an inquiry into the thief's net gain or the victim's net loss once the fact of a deprivation was established. The evidence establishing existence and value of a deprivation would be the same in takings theft cases (and often, in unauthorized control cases as well), but in deception cases, the statute required a different analysis. Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.56.020(1)(b) looked only to the value of the property obtained, not the net result of the exchange. The property defendants attempted to obtain was a valid cashier's check for $ 5,500. Where the property stolen was money, there was no need to determine value. Thus, the evidence was sufficient to establish the value element of attempted theft in the first degree.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1657 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Pers. Restraint of Adams


No. 54389-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


132 Wn. App. 640; 134 P.3d 1176; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 795



May 1, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

As Amended by Order of the Court of Appeals July 18, 2006.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Amended by, Reconsideration denied by In re Pers. Restraint of Adams, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1566 (Wash. Ct. App., July 18, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: State v. Adams, 102 Wn. App. 1006, 2000 Wash. App. LEXIS 2186 (2000)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate filed a personal restraint petition challenging the determination of respondent Department of Corrections (DOC) that he was not eligible for the enhanced early release under a program in Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.728(1).


OVERVIEW: As directed, DOC evaluated the inmate and determined he was eligible to earn early release under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.9A.728(1)(b) for 50 percent of his sentence instead of the 33 percent maximum previously available. Three weeks before his scheduled release, DOC decided the inmate was not eligible for early release under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.728 and changed his release date. Based on its review of the inmate's file, DOC recalculated his score. The inmate contended DOC's decision to review the previous risk assessment was not authorized by Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.728(1)(b). The inmate also contended he was entitled to minimal due process before DOC changed its determination that he was eligible to earn early release under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.728 and cancel his scheduled release date. The appellate court concluded that DOC's decision to change the LSI-R score making him ineligible for release under § 9.94A.728(1)(b) was not based on the LSI-R risk assessment instrument. DOC engaged in a retrospective review; the inmate was entitled to minimal due process including notice and the opportunity to address any erroneous information that was the basis for the decision.


OUTCOME: The personal restraint petition was granted.

 

1658 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Lawrence v. Dep't of Health


No. 33483-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


133 Wn. App. 665; 138 P.3d 124; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 774



April 25, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Respondent's Motion to Publish July 5, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 04-2-01925-4. Date filed: 06/24/2005. Judge signing: Hon. H. Christopher Wickham.
Lawrence v. Dep't of Health, 132 Wn. App. 1042, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1222 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant physician sought review of respondent medical quality assurance commission's summary dismissal of unprofessional conduct charges against the physician. The Thurston County Superior Court, Washington, affirmed the commission's order. The physician appealed the superior court's judgment.


OVERVIEW: The physician argued that the commission acted arbitrarily and capriciously in excess of its authority and denied him due process when it refused to conduct a hearing, dismissed the charges against him without prejudice, and failed to accord him a public exoneration. The court disagreed, concluding that the commission did not deprive the physician of his constitutional right to due process under the Fourteenth Amendment by failing to hold a hearing after issuing a press release withdrawing the statement of charges against him. Although professional courtesy may have entitled the physician to a hearing so he could clear his name, due process did not require one. The commission had the statutory authority to withdraw the charges against the physician without a hearing. Because the commission did not decide the case on its merits, the physician was not entitled to dismissal with prejudice. The physician was not entitled to public exoneration under Wash. Rev. Code § 18.130.110 because the commission never reached the point of determining whether the physician engaged in unprofessional conduct. Thus, the public exoneration requirement of § 18.130.110 was never triggered.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1659 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Medrano


No. 55046-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 722



April 24, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-1-09884-8. Date filed: 09/03/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Charles W Mertel.
State v. Medrano, 132 Wn. App. 1038, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1205 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Superior Court of King County (Washington) found defendant guilty of robbery in the first degree and two counts of assault in the first degree. The trial court ruled the convictions for the robbery and assault of the store owner involved the same criminal conduct, but it ordered standard range sentences for the two separate first-degree assault convictions involving different victims to be served consecutively. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: During a robbery, defendant fired two shots. Two victims, a store owner and a customer, were injured. Defendant admitted he went into the store with the intent to commit robbery. He admitted that he had a loaded gun and he intentionally shot at the owner. There was also no dispute that the owner and the customer were both injured. The owner was shot in the hand and the customer in the cheek. Even if one bullet caused both injuries, there was more than one criminal act. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in concluding defendant's criminal conduct was separate and distinct for purposes of imposing a consecutive sentence for the two first-degree assault convictions under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.589(1)(b). On appeal, defendant also contended that the firearm enhancement for the two first-degree assault convictions violated the state and federal double jeopardy clauses. He argued that he was being punished twice - once for first-degree assault with a firearm and again for being armed with a firearm while committing the same assault. The appellate court rejected defendant's double jeopardy challenge to the imposition of the firearm enhancement.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision imposing consecutive sentences was affirmed. However, the appellate court remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing for the robbery conviction.

 

1660 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martel


No. 24068-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 697



April 18, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: County: ADAMS. Docket No(s): 04-1-00126-9. Judge signing: RICHARD W. MILLER. Date filed: March 24, 2005.
State v. Martel, 132 Wn. App. 1036, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1200 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of third degree child rape by the Superior Court of Adams County, Washington, and was sentenced to 31 months incarceration and 36 to 48 months community custody. Defendant appealed and alleged that the court erred by imposing a sentence in excess of the statutory maximum and that the third degree rape statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.079, was unconstitutional because consent was not allowed as a defense.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was 21 years old and engaged in sexual intercourse with the victim who was 14 years old. The appellate court agreed with defendant that his sentence had to be remanded because the statutory maximum for third degree rape was 60 months. Thus, defendant's sentence of 31 months incarceration and 36 to 48 months community custody exceeded the statutory maximum. The appellate court remanded for resentencing. The appellate court rejected defendant's claim that Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.079 was unconstitutional because consent was not allowed as a defense because the instant court, in applying the minimum scrutiny test, concluded that the classifications in § 9A.44.079 drew a rational distinction between older, potentially predatory persons and younger, less mature persons in the victim's age group. More importantly, the court also concluded that the distinction between the classifications was not wholly unrelated to the legitimate interest of protecting children from sexually predatory adults. Finally, the court held that the child rape statutes advanced the State's legitimate interest in protecting children who were too immature to consent.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction, but remanded for resentencing.

 

1661 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Cary v. Mason County


No. 32753-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


132 Wn. App. 495; 132 P.3d 157; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 703



April 18, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Cary v. Mason County, 159 Wn.2d 1005, 153 P.3d 196, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 119 (2007)
Appeal after remand at, Remanded by Cary v. Mason County, 2009 Wash. App. LEXIS 2772 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 9, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer brought an action for declaratory judgment, arguing that appellee county's ordinance, Mason County, Wash., Ordinance § 121-02, adopted as a "special assessment," was actually an invalid and unconstitutional "property tax." The Superior Court of Mason County (Washington) ruled that the taxpayer should have appealed within 30 days and his action was time-barred because he waited six months to file. The taxpayer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The county adopted the ordinance under Wash. Rev. Code § 89.08.400 as a conservation "special assessment." The taxpayer argued that the appeal period for actions to recover any tax levied or assessed was the analogous appeal period. Under Wash. Rev. Code § 84.68.060, actions to recover any tax levied or assessed could be commenced until after the 30th day of the next succeeding June following the year in which the tax became payable. The taxpayer claimed that the instant tax was not payable until 2003; thus, he had until June 30, 2004, to bring his complaint. He filed his complaint for declaratory judgment on March 10, 2003. His complaint was clear; he argued that the ordinance was an invalid tax, not a special assessment or a local improvement. The action was more analogous to one seeking to recover a tax than to one challenging municipal local improvements, thus, the appellate court held that § 84.68.060 was the analogous appeal period. Under that rule, the appellate court held that the taxpayer's complaint was timely and the trial court had erred in ruling that the action was barred by analogy to the 30-day period that limited other actions against the county.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed. The case was remanded.

State v. Whitaker


No. 54834-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


133 Wn. App. 199; 135 P.3d 923; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 695



April 17, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Appellant's Motion to Publish May 24, 2006.
Reported at State v. Whitaker, 132 Wn. App. 1033, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1188 (2006)
Review denied by State v. Whitaker, 159 Wn.2d 1017, 157 P.3d 404, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 257 (2007)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Whitaker v. Washington, 552 U.S. 948, 128 S. Ct. 375, 169 L. Ed. 2d 260, 2007 U.S. LEXIS 11318 (2007)
Post-conviction relief granted at, Remanded by In re Pers. Restraint of Whitaker, 2013 Wash. App. LEXIS 1443 (Wash. Ct. App., June 17, 2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which convicted him of aggravated murder and conspiracy to commit first-degree murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions stemming from his participation in the kidnapping and killing of the victim. With respect to the primary issues he raised on appeal, the court held that despite extensive local publicity about the murder, no change of venue was called for. The prospective jurors had little awareness of the publicity and the details of the crime. Given the scrupulous care taken by the trial court, the circumstances did not show a probability of unfair prejudice. The court further held that upon arrest, defendant was properly advised of his right to counsel under U.S. Const. amends. V and VI before he gave an incriminating statement. Although photographs were gruesome and disturbing, a reasonable person could have concluded that jurors would better understand the doctor's testimony with photographs than they would have with diagrams. The court concluded that defendant had a fair trial.

State v. Neu


No. 23927-6-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 646



April 11, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Neu, 132 Wn. App. 1030, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1179 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 03-1-03087-3. Judge signing: MARYANN C. MORENO. Date filed: March 1, 2005.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of a controlled substance with the intent to deliver, based on marijuana found in his vehicle incident to the arrest. On appeal, defendant contended the Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, erred in considering drug evidence found during the search.


OVERVIEW: A deputy stopped defendant's vehicle because he was not wearing a seat belt. Defendant identified himself with a "punched" driver's license. A records search confirmed defendant's driver's license was suspended in the third degree. The deputy arrested defendant for third degree driving with a suspended license and searched his vehicle incident to arrest. During the search, the deputy found two baggies of marijuana and a digital scale. The deputy then arrested defendant for possession of a controlled substance with the intent to deliver. Defendant admitted he bought the marijuana and stated he intended to sell it due to financial difficulties. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction and the denial of motion to suppress. The appellate court noted that in order for defendant to take advantage of the rule of law in City of Richmond v. Moore that held that two means of suspending a license were unconstitutional, defendant had to show that his license suspension fell under the unconstitutional statute and not one of constitutional reasons in Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c). As the record did not show why defendant's license was suspended, he was not entitled to relief.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

1664 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Howard


No. 32416-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 586



April 4, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Howard, 132 Wn. App. 1023, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1011 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 04-1-00995-6. Date filed: 09/15/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Richard D Hicks.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) convicting him of unlawful methamphetamine possession and first-degree escape.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was searched after the vehicle he was riding in was pulled over for having a defective muffler. A computer check indicated that a warrant had been issued for his arrest for failing to return to jail from a work release program. Methamphetamine was found both in his pocket and his backpack. On appeal, the court held that the trial court erred by denying defendant's motion to suppress the methamphetamine because the request for information amounted to an illegal seizure that violated defendant's constitutional rights to privacy under Wash. Const. art. I, § 7, and the fact that defendant provided false identification information to the officer could not create an articulable suspicion justifying the further investigation and arrest. Because the officer unlawfully seized defendant before conducting a vehicle search, the methamphetamine should have been suppressed. However, because the State did not rely on any excludable evidence to convict defendant of escape, as the outstanding arrest warrant was valid and existed independently of the illegal seizure, the trial court's error in denying defendant's suppression motion did not require reversal of the escape conviction.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for unlawful methamphetamine conviction was reversed, but his first-degree escape conviction was affirmed.

 

1665 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Farhood v. Allyn


No. 33365-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


132 Wn. App. 371; 131 P.3d 339; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 597



April 4, 2006, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court of Clark County. Superior Court Docket No. 99-2-01218-0. Date Filed In Superior Court: June 1, 2005. Superior Court Judge Signing: John Nichols. Clark County Case No. 99 2 01218 0, Clark County Case No. 01 2 03179 5, Clark County Case No. 05 2 00065 5 (all Clark County Case Nos. consolidated under No. 99 2 01218 0).
Hi-Way Fuel Co. v. Estate of Allyn, 128 Wn. App. 351, 115 P.3d 1031, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1615 (2005)
Farhood v. Asher, 118 Wn. App. 1050, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 2830 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant surviving spouse moved for reconsideration of the reversal of a prejudgment attachment she obtained against a judgment debtor in her wrongful death action. The Superior Court of Clark County, Washington, denied the spouse's motion and granted the motion to vacate the writ brought by respondent, the buyer of the judgment debtor's property, setting aside the sale and quieting title in the property to the buyer. The spouse sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, the spouse challenged the trial court's action quieting title to the property at issue to the buyer. The appellate court found that the spouse did not formally file any post-judgment motion, such as a motion for new trial or relief from judgment. Instead, she simply asked the trial court to refuse to enter the order enforcing the mandate in order to preserve the status quo, suggesting that the parties might develop further facts for a future trial. Further, the issue the spouse raised--the effect, if any, of the adversarial hearing after issuance of the ex parte prejudgment writ--was one the appellate court already had considered in a prior appeal. The spouse made the same arguments she was raising in the instant appeal during the earlier appeal, and the appellate court agreed with the buyer that this particular hearing could not cure the constitutional violation. Thus, the issue the spouse raised in the trial court was one already decided by the appellate court under Wash. R. App. P. 12.2, which barred the spouse's attempt to appeal the order enforcing the clear mandate of the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The appeal was dismissed.

 

1666 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


In re Pers. Restraint of Bowman


No. 53250-2-I, No. 55488-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 569



April 3, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Pers. Restraint of Bowman, 132 Wn. App. 1017, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 990 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were both convicted of second degree felony murder in 1997 and 1998. Defendants then filed personal restraint petitions and claimed that recent case which held that second degree assault could not be a predicate offense for felony murder represented a change in the law material to their conviction such that their petitions were not time-barred.


OVERVIEW: Both defendants were convicted of second degree felony murder with drive-by shooting/reckless endangerment as the predicate underlying offense. Defendants were convicted in 1997 and 1998. In 2002, the state supreme court held that second degree assault could not be a predicate crime for second degree felony murder. Defendants argued that the instant court should apply the reasoning of In the Personal Restraint Petition of Andress and hold that drive-by shooting/reckless endangerment also could not be a predicate offense for second degree felony murder. Pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090(1), the personal restraint petition could not filed more than a year after the judgment became final unless there was a significant change in the law that was material to their convictions. The appellate court held the petitions were time-barred because they were not filed within a year of the judgments becoming final and Andress did not represent a significant change in the law material to their convictions as it only applied where assault was the predicate offense for second degree felony murder.


OUTCOME: Defendants' petitions were time-barred.

 

1667 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mehaffey


No. 55659-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE

1668 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Wiberg


No. 55117-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 600



April 3, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Wiberg, 132 Wn. App. 1018, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 993 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King. County Docket No: 03-1-07854-5. Date filed: 10/20/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Palmer Robinson.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant moved to withdraw his guilty plea, and the motion was denied by the Superior Court of King County, Washington. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On January 23, 2004, the court imposed a 62-month exceptional sentence, based on findings that the parties had agreed to an exceptional sentence, that the offense involved a quantity of cocaine that was substantially larger than for personal use, and that the offense was a major violation of the Uniform Controlled Substances Act. The judgment and sentence was filed on January 26, 2004, and defendant did not seek further review. Defendant sought to withdraw his guilty plea after Blakely v. Washington was decided by the U.S. Supreme Court and claimed that his sentence was unconstitutional because it was based on facts neither charged in the information nor proved to a jury beyond a reasonable doubt. The appellate court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion because the state supreme court held that Blakely was not to be applied retroactively. Also, in imposing the exceptional sentence in this case, the sentencing court expressly relied on former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.535(2)(e)(ii), which defined as an aggravating circumstance the fact that defendant's current offense was a "major violation" of the Uniform Controlled Substances Act.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea was affirmed.

 

1669 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Matheson v. Liquor Control Bd.


No. 23770-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


132 Wn. App. 280; 130 P.3d 897; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 543



March 28, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by, Motion to strike granted by Matheson v. Wash. State Liquor Control Bd., 149 P.3d 378, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 908 (Wash., 2006)
Related proceeding at Matheson v. Gregoire, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 1937 (Wash. Ct. App., July 10, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a cigarette wholesaler licensed in Idaho, challenged a judgment of the Superior Court Kittitas County (Washington) that granted summary judgment in favor of respondent Washington State Liquor Control Board on the wholesaler's petition for return of tobacco products and certain personal property seized by the State as contraband under Wash. Rev. Code § 82.24.130.


OVERVIEW: The wholesaler claimed the cigarette tax was unconstitutional as applied to him as an Indian and that he was exempt under state law. On appeal, the court found that the wholesaler possessed, transported and intended to sell unstamped cigarettes and that no exemption applied; therefore, the contested cigarettes were contraband under Wash. Rev. Code § 82.24.130, and the seized cigarettes, truck, and trailer were subject to forfeiture under § 82.24.130(1)(a), (b). The court rejected the wholesaler's claim that the cigarette tax violated the Commerce Clause because Chapter 82.24 applied evenly to in-state and out-of-state transactions. Also Chapter 82.24 did not unduly burden or discriminate against Indian commerce because the incidence of the tax was on non-Indian or non-tribal Indian consumers. The court found that the wholesaler was not exempt from tax under state law because he was not a Washington licensed wholesaler or a certified out-of-state wholesaler, and his Indian status did not prevent the State from imposing an excise tax on his activities off-reservation. The wholesaler failed to show he was conducting business under tribal license or approval or in Indian country.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

1670 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Wash. Shell Fish v. Pierce County


No. 32471-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


132 Wn. App. 239; 131 P.3d 326; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 536



March 28, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Wash. Shell Fish, Inc. v. Pierce County, 158 Wn.2d 1027, 152 P.3d 347, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 26 (2007)
Related proceeding at Darrell De Tienne & Chelsea Farms v. Shorelines Hearings Bd., 2016 Wash. App. LEXIS 2748 (Wash. Ct. App., Nov. 14, 2016)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant shell fish company challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington affirming respondent county's orders to cease and desist planting and harvesting geoducks without shoreline permits and to cease and desist working in eelgrass beds without authorization as required by the Shoreline Management Act (SMA) and Growth Management Act (GMA).


OVERVIEW: The company was in the business of geoduck aquaculture and leased parcels of shoreland from owners. The company did not have a permit and claimed that it was not required to obtain an SMA permit. The court held that the company engaged in development under Pierce County, Wash., Code § 20.76.030 when it harvested and planted geoducks on the leased properties because the activities prevented the general public from using certain areas of the water. Also, because the company engaged in shoreline development worth more than $2500 when it harvested and planted geoducks, this constituted a substantial development under § 20.76.030. The court also held that § 20.24.030(A) was not ambiguous, and did not exempt commercial geoduck harvesting from the need for a shoreline substantial development permit. The provision clearly subjected geoduck harvesting to one overall qualifier--substantial development permit review under Pierce County, Wash., Code § 20.24.020. Further, the county properly ordered the company to cease working in eelgrass beds on the property where the hearing examiner found that the company was working without the necessary authorization.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

 

1671 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Saunders


No. 53366-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


132 Wn. App. 592; 132 P.3d 743; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 535



March 27, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

 [***1] Order Granting Respondent's Motion to Publish April 24, 2006.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Saunders, 132 Wn. App. 1011, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 876 (2006)
Review denied by State v. Saunders, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 225 (Wash., Apr. 4, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury for the Superior Court of King County (Washington) found defendant guilty of assault in the third degree, domestic violence, and malicious mischief in the third degree, domestic violence. Defendant received a standard range sentence for third degree assault and a 12-month suspended sentence for malicious mischief in the third degree. Without notice to defense counsel, the trial court later ordered him to pay restitution. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The victim, defendant's girlfriend, called 911 from her home. Audibly distressed and crying, she told the operator that defendant, her boyfriend, had just punched her, grabbed her by her throat, and broken her cell phone by throwing it against a wall. She complained of neck pain and accepted the operator's offer of medical aid. The appellate court found that a rational trier of fact could conclude that defendant caused the victim substantial pain and considerable suffering because there was evidence that she complained of neck pain lasting for more than three hours, and that she had swelling on her cheek and an abrasion on her forehead, all of which was consistent with her claim that defendant threw her against a wall and choked her. Thus, there was sufficient evidence to support his conviction for third degree assault, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.031(1)(f). But, the trial court exceeded its authority when it imposed a 12-month suspended sentence for the malicious mischief charge, which carried a maximum sentence of 90 days in jail. Also, under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.753(1), because no notice of the hearing was given to defendant, the restitution order entered was invalid.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction, vacated his malicious mischief sentence and remanded for resentencing, and vacated the order of restitution.

 

1672 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. A.T. P.-R.


No. 23381-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


132 Wn. App. 181; 130 P.3d 877; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 472



March 23, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile appealed the judgment of the Superior Court, Yakima County, Washington, finding him guilty of being a minor in possession of alcohol, Wash. Rev. Code § 66.44.270(2)(a).


OVERVIEW: A group of boys were playing basketball. Appellant, a 17-year-old, was holding a cigarette and standing next to his 15-year-old friend. When the officer asked to see what his friend had in his hand, the friend showed him an open 40-ounce bottle of beer. The officer smelled alcohol emanating from appellant's body. Appellant was charged with being a minor in possession of alcohol under Wash. Rev. Code § 66.44.270(2)(a). He challenged the sufficiency of the evidence to support his disposition. The appellate court held that the odor of alcohol and his close proximity to his friend were insufficient to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that appellant possessed or consumed alcohol. The State provided no evidence that there was alcohol in appellant's system.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the case dismissed with prejudice.

In re Marriage of Pegues


54303-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 465



March 20, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Marriage of Pegues, 132 Wn. App. 1005, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 853 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-3-06308-1. Date filed: 04/23/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Michael J Trickey.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant husband appealed from a decree of dissolution and related orders entered by the Superior Court of King County, Washington, regarding the dissolution of his marriage to respondent wife.


OVERVIEW: The parties had two children together. They separated in 2003, and the matter came to trial in March 2004. The husband represented himself, as he did on appeal. The trial court rejected the husband's allegations that the wife abused the children, found a repeated pattern of domestic violence required limitations on the husband's residential time with the children, imputed income to the husband based upon his choice to pursue a doctorate in education rather than seek continued employment in business based upon his MBA degree, and extended the protection order for five years. The only argument the appellate court could consider on appeal due to the husband's failure to properly brief the court and prepare the record was whether the trial court erred by denying the husband the right to question a domestic violence treatment provider. However, the appellate court held the trial court did not err as the husband failed to lay the foundation the witness was qualified to answer a question regarding what arrangement was in the best interest of the children. The mother was awarded her attorney fees on appeal subject to her compliance with Wash. R. App. P. 18.1(d).


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment and orders were affirmed.

 

1674 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fox


No. 23499-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 424



March 14, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Fox, 132 Wn. App. 1004, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 849 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: County: BENTON. Docket No(s): 03-1-01023-9. Judge signing: CAMERON MITCHELL. Date filed: September 29, 2004.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Benton County trial court, Washington, convicted defendant on two counts of second degree child rape and imposed a standard sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended, inter alia, that the trial court erred in admitting a deputy's testimony about statements made to him by the victim, and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel. The appellate court found that the child's statements to the deputy were not hearsay because they were prior consistent statements and were not offered for their truth, but to rebut the implication that the child was fabricating the allegations; they were also admissible under the excited utterances exception to the hearsay rule. Contrary to defendant's assertion, his counsel was not ineffective by failing to move to dismiss the second rape charge based on joinder principles as the two charges were not based on the same crime. Nor was counsel ineffective for failing to request an instruction telling the jury defendant was not compelled to testify as requesting such an instruction was a tactical decision. And as the conduct that formed the basis of defendant's conviction was clearly prohibited and specifically charged, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.076 was constitutionally precise as applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1675 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Marriage of Momb


No. 23514-9-III, No. 23712-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


132 Wn. App. 70; 130 P.3d 406; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 425



March 14, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by Momb v. Ragone, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 918 (Wash., Dec. 6, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT SPOKANE COUNTY. Superior Court No: 92-3-00729-9. Date filed in Superior Court: 10/21/04 (No. 23514-9III); (12/8/04 (No. 23712-5-III). Superior Court Judge signing: PAUL A. BASTINE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: When the parties were divorced, respondent mother was awarded primary custody of their child. Later, appellant father successfully moved for a change of placement for the child and was awarded primary custody. One year later, he gave notice that he intended to move the child out of state, and the mother objected. The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, denied the father's request for relocation. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the father contended the relocation statutes, Wash. Rev. Code §§ 26.09.260(6), .480, .520, were unconstitutional because they violated a fit custodial parent's fundamental right to autonomy in child-rearing decisions. The appellate court disagreed, finding first that the relocation statutes did not prevent the father from relocating; the trial court's order prevented the child from relocating. Further, the trial court considered each of the factors under Wash. Rev. Code § 26.09.520 in making its decision, and the father did not challenge any of the trial court's findings. When considering the child's relationship with her mother, the trial court found that this relationship was equal to, if not better than, the child's relationship with the father, the child was at an age where her mother was very important to her, the mother was the parent that the child confided in, and the father's new location was not conducive to a continued relationship between the child and her mother. Isolating the child in the father's new location from currently available activities was not a positive factor, and the father's request for relocation was not an exercise in good faith.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Nixon


No. 32681-7-II, No. 32688-4-II consolidated


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 430



March 14, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Nixon, 132 Wn. App. 1002, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 844 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 04-1-00829-1. Date filed: 12/22/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Christine a Pomeroy.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington, for manufacturing methamphetamine (within 1,000 feet of a school bus stop and while possessing a firearm) in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401(2)(b) and unlawful possession of pseudoephedrine with intent to manufacture methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped and arrested defendant for driving with a suspended license. During the search incident to this arrest, the officer found three boxes of Sudafed among other items. The State charged defendant with possession of pseudoephedrine with intent to manufacture methamphetamine. On June 7, police officers visited and searched the trailer where defendant lived. During these searches, the police found evidence of the possession and manufacture of methamphetamine. The police also found firearms in the trailer. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction the evidence obtained following the search incident to the arrest was not obtained unlawfully as the police had probable cause to stop defendant. The evidence was sufficient to find defendant was in unlawful possession of pseudoephedrine with intent to manufacture methamphetamine because a forensic scientist testified that the labels on the boxes listed pseudoephedrine as one of the drugs contained in the Sudafed, leading to the reasonable inference that the boxes contained pseudoephedrine.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

1677 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Soter v. Cowles Publ'g Co.


No. 23136-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


131 Wn. App. 882; 130 P.3d 840; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 404; 34 Media L. Rep. 1598



March 9, 2006, Decided  
March 9, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at Soter v. Cowles Publ. Co., 2006 Wash. LEXIS 949 (Wash., Dec. 6, 2006)
Review granted by Soter v. Cowles Publ. Co., 152 P.3d 1033, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 5 (Wash., 2007)
Affirmed by Soter v. Cowles Publ'g Co., 2007 Wash. LEXIS 958 (Wash., Dec. 27, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant newspaper requested records of an investigation and settlement by appellee school district following the wrongful death of a young student. The district moved for a declaration that the records were exempt from disclosure. The Superior Court for Spokane County (Washington) held that the documents were "classic" attorney work product and exempt from disclosure under Wash. Rev. Code § 42.17.310(1)(j). The newspaper appealed.


OVERVIEW: The student died from anaphylactic shock after being fed peanut-laden food on a school outing. The superintendent was informed of the unfolding tragedy by telephone and immediately called the district's private law firm. Counsel advised that a wrongful death action was a near certainty and then took over all aspects of the district's response and hired a private investigator to gather facts and interview witnesses. The lawyers prepared all documents and quickly negotiated a settlement between the district and the child's parents. The settlement agreement was released. The documents requested were all generated by the district's attorneys and their investigators in preparation for the anticipated wrongful death claim, which quickly followed the child's death. The court's finding that the documents were prepared in anticipation of litigation was easily supported by the record based on the nature of the incident, counsel's advice to the district, and the fact that a claim was in fact filed within days. The documents were memoranda of witnesses' oral statements to the investigator and notes by the district's lawyers of their own pretrial preparations and were "classic" work product.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1678 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Baker


No. 32712-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 296



March 7, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Baker, 131 Wn. App. 1059, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 753 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County Docket. No: 04-1-00767-4. Date filed: 12/09/2005. Judge signing: Hon. Roger A Bennett.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision by the Clark County Superior Court, Washington, suppressing evidence, which resulted in dismissal of the charge that defendant possessed marijuana with intent to deliver.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendant for driving with expired license tags. She told him that her license was suspended, and he arrested her. When he searched defendant's car incident to the arrest, he discovered a brown paper bag containing a $ 20 bill and four baggies of marijuana. Defendant admitted that the marijuana belonged to her and that she had already sold one baggie of it. The State charged her with possession of marijuana with intent to deliver and third degree driving while license suspended (DWLS). Relying on City of Redmond v. Moore, defendant moved to suppress the drug evidence because Moore had held that license suspensions pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.289 and .342(1) were unconstitutional because they did not provide for a hearing prior to suspension of a driver's license and could not justify convictions of DWLS. Thus, the trial court granted the motion to suppress because it was the result of an arrest following an invalid suspension. The appellate court reversed and held that as the officer knew defendant's license was suspended, and had no reason to believe the suspension was invalid, his arrest and the subsequent search of the car was lawful.


OUTCOME: The suppression order and the order dismissing the drug charge were reversed, and the case was remanded for trial.

 

1679 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Krouch


No. 32233-1-II/32567-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 303



March 7, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Cowlitz County. Docket No: 97-1-00156-8. Date filed: 08/04/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Stephen M Warning.
State v. Krouch, 131 Wn. App. 1058, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 748 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington), which denied his motion for a new trial under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8(b)(2) based on the discovery of new evidence. The inmate also filed a personal restraint petition (PRP).


OVERVIEW: The inmate was convicted of first degree assault under an accomplice liability instruction, and this conviction was affirmed on appeal. Thereafter, he filed a motion for a new trial based on newly discovered evidence. The trial court denied the motion, and the inmate appealed. He also filed a PRP, arguing that the evidence at trial was insufficient to show accomplice liability. In affirming, the appellate court determined that the inmate failed to show that the information in some of the affidavits could not have been discovered at trial or within 10 days of the trial since two persons giving the affidavits were among the original defendants in the assault case. Next, there was no evidence to support the reliability of the affidavit of another witness. An alleged recantation was submitted seven years after the original trial and absent the procedures and protections of trial court. No evidentiary hearing on the issue was required. Since there was no newly discovered evidence, the motion was time barred under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090(1). Moreover, the PRP was untimely under this section as well, and it presented no evidence that had not already been considered on direct review.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.
