State v. Farnsworth


No. 32322-2-II consolidated with No. 32903-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


133 Wn. App. 1; 130 P.3d 389; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 305



March 7, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by orders of the Court of Appeals June 14, 2006 and March 13, 2007.   [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by, in part, Review denied by, in part, Remanded by State v. Farnsworth, 151 P.3d 976, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 63 (Wash., 2007)
Amended by State v. Farnsworth, 2007 Wash. App. LEXIS 455 (Wash. Ct. App., Mar. 13, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which convicted him of first-degree robbery and imposed an exceptional sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his convictions for first-degree robbery and his resulting sentence, arguing in part that the trial court denied his right to a speedy trial under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 3.3. The court disagreed and affirmed his two convictions, stating that he failed to object within 10 days of notice of his trial date. Thus, his right to a speedy trial was not violated. The court further held that the trial court did not violate his Sixth Amendment right under Blakely by engaging in a factual comparability analysis when it calculated his offender score for sentencing. The court did however remand to the trial court to review the Utah federal court record to determine what prior felony conviction the Utah court used as the predicate offense to convict defendant of unlawful firearm possession; to make appropriate comparability determinations; to recalculate defendant's offender score; and to resentence defendant if necessary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction, vacated defendant's exceptional sentence, and remanded for resentencing.

 

1681 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Clallam County v. Feakes


No. 33033-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 313



March 7, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Clallam County v. Feakes, 131 Wn. App. 1060, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 756 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clallam County. Docket No: 02-2-00671-2. Date filed: 03/11/2005. Judge signing: Hon. George Lamont Wood.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner challenged the judgment of the Superior Court of Clallam County, Washington, ordering the owner to remove certain signage and to obtain a septic permit, and enjoining the owner from operating an RV park and campground, in the action with respondent county.


OVERVIEW: The county enacted a zoning code in 1982, and amended its zoning code in December 1995. The county sued the owner in 2002 to remove certain signage on his property, to enjoin him from operating an RV park and campground, and to enjoin him from using his broken septic system without a septic permit. The appellate court determined that the issue before it was whether the RV park and campground did not grandfather in under the 1995 zoning amendments. The appellate court ruled that substantial evidence supported the trial court's finding. Substantial evidence indicated that the RV park and campground did not exist until well after 1995. A neighbor testified that the RV park and campground did not exist prior to 2000 or 2001. The owner was unable to present any business records for the rental activity prior to 2001, and there was a lack of any reference to the RV park and campground in submitted business documents and the owner's 1998 letter to the water district. The owner's testimony was the only evidence in the record indicating that the RV park and campground were operating prior to 1995.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


 

1682 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Barton


No. 23036-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 271



February 28, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Barton, 131 Wn. App. 1051, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 682 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Spokane County. Docket No: 02-1-03433-1. Date filed: 05/21/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Maryann C Moreno.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington of taking a motor vehicle without permission and first degree burglary under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.52.020(1)(b). The State cross-appealed alleging the trial court erred in calculating defendant's offender score in washing out certain juvenile class C felony offenses by failing to consider an intervening misdemeanor conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was drinking with his girlfriend and the car owner. When the owner parked the car, defendant pushed her out and drove away. He crashed and left the scene. Soon thereafter, defendant broke into a home. The court held that the State did not comment on the evidence by pointing out defendant's flippant and evasive exchanges with the officers as defendant never quit talking after he was arrested. Also, because intent had to be shown in the burglary charge, defendant opened the door for asking defendant's expert's questions regarding defendant's "silence" by the expert testifying that defendant's capacity was diminished. Also, neither term of the burglary victim and car owner no-contact order exceeded the maximum sentence for convictions. The court concluded that prior juvenile adjudications may be considered by the trial court in setting a sentencing range without being proved to a jury. Finally, the State did not provide any evidence to the trial court to support its "representations" of the 1994 conviction in the face of defendant's specific objection to the use of this conviction in the calculation of his offender score.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Materne


No. 23639-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


131 Wn. App. 734; 129 P.3d 298; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 264



February 28, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Spokane County Superior Court, Washington, which convicted him for possession of methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: An officer stopped defendant for a minor traffic infraction. The officer discovered defendant's driving privileges had been suspended in the third degree and arrested him. In a search incident to the arrest, the officer found a baggie of white powder that tested positive for methamphetamine. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because the statute upon which his arrest was based, third degree driving with license suspended, had been declared unconstitutional in another case. The instant court noted that defendant was entitled to relief only if his license was suspended pursuant to former Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.289 (2002) and former Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.324(1) (1965), the statutes that had been declared unconstitutional. The instant court concluded that because defendant did not identify the statute under which his license was suspended and the record did not reflect the information, it could not review his claim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1684 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Cingular Wireless v. Thurston County


No. 32967-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


131 Wn. App. 756; 129 P.3d 300; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 256



February 28, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:

 [***1] As amended by Order of the Court of Appeals May 23, 2006.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Amended by, On reconsideration by Cingular Wireless, LLC v. Thurston County, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 1048 (Wash. Ct. App., May 23, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant wireless service provider challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which on the provider's appeal of a hearing officer's decision under the Land Use Petition Act (LUPA), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 36.70C, affirmed the hearing examiner's ruling denying the provider's application for a special use permit to erect a cell phone tower in a rural residential area.


OVERVIEW: The county planning department recommended issuance of the permit, and when residents appealed, the hearing officer denied the permit. The trial court held that the examiner could properly reject the permit based on the Thurston County Code even though the provider met the specific wireless communications facility (WCF) requirements. The court affirmed, and held that because the comprehensive plan was not inconsistent with the specific zoning code, the county properly required a proposed WCF to satisfy both the comprehensive plan, under Thurston County, Wash., Code 20.54, and the specific standards in Thurston County, Wash., Code 20.33. The examiner based his decision that the proposed WCF was contrary to the plan's utilities' policy on finding that the WCF failed to meet the general standard contained in the special use code provision. The general standards of Thurston County, Wash., Code 20.54.040 applied independently of, and parallel with, the specific standards of Thurston County, Wash., Code 20.33. Also, because the code clearly stated in multiple provisions that proposed special uses were subject to both general and specific standards, due process was not violated.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the superior court.

 

1685 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State Dep't of Soc. & Health Servs. v. Wilson (In re N.E.R.)


No. 54160-9-I (Consolidated with Nos. 54161-7-I, 55360-7-I, 55361-5-I)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 262



February 27, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Dep't of Soc. & Health Servs. v. Wilson (In re N.E.R.), 131 Wn. App. 1048, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 672 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-7-00226-5. Date filed: 03/23/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Philip G Hubbard Jr.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a mother and father, challenged the findings of the Superior Court of King County (Washington) regarding the statutory requirements under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.34.180 for terminating the relationship between appellants and their two daughters. The petition was filed by respondent Washington State Department of Social and Health Services.


OVERVIEW: The children were declared dependent after it was reported that the mother and children were living in a filthy hotel room. Throughout the dependency proceedings, appellants were not able to maintain housing for any period of time. The court held that although the caseworker appeared to have undermined the parents' trust in the dependency system, substantial evidence supported the trial court's findings inasmuch as the Department fulfilled its obligation to provide information about how to obtain housing. Appellants separated and lost their apartment within six months. The court held that appellants were not prejudiced by any alleged failure to maximize parent-child contact. Evidence supported the finding that there was little likelihood that conditions would be remedied so that the children could be returned to appellants in the near future and that termination was in the girls' best interests. However, because both appellants claimed that their parents were enrolled members of Native-American tribes, the court remanded because it was unclear from the record whether the Indian Child Welfare Act (ICWA) applied to the case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed as to the trial court's findings regarding the statutory requirements for termination. The court reversed and remanded for a determination of whether the ICWA applied.

 

1686 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Donery


No. 31974-8-II Consolidated with: No. 32232-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


131 Wn. App. 667; 128 P.3d 1262; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 233



February 22, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] PART PUBLISHED OPINION


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Amended by State v. Donery, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 2287 (Wash. Ct. App., Oct. 17, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Clallam County, Washington, convicting him of persistent prison misbehavior under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94.070, and defendant filed a personal restraint petition.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was serving a 27-month sentence for a second degree assault. As a result of his misbehavior while in state prison, defendant lost all of his potential early release time for time served at the Washington Department of Corrections (DOC) facilities. But defendant had 38 days of earned early release time from time he spent in county jail awaiting his trial and sentencing. The DOC did not take away the county jail time because it believed it did not have the authority to do so. The appellate court determined that to convict defendant of persistent prison misbehavior the State had to prove that he lost all earned early release time that he could potentially have earned in the state correctional facility. The appellate court ruled that there was adequate evidence in the record to support this conclusion, and Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94.070 was properly applied to defendant. Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.728 required the State to prove that defendant had lost all time within the state system, not the county jail. The persistent prison misbehavior statute applied only to state correctional facilities.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed and the petition was denied.

Clover Park Sch. Dist. No. 400 v. Wash. State Bd. of Educ.


No. 32953-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 236



February 22, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Clover Park Sch. Dist. No. 400 v. Wash. State Bd. of Educ., 131 Wn. App. 1046, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 662 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 04-2-07167-0. Date filed: 02/04/2005. Judge signing: Hon. Sergio Armijo.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant school district No. 400 (District 400) appealed the grant of summary judgment by the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, in favor of respondent school district No. 1 (District 1) that affirmed a decision by respondent educational school district committee that approved a transfer of territory from District 400 to District 1.


OVERVIEW: A Master Planned Committee (MPC) was being developed within the City of DuPont. The current boundaries placed almost all of the commercial property in District 400 and almost all of the residential property in District 1. District 1 sought a transfer of territory from District 400 because the city had issued a mandate to have all of its students within its limits attend school in the same district. The appellate court affirmed the grant of summary judgment in favor of District 1 as, inter alia, (1) the proposed transfer, even if it did decrease funding to District 400, did not violate Wash. Rev. Code §§ 28A.315.015(2) and 28A.315.205(4) because the Committee considered the financial impact and ways to lessen its effect on District 400, (2) the transfer did not exacerbate any existing racial or economic divisions between the two districts, and (3) District 1 did not negotiate in bad faith in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 28A.315.195 because to the extent that negotiations were even required, District 1's refusal to change its position during negotiations did not constitute bad faith.


OUTCOME: The grant of summary judgment was affirmed.

 

1688 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Bradford


No. 32381-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 238



February 22, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Bradford, 131 Wn. App. 1044, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 657 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County, Docket No: 04-1-02776-6, Judgment or order under review, Date filed: 09/03/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Frederick Fleming.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) that convicted him of one count of second-degree burglary and one count of attempted second-degree burglary under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.52.030(1). Defendant challenged the sufficiency of the evidence, and raised claims of error regarding the jury instructions given; the ineffectiveness of his counsel, and improper prosecutorial remarks during closing arguments.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his convictions. The court held that defendant's conviction for burglary was supported by sufficient evidence that included the store owner's photographs of defendant in the store with the broken door and hopping over the counter and searching behind it. Also when defendant was arrested the next night in front of a deli-mart with a broken window, he had items that matched the items taken from the store and was wearing a jacket that matched the person's jacket in the photographs. Also there was sufficient evidence to support his conviction for attempted burglary of the deli-mart where he was acting suspiciously and hiding from police. The court rejected defendant's claims of error as to the permissible inference jury instruction and his claim that his counsel was ineffective for failing to object because even though the instruction regarding the inference of intent was improper for an attempted burglary charge, defendant was also charged with burglary; thus the instruction was warranted. The court held that any improper prosecutorial remarks were harmless where defendant failed to show prejudice.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

State v. Tennyhill


No. 23561-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 213



February 16, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Tennyhill, 131 Wn. App. 1042, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 525 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: BENTON. Docket No(s): 04-1-00560-8. Judge signing: VIC L. VANDER SCHOOR. Date filed: November 17, 2004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Benton County (Washington), which convicted him of the unlawful possession of a controlled substance.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction, arguing that the police unlawfully arrested him and searched him incident to his arrest for the crime of driving while license suspended in the third degree. He argued that his license was unconstitutionally suspended, but the court stated that he failed to prove that assertion. Further, the court stated that the crime of driving while license suspended in the third degree was a constitutionally valid crime under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342. The court thus affirmed, concluding that the officer had adequate probable cause to arrest and search defendant. The court stated that defendant failed to show that his license was suspended under the procedural statutes declared unconstitutional, which were former Wash. Rev. Code §§ 46.20.289 (2002) and 46.20.324(1) (1965). Even if his license had been suspended under those statutes, they were presumptively valid at the time of arrest and were not flagrantly unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1690 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Worden


No. 23791-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 216



February 16, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Worden, 131 Wn. App. 1043, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 527 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 04-1-00289-4. Judge signing: LINDA G. TOMPKINS (Suppression Hearing) SALVATORE F. COZZA (Trial). Date filed: January 27, 2005 (Suppression Hearing) February 3, 2006. (Trial).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, for possession of methamphetamine and the denial of his motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: The driver was pulled over for expired license plate tabs. The driver was arrested for driving while her license was suspended in the third degree. Defendant was a passenger in the vehicle. The officer saw him reach under the passenger seat. The officer asked him to step out of the car. The officer then searched the car incident to the driver's arrest. He found a black leather case under defendant's passenger seat. It contained methamphetamine. The officer arrested defendant. Defendant claimed that as former Wash. Rev. Code §§ 46.20.289 and .324(1), the procedural statutes for suspending a license, had been ruled unconstitutional, the officer had no authority to arrest the driver for a suspended license. The appellate court noted that the crime of driving while license suspended under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c) was not unconstitutional. As an arresting officer did not have to know if an individual's license had been unconstitutionally suspended before arresting an individual for driving with a suspended license, the arrest of the driver was valid and so was the search incident to the arrest. Thus, defendant's conviction and the denial of his motion to suppress were affirmed.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

 

1691 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Martinez


No. 23505-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 217



February 16, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Martinez, 131 Wn. App. 1042, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 523 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: County: GRANT. Docket No(s): 04-1-00078-8. Judge signing: KEN L. JORGENSEN. Date filed: October 26, 2004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of possession of cocaine with intent to deliver, possession of marijuana with intent to deliver, driving while license suspended in the second degree, and use of drug paraphernalia after the Superior Court of Grant County, Washington refused to grant defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had a previous conviction for driving while license suspended in the second degree. The Department of Licensing automatically suspended his license following this conviction. The Department did not provide defendant a hearing before it suspended his license. When defendant was pulled over for following too closely, defendant was arrested when it was determined that he was driving on a suspended license. Defendant's car was searched, and the police found drugs and paraphernalia. The appellate court affirmed the suspension of defendant's license, the search of his car, and his convictions. As defendant had a prior conviction for driving while his license was suspended in the second degree, his license was automatically suspended as a result of the conviction under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(2). That criminal proceeding provided adequate due process. As an administrative hearing was not a constitutional prerequisite to the automatic suspension of a license due to a criminal conviction under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(2), the underlying suspension was proper, and so too were defendant's arrest and the search of his car.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

 

1692 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Marshall


No. 32628-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 208



February 14, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Marshall, 131 Wn. App. 1040, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 515 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Mason County. Docket No: 04-1-00216-8. Judge signing: Hon. James B II Sawyer. Date filed: 11/18/2004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Mason County (Washington) denied defendant's motion to suppress. At a bench trial, the trial court convicted her of unlawful possession of methamphetamine. At a jury trial, the jury found defendant guilty of third degree assault. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer responded to a call from a store employee who was reporting several uncooperative shoplifters. The employee informed the officer that defendant drove a vehicle involved in the shoplifting. The officer contacted police dispatch and learned that, according to the Washington Department of Licensing records, defendant's driving status was suspended in the third degree. He arrested defendant, placed her in the backseat of his squad car, and then searched her car. On the driver's floorboard, the officer found a black nylon duffel bag that contained, inter alia, two metal cups. Residue from one of the metal cups tested positive for methamphetamine. The statute under which defendant was stopped, Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c), was not held to be grossly or flagrantly unconstitutional. Also, there was probable cause for the arrest because the police responded to a call indicating that defendant was involved in shoplifting. Thus, the trial court did not err in admitting the evidence seized as a result of the officer's search. Because the search of her car was lawful, it could not be argued that her counsel was incompetent in resisting the admission of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1693 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Redington


No. 23687-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 174



February 9, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Redington, 131 Wn. App. 1033, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 490 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 03-1-02763-5. Judge signing: TARI S. EITZEN (Suppression Hearing), GREGORY D. SYPOLT (Bench Trial). Date filed: December 7, 2004 (Suppression Hearing), December 20, 2004 (Bench Trial).



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After the Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, denied defendant's motion to suppress drug evidence, he was convicted of the offense of possession of a controlled substance and sentenced accordingly. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Cocaine was found in a search incident to defendant's arrest for driving with a suspended license. On appeal, he argued that the trial court erred in denying his motion to suppress because the statute upon which his arrest was based, third-degree driving with license suspended, was declared unconstitutional. In a challenge to the sufficiency of the evidence, he contended that the State failed to prove that the substance he possessed was cocaine. The appellate court noted that because the record was silent as to the means by which defendant's license was suspended or the grounds for the suspension, he had not met his burden of showing that his argument bore relevance to the record or that his license was suspended under a statute that was declared unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the State had to prove the nature of the controlled substance as an essential element of the crime of unlawful possession of a controlled substance. The appellate court concluded that defendant's admission that he possessed cocaine together with the positive field test was sufficient to support his conviction under Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1694 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Hearn


No. 23715-0-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


131 Wn. App. 601; 128 P.3d 139; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 171



February 9, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On two separate occasions, defendant was stopped by police for traffic infractions; on each occasion, she was arrested when police discovered she was driving with a suspended license. On each occasion, police discovered methamphetamine among her possessions in the vehicle in the search incident to arrest. The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, convicted defendant on two counts of possession of methamphetamine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendant contended that the evidence obtained from the search of her vehicle was inadmissible because the statute upon which her arrest was based was declared unconstitutional in City of Redmond v. Moore; the trial court erred when it ordered that as a condition of her community placement she refrain from associating with known drug offenders; and the trial court erred when it determined, for sentencing purposes under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.285(4), that a vehicle was used in the commission of a felony. The appellate court ruled that it could not review defendant's claim regarding the unconstitutional statute as she failed to show that Moore was relevant. Further, the restriction imposed as a condition of defendant's community placement was not unreasonable as associating with known drug offenders was conduct intrinsic to possession of methamphetamine and was directly related to the circumstances of the crime. However, the appellate court agreed with defendant that the drugs found in her purse did not have a reasonable relation to the operation of the vehicle and the use of the vehicle did not contribute in some reasonable degree to the commission of the crime.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed, but the finding that defendant used a motor vehicle in the commission of her crimes was reversed, and the case was remanded for further proceedings.

 

1695 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Paulson


No. 32382-6-II (consolidated with 32418-1-II)


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


131 Wn. App. 579; 128 P.3d 133; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 156



February 7, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Two defendants sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which convicted them of first-degree animal cruelty in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 16.52.205.


OVERVIEW: Defendants appealed their convictions, but the court affirmed, stating that it was difficult to imagine that any dog, especially one who had followed the two defendants around for almost two weeks, would not unduly suffer with a killing scheme involving shooting the dog with an arrow. The means showed an intent to cause undue suffering because defendants would not have continued to shoot at the dog if it had died with the first shot. Furthermore, pulling the arrows out of a living dog to shoot it repeatedly aggravated the suffering. It was within defendants' ability to understand that those repeated actions intentionally inflicted suffering in the course of killing the dog. Thus, the trial court could have concluded that defendants possessed the requisite intent. Interpreting the evidence in a manner most favorable to the State, the record clearly established sufficient evidence of defendants' intent to cause undue suffering and their guilt under Wash. Rev. Code § 16.52.205(1). Further, it was not error for the trial court to give the second defendant up to 24 months to complete the animal cruelty prevention program and his community service hours under Wash. Rev. Code § 16.52.200.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

1697 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Ludwig v. Dep't of Ret. Sys.


No. 32462-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


131 Wn. App. 379; 127 P.3d 781; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 124



January 31, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant sued respondent Washington State Department of Retirement Systems (DRS), asserting that she was deprived of her vested right to a survivor benefit. The Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington, ruled in favor of the DRS, and the claimant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent elected to receive a reduced monthly retirement allowance so she could provide a survivor benefit to a designated beneficiary. The decedent's designated beneficiary was her niece, the claimant. Substitute House Bill (SHB) 2604 authorized certain retired members of the state pension system to delete what had previously been an irrevocable survivor benefit in exchange for increased monthly benefits. The decedent deleted her designation of a survivor benefit in favor of the claimant. The decedent's request was made effective with her June 2000 benefit, and the decedent died in May 2001. The claimant maintained that SHB 2604 deprived her of a vested right in the decedent's survivor benefit. The appellate court ruled that the claimant had no vested right in the decedent's pension because her "right" derived from nothing more than an expectation in the continuation of a law that made the survivor designation irrevocable. Also, since the State did not deprive the claimant of any potential vested right, the claimant's due process claim failed. The decedent, not the State, exercised the option to revoke the nonspousal survivor benefit.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Elgin


No. 23346-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 95



January 26, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Elgin, 131 Wn. App. 1020, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 370 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 04-1-00271-1. Date filed: July 26, 2004. Judge signing: MARYANN C. MORENO.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court, Spokane County (Washington), which denied his motion to suppress evidence that was obtained by the police after he was arrested for driving while license suspended in the third degree, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c). Defendant was ultimately convicted of possession of methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped defendant for a broken taillight. The officer checked the status of his license. It was suspended in the third degree. The officer arrested defendant for the crime of driving while license suspended in the third degree. A second officer searched defendant's car incident to the arrest. She found methamphetamine. The State charged defendant with possession of methamphetamine. He moved to suppress the drug evidence on the authority of Wash. Const. art. I, § 7. The trial court denied his motion and found him guilty at a bench trial. On appeal, the court found that the officer had legal authority to arrest defendant. Further, § 46.20.342(1)(c) was not unconstitutional at the time of arrest. The arrest and subsequent search were lawful. The exclusionary rule did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.

 

1699 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Jones


No. 23459-2-III, No. 23460-6-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 98



January 26, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Jones, 131 Wn. App. 1021, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 372 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 04-1-00015-8 (23459-2-III), 04-1-00655-5 (23460-6-III). Judge signing: TARI S. EITZEN. Date filed: September 23, 2004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, convicted defendant of several charges, including possessing a controlled substance, methamphetamine. The drug was found during a search subsequent to an arrest for driving while license suspended. The trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the methamphetamine found subsequent to his arrest for third degree driving while license suspended should have been suppressed. The appellate court found that defendant's stipulation to not contest the stop and/or search was a knowing, intelligent waiver of all factual, procedural, or legal issues he might try to assert if his participation in drug court was terminated. Thus, defendant waived his right to contest the search that produced the methamphetamine. Defendant did not show that his license was suspended under the specific unconstitutional provision. Defendant had affirmatively agreed to his offender score and standard range sentence. The agreement represented a failure to identify a factual dispute for the court's resolution and a failure to request an exercise of the court's discretion, which waived the challenge to his offender score. No record supported defendant's contention he served more than 88 days prior to sentence. The remaining alleged facts by defendant were based on evidence outside the appellate court's record.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1700 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Wolverton v. Young


No. 24117-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 78



January 24, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Wolverton v. Young, 131 Wn. App. 1020, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 368 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: FRANKLIN. Docket No(s): 04-2-50599-5. Judge signing: ROBERT G. SWISHER. Date filed: January 4, 2005.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, cities and an animal control authority, filed a motion to dismiss appellant citizens' complaint that the animal control authority improperly and inhumanely performed its animal control services contract and that the cities were responsible for the conduct of the animal control authority. The Superior Court of Franklin County, Washington, found that the citizens lacked standing. The citizens appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court noted that the citizens had standing to challenge illegal governmental acts related to the letting and managing of the contracts without pleading a special injury or violation of a unique right to challenge illegal acts. The citizens lacked standing to challenge the cities' discretionary acts unless they could demonstrate a special injury, and none of the citizens owned an animal that was impounded or mistreated. The citizens had taxpayer standing to challenge the bidding procedures and the trial court erred by dismissing the public contract bidding claim. The citizens lacked third party beneficiary standing because the animal control authority did not assume a direct obligations to them when the it made a contract with the cities. Sufficient facts were alleged with regard to two of the citizens' 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims. Because some of the claims should not have been dismissed, and the citizens had standing to pursue these claims, the trial court erred by dismissing the citizens' requests for injunctive and declaratory relief. The citizens lacked next friend status to sue on behalf of animals. The citizens were allowed to amend their complaint.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed where the citizens lacked standing to challenge the cities' discretionary acts and as third party beneficiaries. The § 1983 claims, except for those relating to two citizens, were dismissed. The judgment was reversed where the taxpayers did have standing. Also, the trial court erred by denying the motion for leave to amend.

1702 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. O'Brien


No. 54827-1-I Consolidated with: No. 54828-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 84



January 23, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. O'Brien, 131 Wn. App. 1015, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 349 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 04-1-00027-5. Judge signing: Hon. Anita L Farris. Date filed: 08/02/2004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed orders of the Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington suppressing evidence in two cases based on the trial court's reasoning that the arrests of defendants for driving with suspended licenses (DWLS 3), Wash. Rev. Code §§ 46.20.342, 46.20.289, were unconstitutional because the underlying suspensions were based on statutes held to be unconstitutional in the Moore decision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant one was arrested for failure to appear on a charge of DWLS 3, and methamphetamine was recovered. Defendant two was arrested for DWLS 3, and methamphetamine and an unlawful firearm were recovered. The court reversed and held that the Moore decision did not address the constitutionality of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342. Instead, in the course of defending their criminal charges for driving while license suspended, the Moore defendants challenged the constitutionality of the statutes leading to the license suspension underlying the criminal charges. Because defendant one's identification information revealed that his driving status was suspended in the third degree, the deputy had probable cause to arrest defendant one for driving with a suspended license. Because the criminal statute at issue has not been held to be unconstitutional, and because the arrests here were based on a valid warrant and probable cause, the trial court erred in suppressing the evidence discovered in the searches incident to the arrests. Other appellate divisions had concluded that Moore did not affect the validity of other defendants' arrests for DWLS 3.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the orders of the trial court.

Mansour v. King County


No. 55292-9-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


131 Wn. App. 255; 128 P.3d 1241; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 61



January 23, 2006, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual appealed an order by the Superior Court of King County, Washington, that affirmed the decisions of the King County Animal Control and King County Board of Appeals that ordered the individual to remove his dog from King County or have it euthanized.


OVERVIEW: The individual had received a notice about letting his dogs run loose in the neighborhood, but his housekeeper allowed his dogs to go outside, and the dog picked up a cat. While most of the cat's injuries were likely to have been caused by a car accident, the cat also had puncture wounds that were consistent with being bit. The cat was euthanized. As a result of the cat's injuries, Animal Control issued a removal notice to the individual indicating that his offending dog had to be removed from the county or euthanized. The individual appealed the ruling to the Board and sought to subpoena and/or depose witnesses and requested production of veterinary documents regarding the cat and the cat's body for evaluation, but the Board denied the requests. Also, the Board acted in an appellate capacity to determine if Animal Control's order was arbitrary or capricious. The appellate court reversed the decision of the trial court as (1) the individual was denied due process rights by not being allowed to conduct discovery, (2) the improper standard of proof violated the individual's due process rights, and (3) the individual was not given proper notice that his dog was considered vicious.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was reversed, and the matter was remanded to the Board of Appeals.

 

1704 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Davis


No. 32618-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


131 Wn. App. 246; 126 P.3d 827; 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 44



January 18, 2006, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review pending at State v. Davis, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 810 (Wash., Oct. 10, 2006)
Review denied by State v. Davis, 145 P.3d 1215, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 835 (Wash., Nov. 2, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington) that convicted him of unlawful storage of ammonia in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.55.020 and denied his pre-trial motion to dismiss the charges based on defendant's claim that § 69.55.020 was unconstitutionally vague on its face and as applied to his case. The charges stemmed from a citizen's report that methamphetamine was being manufactured on her property.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed Wash. Rev. Code § 69.55.020 was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to provide legal citations to the applicable federal and state regulations pertaining to the storage and handling of ammonia, and the standards were hard to find. The court noted that the Washington Supreme Court had previously rejected this argument and held that a statute that incorporated detailed standards that were difficult to find did not overcome the strong presumption of constitutionality. The court held that § 69.55.020 put the average citizen on notice of the agency regulations controlling the storage of ammonia. The court found that § 69.55.020(1) indicated the relevant federal agency, i.e., the Department of Transportation (DOT), and that § 69.55.020(2) directly identified regulations. Also § 69.55.020 plainly pertained to situations where a person "possessed" pressurized ammonia gas. The court concluded that because defendant did not set forth facts regarding what steps, if any, he undertook to locate and comply with the applicable federal and state regulations, he failed to show that § 69.55.020 was vague as applied to a reasonable person or himself.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

 

1705 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Vessey


No. 32620-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 47



January 18, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Vessey, 131 Wn. App. 1012, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 339 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Grays Harbor County. Docket No: 04-1-00328-1. Date filed: 11/22/2004. Judge signing: Hon. David E Foscue.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court of Grays Harbor County of second degree trafficking in stolen property under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.82.055(1). The trial court imposed a sentence of two months and ordered him to pay $1,800 in restitution.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted taking an awning structure and selling it for scrap. He said that he had permission from two employees to take scrap from the yard, but could not identify the employees. The court held that whether the material was scarp metal or not, defendant had no right to take the property of another that had value. Therefore, the State provided sufficient evidence that proved all the elements, including recklessness, of second degree trafficking of stolen property. The court also held that § 9A.82.055 was not vague because an ordinary person would understand that one would have to have possession in order to sell something. Thus, a sensible, meaningful, and practical interpretation of the statute left no room for a reasonable person to guess at its meaning or to differ as to its application. Also, the jury instruction regarding a person acting with knowledge was not confusing because the verdict of the lesser crime of second degree trafficking showed that the instructions on knowledge and recklessness actually informed the jury on the correct elements of the crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

State v. Thomas


No. 53474-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 41



January 17, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Thomas, 131 Wn. App. 1009, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 329 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 00-1-01828-9. Date filed: 09/22/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Leroy McCullough.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which denied his motion for a continuance during his sentencing hearing. He had pled guilty to two counts of rape of a child in the first degree and one count of sexual exploitation of a minor arising from the sexual abuse by way of an Alford plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant asserted that the trial court's refusal to continue a sentencing hearing for the second time so that he could present an expert's evaluation on his amenability to treatment and eligibility for a Special Sex Offender Sentence Alternative (SSOSA) was an abuse of discretion and a violation of his constitutional right to due process. The court affirmed on appeal however, stating that the trial court assumed that defendant was eligible for a SSOSA and then considered whether the offender and the community would benefit from the imposition of the SSOSA. It was clear from the record that the trial court properly exercised its discretion by basing the denial of a SSOSA on information admitted by the plea agreement or admitted, acknowledged, or proved at trial or sentencing. Contrary to defense counsel's argument, the trial court followed the required procedures contained in former Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.110 (2000) (recodified as Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.500 by 2001 Wash. Laws ch. 10, § 6). The trial court did not prevent defendant from presenting meaningful arguments by failing to continue the hearing to allow a later introduction of an evaluation involving support for a SSOSA.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Corder


No. 23315-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 31



January 12, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Corder, 131 Wn. App. 1009, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 328 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: BENTON. Docket No(s): 03-1-01191-0. Judge signing: ROBERT G. SWISHER. Date filed: August 13, 2004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to two counts of first degree rape of a child, one count of second degree rape of a child, one count of third degree rape of a child, and two counts of possession of depictions of minors engaged in sexually explicit conduct. The Superior Court, Benton County (Washington) imposed an exceptional sentence of 600 months. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Inter alia, defendant argued that the information charging him with two counts of possession of depictions of a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct omitted the essential statutory element of knowledge. He was charged with two counts of possession of such depictions under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.070 which stated that a person who knowingly possessed visual or printed matter depicting a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct was guilty of a class C felony. The knowledge element required the State to prove defendant was not only aware that the materials were in his or her possession, but also knowledge of the general nature of the materials possessed. Although the caption of the charging document cited to the correct statute, § 9.68A.070, the description of the charges for counts V and VI cited to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68.070 instead. That scrivener's error was not of a magnitude to require reversal on its own. But, as the State failed to provide defendant with the correct statutory citation for the charge of possession of depictions of a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct, the incorrect statutory reference that the State provided did not give notice to defendant.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentence for the charges of first, second, and third degree rape of a child were affirmed. The charges of possession of depictions of a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct was reversed and dismissed without prejudice to the State's ability to refile and the case was remanded to the trial court for correction of the scrivener's error in the listing of the victim's birth date in the information.

State v. Hanna


No. 32123-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 23



January 10, 2006, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 03-1-02236-9. Date filed: 08/12/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Wm Thomas McPhee.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which convicted her for methamphetamine possession in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401(d).


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed her drug conviction, but the court affirmed, stating that the trial court did not err in denying her motion to suppress. Defendant's cited caselaw did not nullify probable cause for her driving while license suspended arrest. Further, the doctrine of invited error precluded her from complaining on appeal about the testimony at issue because she both agreed in advance to the question and answer's propriety and failed to object below that the State deviated from the agreed format. Her counsel was not ineffective because he failed to support her argument as required by Wash. R. App. P. 10.3. The uncontroverted testimony showed that, contrary to defendant's assertion, the officer exercised his discretion to determine whether issuing a citation or arresting defendant was the more appropriate cause of action. Therefore, defense counsel did not render ineffective assistance in failing to argue for suppression of the evidence on that ground. Further, there was nothing inherently suggestive of defendant's guilt in the officer's testimony.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

No. 32415-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 26

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which convicted him of possession of child pornography with sexual motivation, first degree child rape, and first degree child molestation.


OVERVIEW: A trooper stopped defendant for failing to wear his seat belt and subsequently arrested him on an outstanding warrant for driving with a suspended license (DWLS). Probable cause supported defendant's arrest for DWLS. The arrest was valid as was the search incident to it and the fruits of the search were admissible.

State v. J. E.


No. 54646-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3211



December 12, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 04-8-00833-8. Date filed: 06/29/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Suzanne M Barnett.
State v. J.E., 130 Wn. App. 1043, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3424 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile pled guilty to second degree robbery but appealed the finding by the Superior Court of King County, Washington, that his prior adjudications did not arise from the "same course of conduct."


OVERVIEW: In July 2002, defendant and an accomplice trespassed onto the property of the victims. While the boys were hiding in the victims' backyard, they let the dog out of its kennel, took off its collar, and dumped out the dog's food. A neighbor observed the boys lighting pipe bombs in the victims' driveway and throwing unknown objects at the victims' house. As the boys were leaving, they both put dirt on the victims' vehicles in the driveway and damaged one of the driver's side windows of an automobile. Defendant claimed that the July 2002 crimes arose from the "same course of conduct." The appellate court affirmed the disposition order and held that the prior convictions did not arise from the "same course of conduct" under Wash. Rev. Code § 13.40.020(7)(a) as the intent was different for malicious mischief than it was for criminal trespass. The appellate court also held that defendant's Sixth Amendment rights were not violated by not having a jury determine if the prior convictions arose from the same course of conduct as such finding by a trial court could only lower the applicable sentencing range.


OUTCOME: The disposition order was affirmed.

 

1712 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Des Moines v. Gray Businesses


No. 54683-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


130 Wn. App. 600; 124 P.3d 324; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3090



December 5, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Reconsideration denied by City of Des Moines v. Gray Businesses, LLC, 2006 Wash. App. LEXIS 99 (Wash. Ct. App., Jan. 30, 2006)
Review pending at City of Des Moines v. Gray Bus., LLC, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 865 (Wash., Oct. 31, 2006)
Review denied by City of Des Moines v. Gray Bus., LLC, 149 P.3d 379, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 969 (Wash., Dec. 7, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent corporation filed a regulatory takings claim against appellant city, alleging the city terminated its nonconforming use, which in turn denied the corporation its right to lease its land. The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment on the takings issue. The King County Superior Court (Washington) granted the corporation's motion and awarded the corporation the damages it requested as well as attorney fees. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation leased space in its mobile home park, operating it as a legal nonconforming use. The city notified the corporation that it could no longer fill vacant mobile home spaces at the mobile home park because the corporation had never submitted a site plan required by an ordinance (site plan regulation). That prompted the corporation to file the regulatory takings claim. The city did not confer the corporation's private property rights to anyone; thus, this case had to be analyzed as a challenge to the city's exercise of the police power. In this "as applied" challenge, the appellate court was required to balance the State's interest against the regulation's adverse impact on the corporation. The appellate court considered the regulation's impact on the property, the extent the regulation interfered with investment-backed expectations, and the character of the government action. Because the site plan regulation was a valid exercise of the city's police power, and the application of the regulation to the mobile home park did not destroy or derogate a fundamental attribute of the corporation's ownership, there was no regulatory taking.


OUTCOME: The trial court was reversed, and the case was remanded for entry of summary judgment in favor of the city.

State v. Smith


No. 54175-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


130 Wn. App. 721; 123 P.3d 896; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3089



December 5, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by State v. Smith, 157 Wn.2d 1026, 142 P.3d 609, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 659 (Wash., Sept. 7, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, King County (Washington) held a hearing at which the State was required to prove defendant's violation of his community placement sentence by a preponderance of the evidence, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.634(3)(c). The court found defendant had violated a condition of community placement and sentenced him to the time he had already served in custody. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant possessed a movie which was considered pornographic. He contended he was not afforded due process because he was punished for violating a rule that was unconstitutionally vague. However, he had not shown that the prohibition was unconstitutionally vague. An ordinary person would know, without having to consult a treatment specialist or a community corrections officer, that the restriction on defendant's conduct prohibited possession of the movie. He also contended the restriction of the materials he was allowed to possess or view was an unlawful delegation of powers. The version of the Sentencing Reform Act in effect at the time defendant committed his crimes authorized the sentencing court to order, as a sentence condition, that the offender comply with any crime-related prohibitions, pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.120(8)(c)(v) (1992). Defendant argued the sentencing court improperly delegated its duty to define crime-related prohibitions. This argument was not presented below, but any improper delegation that may have occurred did not amount to a manifest constitutional error warranting appellate review despite the lack of objection below.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1714 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Clinkenbeard


No. 23189-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


130 Wn. App. 552; 123 P.3d 872; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3043



November 29, 2005, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Superior Court Okanogan County (Washington) of sexual misconduct with a minor in the first degree under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.093(1)(b). Defendant, a bus driver, allegedly had a relationship with a high school student.


OVERVIEW: While evidence indicated that the sexual component did not begin until after the student turned 18, it also showed the romantic relationship began when the student was only 12. Defendant asserted that § 9A.44.093(1)(b) was unconstitutional on its face and as applied in his case. The court held that defendant could not show that § 9A.44.093(1)(b) was facially unconstitutional because he could not show that there was no set of circumstances in which it could be constitutionally applied. Applying a rational basis review, the court held that because the statute was not wholly irrelevant to the goal of preventing the exploitation of students, and therefore not arbitrary, § 9A.44.093(1)(b) did not violate defendant's right to substantive due process. Furthermore, the singling out of school employees had a basis that was rationally related to compelling government purposes. As such, the application of § 9A.44.093(1)(b) to the case did not constitute an equal protection violation. However because the only evidence of substantive guilt was out-of-court statements made by the student, there was insufficient evidence to convict defendant of sexual misconduct with a minor.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction with prejudice.

Stamm v. Guardianship Servs. of Seattle


No. 53334-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3030



November 28, 2005, Filed

Stamm v. Guardianship Servs. (In re Stamm), 130 Wn. App. 1034, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3390 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a former ward (ward), sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which found in favor of respondent, the Guardianship Services of Seattle (guardian). The ward appealed the award of guardian fees, attorney fees, and costs against him.


OVERVIEW: In a successive appeal arising from a guardianship proceeding, the ward appealed the awards of guardian fees, attorney fees, and costs to the guardian. The court affirmed, stating that under both a substantial evidence and a de novo review of the challenged factual findings, the record supported them. There was no breach of any fiduciary duty owed by the guardian to the ward. Additionally, Wash. Rev. Code § 11.92.010 was not unconstitutional. The trial court patiently considered extensive litigation of matters involving 12 superior court hearings and 6 interlocutory rulings by the court's commissioner. The ward simply failed to establish the existence of a constitutional right to unlimited court access provided by the guardian statutes. The award of attorney fees was proper pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 11.96A.150 because there was no breach by the guardian or its counsel, and the ward dis not contest either the reasonableness of the number of hours or the billing rate. Thus, there was no basis for reversing the trial court's attorney fee award.

1716 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Robertson v. Parks & Rec. Comm'n


No. 55675-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


135 Wn. App. 1; 145 P.3d 379; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3041



November 28, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] Order Granting Respondents' Motion to Publish dated January 18, 2006.


PRIOR HISTORY: Robertson v. Wash. State Parks & Rec. Comm'n, 130 Wn. App. 1038, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3404 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondents, the Washington State Parks and Recreation Commission and a private landowner (hereinafter, the Commission), agreed on an exchange of State owned land for private land. Appellants, several other citizens of the locale (the citizens), disputed the valuation of the State land. The Superior Court of San Juan County, Washington, held the Washington Administrative Procedure Act (APA) precluded judicial review. The citizens sought review.


OVERVIEW: The Commission had filed a motion to dismiss for lack of subject matter jurisdiction and failure to state a claim upon which relief could be granted, asserting the APA exempted its decision from judicial review. On appeal, the Commission asserted that under either Wash. Rev. Code § 34.05.010(3)(a) or (c), the APA excluded from the definition of "agency action" its approval of the land exchange. The citizens contended that a land exchange was not a simple acquisition of real estate and therefore Wash. Rev. Code § 34.05.010(3)(a) did not apply. The appellate court concluded that the plain language of § 34.05.010(3)(a) indicated that the Washington Legislature intended the exception to be broad because it exempted from judicial review real estate acquisitions by any means. It was apparent the legislature considered an exchange of real estate to be a means of acquisition. For example, Wash. Rev. Code § 79.36.310 authorized the Washington Department of Natural Resources to acquire property interests to access state lands. The appellate court held the APA excluded from judicial review agency decisions to acquire real estate by any means and an exchange was a means of acquisition.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1717 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


McKinney v. Cunniffe


NO. 55631-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3042



November 28, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at McKinney v. Cunniffe, 130 Wn. App. 1038, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3403 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 04-2-30473-3. Date filed: 01/03/2005. Judge signing: Hon. James D Cayce.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sued appellee mother, his ex-wife, for alienating their son's affections. The Superior Court of King County, Washington, held that alienation of a child's affections was not a cause of action in Washington as between parents and dismissed the case on the grounds that the father failed to state a claim. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the father contended the trial court erred in dismissing his claim. The appellate court disagreed, holding that the appropriate remedy was in the family court under Wash. Code ch. 26.09, not through tort litigation. The parties' own agreed-upon parenting plan allowed for remedies, and the father had already availed himself of those remedies offered by ch. 26.09. In addition, the cause of action the father advocated was not in the best interests of the child; it was not in the child's best interests to be used as a vehicle for one parent to extract money from the other. The father's allegation that the dismissal of his claim for loss of consortium constituted unconstitutional sexual discrimination was not considered by the appellate court as the academic article he asked the appellate court to consider regarding how fathers were alienated of their children's affections twice as often as mothers was not before the trial court and was not in the record on appeal. The father's 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claim failed because he did not include it in his amended complaint; since § 1983 claims had to be pleaded with specificity, the trial court did not err by not considering it.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Pacas


No. 23375-8-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


130 Wn. App. 446; 123 P.3d 130; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2939



November 22, 2005, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court, Benton County (Washington) convicted defendant of unlawful possession of methamphetamine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police arrested and searched defendant incident to arrest for the crime of driving while license suspended in the third degree under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c). Defendant moved to suppress the drug evidence based on his belief that the Washington Supreme Court had declared the crime of driving while license suspended in the third degree to be unconstitutional. His motion was denied. Defendant was convicted, and he appealed. The Washington Supreme Court had not declared the actual crime of driving while license suspended in the third degree ( Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c)) to be unconstitutional. The officer had the legal authority to arrest defendant under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c) and § 10.31.100(3)(e). An officer could arrest an individual if there was probable cause that the crime of driving while license suspended in the third degree had been committed. Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c) was not unconstitutional (or flagrantly unconstitutional). The officer also had probable cause to believe that defendant committed the crime of driving while license suspended. The arrest and subsequent search were then lawful.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1719 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Mills


No. 31786-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2895



November 15, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Mills, 130 Wn. App. 1025, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3351 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Grays Harbor County. Docket No: 03-1-00115-8. Date filed: 04/19/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Gordon L Godfrey.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Grays Harbor County, Washington, convicted defendant for driving while intoxicated and driving with a revoked license. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the police officer illegally stopped and arrested him. The appellate court noted that defendant never filed a written motion contesting the legality of his arrest. He did not announce that he wanted to do that until after the State rested its case at trial, and even after trial he did not file a written motion or attempt to schedule a post-trial hearing. He deprived the State of an opportunity to present evidence on the legality of his arrest. Defendant waived review of whether a scientific foundation was required under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.502(4) where at trial, the State offered the breath test results without first laying a scientific foundation. Defendant told the court he did not object. The instruction did not improperly comment on the evidence where it did no more than accurately state the law. The appellate court had no way to review defendant's claim that his driving record should not have been admitted because there was no foundation. Defendant did not include the exhibit number and did not include the document in the record on appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1720 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Watson


No. 32332-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


130 Wn. App. 376; 122 P.3d 939; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2901



November 15, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by State v. Watson, 157 Wn.2d 1016, 142 P.3d 608, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 627 (2006)
Affirmed by State v. Watson, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 211 (Wash., Apr. 5, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which convicted him for the failure to register as a sex offender in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.130(4)(a)(i).


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged his conviction for failure to register as a sex offender, arguing that the registration statute, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.130(4)(a)(i), was unconstitutionally vague because it failed to advise registrants that they must register after release from confinement for probation violations regardless of whether their registration information changed since their initial registration upon release into probationary status. The court disagreed and affirmed, stating that the statute was not void for vagueness under the Fourteenth Amendment. Confinement on the basis of probation violations was a continuing consequence of the original prosecution rather than part of a new prosecution. Although probation status might determine the degree of restraint, the restraint was still a result of the original offense. Furthermore, nothing in the statute suggested that a prior registration exempted a registrant from later registration requirements as long as the registrant was returning to the same address. Later restraint based on probation violations was a continuing consequence of the original offense, and the statute was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1721 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Duckett


NO. 55087-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2879



November 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Duckett, 130 Wn. App. 1023, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3343 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 04-1-11839-1. Date filed: 09/17/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Richard F McDermott.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County (Washington) convicted defendant following a jury trial of two counts of first degree child molestation involving his girlfriend's younger sister. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in excluding an affidavit filed by the victim's mother in a petition for a protection order against the victim's father, and challenged a condition of community custody regarding possession of pornography.


OVERVIEW: Defendant molested his girlfriend's 11-year old sister. During trial, the defense sought to introduce an affidavit the victim's mother filed in support of a petition for a protection order restraining the victim's father. The defense theory was that the mother used official court proceedings to control the men in her life. Citing Wash. R. Evid. 608, the trial court excluded it as irrelevant and inadmissible. As the mother would have testified that she actually filed the affidavit and that its allegations were true, the trial court properly concluded that the affidavit was inadmissible under Rule 608. But the trial court also reasonably concluded that the affidavit was not relevant as substantive evidence under Wash. R. Evid. 404(b). Because the actual allegations in the affidavit were not relevant to the defense theory and the State did not challenge the witness's testimony that such an affidavit existed, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in excluding the affidavit. The appellate court concluded the trial court should amend the community placement condition to provide a more specific definition consistent with defendant's treatment status and goals.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed and the case was remanded for reconsideration of the condition regarding pornographic material.
