State v. Conshafter


No. 54808-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2882



November 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Conshafter, 130 Wn. App. 1022, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3340 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-1-08875-3. Date filed: 07/12/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Richard a Jones.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of King County (Washington) of second degree burglary. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his right to confrontation was violated when statements made by the 911 caller were admitted into evidence. The court of appeals disagreed. The State merely pointed out that the 911 caller indicated that he saw defendant climb over the fence and enter the area of the trailers. Defendant admitted that in his own testimony. Moreover, in closing argument, defense counsel used the statements attributed to the 911 caller as a means of impeaching the credibility of an officer. The properly admitted evidence was more than sufficient to prove defendant's guilt. Defendant was seen rummaging though desk drawers inside the locked trailer and was caught with the stolen property. Therefore, any error resulting from the admission of the 911 caller's statements was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. However, the court miscalculated his offender score when it used his prior Oregon conviction for identity theft. In addition, the State failed to prove that he had been convicted of burglary in California.


OUTCOME: The conviction was affirmed. The case was remanded for resentencing.

 

1723 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gugsa


NO. 53806-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2883



November 14, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Gugsa, 130 Wn. App. 1021, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3337 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-1-08131-7. Date filed: 02/06/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Michael C Hayden.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County (Washington) convicted defendant of two counts of first-degree assault, each with a deadly weapon. Defendant appealed, arguing that the court's imposition of consecutive sentences without a jury fact-finding of separate and distinct criminal conduct violated his right to a jury trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted on two counts of first-degree assault, one for each stabbing victim, and the jury found he was armed with a deadly weapon during each. The trial court found that the two assaults were separate and distinct criminal conduct and imposed consecutive sentences, as well as consecutive two-year terms for each deadly weapon enhancement. Defendant challenged the deadly weapon sentence enhancements and calculation of his sentencing range. The appellate court agreed that the sentencing range was miscalculated. The right to have a jury determine all of the facts necessary to support consecutive sentencing did not apply to the imposition of consecutive sentences for two or more serious violent offenses under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.589(1)(b). Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.533(4) required deadly weapon enhancements to be added to the total standard range for all offenses for which the offender was being sentenced. Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.533(4)(e) required that the deadly weapon enhancements run consecutively to each other. The trial court properly imposed consecutive deadly weapon sentence enhancements.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, and the case was remanded for the trial court to correct a scrivener's error in calculating defendant's sentence range.

 

1724 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Det. of Greenwood


No. 31857-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


130 Wn. App. 277; 122 P.3d 747; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2865



November 9, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review pending at In re Det. of Greenwood, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 677 (Wash., Sept. 6, 2006)
Review denied by In re Det. of Greenwood, 158 Wn.2d 1010, 143 P.3d 830, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 755 (Wash., Oct. 12, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant detainee appealed his civil commitment by the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) under the Sexually Violent Predators Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 71.09.


OVERVIEW: In 2001, the detainee was charged with first degree rape of a child and was found incompetent to stand trial. A year later he was charged with second degree rape with forcible compulsion. He was again adjudged incompetent to stand trial. The State petitioned to commit him as a sexually violent predator (SVP) under Wash. Rev. Code ch. 71.09. The jury found the State proved beyond a reasonable doubt that the detainee committed second degree rape with forcible compulsion. The court determined that the State had proved beyond a reasonable doubt that the detainee was an SVP and was likely to engage in predatory acts of sexual violence in the future if not confined to a secure facility. He was committed. He challenged the constitutionality of Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.060(2), both facially and as it was applied to him. However, SVP proceedings were civil and as such did not constitute prosecution under a criminal statute. The statute did not violate due process by permitting an individual previously found to be incompetent to stand trial in a criminal proceeding to be committed as a sexually violent predator. The trial court did not err.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1725 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Posey


No. 23041-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


130 Wn. App. 262; 122 P.3d 914; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2849



November 8, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review pending at State v. Posey, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 681 (Wash., Sept. 6, 2006)
Review granted by State v. Posey, 158 Wn.2d 1009, 143 P.3d 830, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 741 (2006)
Affirmed in part and reversed in part by, Remanded by State v. Posey, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 706 (Wash., Sept. 20, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Yakima County (Washington) convicted defendant of rape in adult criminal court, although defendant was a juvenile at the time of the crime and when he was convicted. The adult criminal court sentenced defendant to a life sentence with a minimum term of 119 months. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police arrested defendant and the State charged him with three counts of second degree rape-domestic violence, and one count of first degree assault-domestic violence, with a firearm. He was 16 years old when he committed the crimes and when the State charged him. He was charged but acquitted of first degree assault, which required the juvenile court to automatically decline juvenile jurisdiction. He challenged the automatic decline on several grounds, including violations of his constitutional rights to equal protection and due process. The appellate court concluded that the automatic decline statute afforded equal protection of law if the class to be protected was all juveniles charged with a serious violent offense. And the Washington Supreme Court had already held that the statute did not deny due process. The appellate court also concluded the trial court did not abuse its discretion by refusing to admit evidence of an e-mail suggesting the victim would have consented to violence and rape, citing the rape shield statute. Defendant did not have a constitutional right to be tried in juvenile court. He was not deprived of procedural due process; he was properly tried as an adult.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Gilbert


No. 32005-3-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2852



November 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Gilbert, 130 Wn. App. 1018, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3325 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 02-1-00324-7. Date filed: 07/01/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Russell W Hartman.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty to five counts of delivery of methamphetamine and one count of possession of methamphetamine with intent to deliver. The Superior Court of Kitsap County, Washington, imposed concurrent sentences of 108 months. He did not appeal. Two years later defendant filed a motion for relief from judgment under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8(b)(1). Defendant appealed from the denial of that motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant did not appeal his guilty plea or the sentences imposed. Two years later he filed the present motion on the grounds that the controlled substance that he had intended to sell was methamphetamine hydrochloride not methamphetamine. Thus, defendant claimed that he was improperly convicted and sentenced under Wash. Rev. Code § 69.50.401(a)(1)(ii). The trial court denied defendant's Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8(b)(1) motion as untimely under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090. The appellate court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion as the motion was filed more than a year after the judgment, defendant's judgment was valid on its face within the meaning of § 10.73.090 as it showed on its face that defendant pleaded guilty to the crime of unlawful possession of methamphetamine; that such crime carried a maximum sentence of 10 years; and that he was sentenced to not more than ten years. Defendant's sentence was not "in excess of the court's jurisdiction," under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.100 because the expert who opined that defendant only delivered methamphetamine hydrochloride did not examine, or even see, the specific substance that defendant was charged with delivering.


OUTCOME: The denial of defendant's motion for relief from judgment was affirmed.

State v. Bishop


No. 32124-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2858



November 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 04-1-00835-6. Date filed: 07/23/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Gary R Tabor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed her conviction of delivery of a controlled substance, arguing that the Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington, impermissibly commented on the evidence and erred in sentencing and that she received ineffective assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: The State arrested an individual on April 24 after he sold methamphetamine to an undercover officer. The individual arranged, in presence of the arresting officer, to buy methamphetamine from defendant. When defendant and the co-defendant arrived at a designated area, the individual handed the money to the co-defendant, and defendant got a bag containing a white, powdery substance that was later confirmed to be methamphetamine to give to the individual. On appeal, defendant claimed that the trial court improperly commented on the evidence by telling the jury that one of the exhibits contained methamphetamine. The appellate court rejected this argument as no one at trial had disputed that the substance was methamphetamine. Code §  9.94A.589(1)(a), there was no evidence that the crimes involved the same criminal intent or occurred at the same place and time. Finally, defendant's claim that she was deprived of ineffective assistance of counsel was rejected as she did not show prejudice.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction was affirmed.

State v. Carnahan


No. 31084-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


130 Wn. App. 159; 122 P.3d 187; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2770



November 1, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at, Remanded by State v. Carnahan, 2008 Wash. App. LEXIS 859 (Wash. Ct. App., Apr. 8, 2008)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Cowlitz County (Washington) convicted defendant of driving while license suspended (DWLS) and unlawful possession of a controlled substance (UPCS). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police initiated the stop because he recognized defendant and police dispatch had confirmed his suspicion that defendant's driver's license was suspended. A search of defendant's van incident to his arrest led to the discovery of methamphetamine. On appeal, he argued that: (1) the State improperly commented on his right to remain silent; and (2) the officers lacked probable cause to stop him because certain statutes related to the predicate criminal statute were subsequently held unconstitutional under City of Redmond v. Moore. Defendant's license was suspended under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.289. He was therefore entitled under Moore to have his DWLS conviction vacated. His conviction for UPCS had to be reversed because the State violated his right to remain silent by commenting on it and such error was not harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. But the appellate court rejected defendant's contention that the methamphetamine should have been suppressed as the result of an unlawful stop. The officers had probable cause to stop and arrest defendant, and Moore did not vitiate the probable cause for defendant's arrest. Thus, the case was remanded for a new trial on the UPCS charge.


OUTCOME: The appellate court vacated defendant's DWLS conviction, reversed his UPCS conviction, and remanded the case for a new trial.

State v. Scadding


No. 31163-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2721



October 18, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Scadding, 130 Wn. App. 1003, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3263 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Cowlitz County. Docket No: 03-1-01346-1. Date filed: 12/09/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Stephen M Warning.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the dismissal of charges by the Superior Court of Cowlitz County, Washington, against defendant for drug possession and driving with a suspended license, arguing that the trial court erred in concluding that Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.688 was unconstitutionally vague and consequently suppressing the State's evidence.


OVERVIEW: A state trooper saw defendant's truck traveling on a road and saw that defendant was not wearing a seat belt as the trooper could see the seat belt hanging down. The trooper stopped defendant for a seat belt violation, and when asked why he was not wearing a seat belt, defendant stated that he forgot. The trooper asked for defendant's license, registration, and proof of insurance. Defendant explained to the trooper that he did not have a driver's license, and instead was willing to provide a Washington Identification card. When defendant opened his wallet to get the card, a small clear plastic bag fell out of the wallet and onto defendant's lap. The trooper took custody of the baggie and defendant admitted, after being read his rights pursuant to Miranda, that the baggie contained methamphetamine. The appellate court reversed the grant of suppression of evidence and dismissal and remanded the matter for further proceedings as Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.688 was not unconstitutionally vague because defendant never claimed that he believed his truck was exempt from § 46.61.688, and the trooper was not required to know for sure that the vehicle was not exempt before he stopped defendant.


OUTCOME: The appellate court reversed the suppression of the State's evidence and dismissal and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

State v. Burkey


U23243-3-III, Consolidated with 23244-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TEN


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2663



October 11, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: SPOKANE. Docket No(s): 00-1-00801-6 (No. 23243-3-III), 03-1-02543-8 (No. 23244-1-III). Judge signing: RICHARD J. SCHROEDER (No. 23243-3-III), GREGORY D. SYPOLT (No. 23244-1-III). Date filed: February 28, 2001 (No. 23243-3-III), November 11, 2003 (No. 23244-1-III).
State v. Burkey, 129 Wn. App. 1051, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3173 (2005)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In linked cases, defendant challenged the orders of the Superior Court, Spokane County, Washington, failing to suppress evidence obtained during searches of his vehicle incident to three separate arrests for driving while license suspended (DWLS).


OVERVIEW: Police officers saw defendant's car stopped in the road. They learned that his license was suspended. Defendant was placed under arrest for first degree DWLS. During a search incident to the arrest, officers found a substance that field-tested positive for methamphetamine. Four years later, defendant was stopped for driving with his brake lights out. He was again arrested two more times for driving on a suspended license. During both searches of the vehicle, the officer found a firearm. The trial court did not err by denying defendant's motions to suppress the evidence obtained during the search of his vehicles. Because Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(a) made it unlawful to drive while license suspended, the officers were permitted to conduct the searches incident to his arrest. The fact that the one of the charges was later dismissed did not negate the probable cause at the time he was arrested.


OUTCOME: The orders of the superior court were affirmed.

State v. Sharpe


No. 32281-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2672



October 11, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Lewis County. Docket No: 03-1-00734-4. Date filed: 09/14/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Richard Lynn Brosey.
State v. Sharpe, 129 Wn. App. 1048, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3162 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Lewis County (Washington) of possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped when an officer saw that the year sticker on defendant's car license bag had been scratched off. Defendant admitted to driving with a suspended license, at which point she was arrested. The officer searched the fanny pack she was wearing, which contained a plastic tube containing a residue of methamphetamine. Defendant sought to have the evidence suppressed, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court rejected defendant's claim that the drug evidence seized should have been suppressed under Wash. Const. art. I, § 7 because her arrest for driving with a suspended license under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.289 was unlawful under case law. Because defendant admitted that her license was suspended and a records check confirmed that information, under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.31.100(3)(e), the officer's arrest of defendant was permissible, and the evidence seized pursuant to that arrest was also admissible, despite the subsequent invalidation of the driving while license suspended statutes in case law. The court noted that the statutes were not flagrantly unconstitutional and provided probable cause for defendant's arrest.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State v. Aarts


No. 32351-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2681

State v. Aarts, 129 Wn. App. 1048, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3163 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction for unlawful possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine, arguing that the Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington, erred in denying his motion to suppress and that his attorney provided ineffective assistance by failing to raise particular issues while making the motion to suppress.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for third degree driving while his license was suspended. The record on appeal did not reveal on what basis the defendant's license had been suspended. Incident to that arrest, the officer searched defendant and found methamphetamine in his pants pocket. Prior to trial, defendant's attorney moved to suppress the methamphetamine and argued that because the state supreme court had recently held that former Wash. Rev. Code §§ 46.20.289 and 46.20.324(1) were unconstitutional in that they required suspension of a driver's license without a hearing, the that the search was illegal because it was based solely upon the arrest for third degree driving while license suspended. The appellate court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to suppress and held that because the record did not indicate that defendant's license was suspended pursuant to the unconstitutional statutes, he was not entitled to relief. The appellate court also held that defendant was not deprived of effective assistance of counsel as defendant's motion would have been denied even if his attorney had argued that his arrest could not be justified under a good faith exception.

State v. Pittman


No. 32199-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2591



October 4, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 03-1-02090-7. Date filed: 07/27/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Roger a Bennett.
State v. Pittman, 129 Wn. App. 1043, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3142 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to a single amended count of third degree rape of a child. The Superior Court of Clark County, Washington, initially imposed an exceptional 24 month sentence as part of the Special Sex Offender Sentencing Alternative (SSOSA). When the sentencing court revoked the SSOSA sentence two months later, it imposed the previously suspended 24 months sentence. Defendant appealed the exceptional sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded guilty to a single amended count of third degree rape of a child, and the amended charging document alleged in one count that he had intercourse with two different underage females. Defendant provided a factual basis for the plea by admitting to the charged facts. Defendant had no prior felony convictions, resulting in a 12 to 14 month standard sentencing range. The court imposed an exceptional 24 month sentence based on its belief that two victims in one count implicated the statutory aggravating factor that the "multiple offense policy" of the Sentencing Reform Act of 1981 that resulted in a presumptive sentence that was clearly too lenient. Defendant appealed and claimed that under Blakely, which was decided six days after he was sentenced, the trial court could not impose an exceptional sentence without a factual determination by a jury. The appellate court agreed, reversed defendant's and remanded for resentencing. The appellate court noted that the sentencing court increased defendant's sentence beyond that supported by the guilty plea alone when it made findings of fact based on a preponderance of evidence, a procedure declared unconstitutional by Blakely.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was reversed and remanded for resentencing.

 

1736 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



City of Spokane v. Marr


No. 22604-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


129 Wn. App. 890; 120 P.3d 652; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2601



October 4, 2005, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two counts of public nuisance and two counts of pedestrian interference for panhandling. The Superior Court for Spokane County (Washington) found insufficient evidence of "aggressive solicitation" but found defendant guilty of two counts of pedestrian interference in violation of former Spokane, Wash., Municipal Code § 10.10.025(C) and (D) (1994). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to former § 10.10.025(C) and (D), a person committed misdemeanor pedestrian interference if, in a public place, he or she intentionally (1) obstructed pedestrian or vehicular traffic or (2) aggressively solicited. The trial court specifically found that defendant had not aggressively panhandled. The appellate court held, therefore, that she could not have been found to have violated the ordinance. The pedestrian interference ordinance proscribed only "aggressive solicitation" and no other forms of begging. The judge found insufficient evidence at trial to determine there had been "aggressive solicitation." Former § 10.10.025(B)(4) specifically exempted constitutionally protected activity from its purview. Begging was constitutionally protected. From the language of the ordinance, one could legally beg as long as he or she did not do so aggressively. An obstruction to pedestrian traffic by defendant was incidental to the non-proscribed and constitutionally protected activity of non-aggressive begging. The appellate court thus held that the city had failed to prove that defendant had violated the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed.

 

1737 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Estes v. Vashon Maury Island Fire Prot. Dist. No. 13


NO. 55950-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2575



October 3, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Estes v. Vashon Maury Island Fire Prot. Dist. No. 13, 129 Wn. App. 1042, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3140 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of King County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County, Washington, granted judgment in favor of respondent fire protection district on appellant citizen's claim that the district's policy of prohibiting possession of firearms by visitors to the district property violated state statutes and the federal and state constitutional right to bear arms. The superior court dismissed the citizen's suit. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The citizen challenged the district policy on three grounds: statutory preemption of local firearms regulation; the Second Amendment to the United States Constitution; and Wash. Const. art. I, § 24. The appellate court rejected the citizen's claim of statutory exemption where the fire district policy did not fall within the scope of the criminal firearms regulations that a prior court viewed as governed by Wash. Rev. Code § 9.41.290. The citizen failed to cite any authority for his contention that the Second Amendment was made applicable to the states and consequently to entities such as the district that were created by state law. The claim that the district's policy violated Wash. Const. art. I, § 24 also failed. The right to bear arms was not absolute, but instead was subject to reasonable regulation by the State under its police power. The limited effect on the general right to bear arms presented by the district's policy was minimal in comparison to the obvious benefit to the public of enhancing the safety of firefighters and paramedics on the job.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1738 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Morgan


No. 55001-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2543



September 26, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Morgan, 129 Wn. App. 1036, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3076 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of King County.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, who pleaded guilty to eight misdemeanor violations of a no-contact order and was convicted by a jury of felony violation of a no-contact order, appealed an order of the King County Superior Court, Washington, which prohibited him from directly or indirectly contacting the mother of his child.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued the no-contact order unconstitutionally burdened his parental rights and was therefore void. He contended that the trial court's oral ruling extended the prohibition to contact with his son as well. The instant court concluded that the trial court's oral remarks had no legal force since they were never incorporated into the judgments or the no-contact order. Moreover, the instant court did not read the trial court's oral remarks as prohibiting defendant from all contact with his son. At most, they prohibited defendant from visiting his children in the mother's presence. Finally, the trial court's judgments and no-contact order only prohibited direct or indirect contact with the mother. That prohibition was necessary to protect the mother and did not substantially restrict defendant's parental rights. Because the no-contact order applied only to the mother, was necessary to protect her, and did not prevent defendant from arranging for contact with his child, it did not unconstitutionally infringe his right to parent.


OUTCOME: The trial court's order was affirmed.

State v. Moody


No. 31697-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2439



September 20, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Moody, 129 Wn. App. 1032, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3061 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the trial court (Washington), which convicted defendant of first degree assault with a deadly weapon under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.011(1)(a). Based on two out-of-state convictions, the court sentenced defendant to life without possibility of parole as a persistent offender under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.030(32).


OVERVIEW: Defendant got into an altercation with the victim and stabbed him. Defendant claimed that the victim attacked defendant first. The court held that sufficient evidence supported a conviction for first degree assault with a deadly weapon in that defendant's conduct in leaving the victim's bedroom after a verbal altercation and then returning with a knife to commit a lengthy and violent assault was alone sufficient to support the finding of assault and the intent to inflict great bodily harm. The court also held that assault with a deadly weapon in Washington encompassed the California assault definition and was comparable to the California crime of second degree assault with a deadly weapon and that defendant's Utah offense was comparable to second degree assault in Washington. The State presented out-of-state charging documents, plea paperwork, and statutory provisions to the sentencing court to establish comparability. Defendant admitted the facts contained in the paperwork when he pleaded guilty to the out-of-state offenses. The trial court could properly rely on the admitted factual assertions in those documents to establish factual comparability under Apprendi.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

State v. Mahoney


No. 31990-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2442



September 20, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Mahoney, 129 Wn. App. 1032, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3062 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Clark County. Docket No: 03-1-01072-3. Date filed: 6/28/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Diane M Woolard.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Clark County, Washington, convicting him of first degree assault, unlawful imprisonment, felony, harassment, and a misdemeanor violation of a no contact order.


OVERVIEW: Defendant attacked his wife and ended up in a standoff with police. The trial court precluded the insanity defense, but it allowed the defense of diminished capacity. The court affirmed and held that substantial evidence did not support an insanity defense given the conflicting expert testimony and testimony by one expert that defendant was malingering. Further, because defendant raised the insanity and incompetence issues himself, it was reasonable for him to anticipate that the State's mental health experts would challenge his expert's testimony at trial. As to defendant becoming incompetent during trial, the court noted that before defendant's outburst, nothing in the record indicated that he was incompetent to stand trial. Also, the trial court properly admitted statements that defendant made to an officer while in custody for driving with a suspended license because the record did not indicate that defendant's license was suspended under the provision that had been held unconstitutional. The court also held that the prosecutor's misstatement of law that there was such a thing as a voluntary intoxication defense was not sufficiently inflammatory to affect the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court.

State v. Rogers


No. 22927-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SIX


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2401



September 15, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Rogers, 129 Wn. App. 1028, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3016 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Benton County. Docket No: 03-1-01219-3. Date filed: April 5, 2004. Judge signing: Hon. Carolyn A. Brown.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Benton County, Washington, convicting him of possession of methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped by police for a traffic infraction. The officers observed defendant make furtive gestures toward the passenger side of the vehicle while he was stopping defendant's vehicle. The officers learned that defendant's driving privilege was suspended. The officer searched the vehicle pursuant to the arrest for driving while license suspended. During the search, the officer uncovered a glass smoking pipe under the driver's seat and a baggie with white powder in the pocket of pants found in a bag on the front seat. Defendant argued that the evidence obtained from the search of his vehicle was inadmissible. The appellate court ruled that the search of defendant's vehicle was proper. The stipulated facts revealed that defendant's driving privilege was suspended. Nothing in the record established that defendant's license was suspended under one of the provisions found unconstitutional by the Washington Supreme Court. Hence, the appellate court had to assume that defendant was lawfully arrested and that the subsequent search of the vehicle was also lawful.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1742 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Hodgkiss v. Dietsch (In re M.C.)


No. 29818-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2406



September 15, 2005 Source of Appeal Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at In re Parentage of Hodgkiss, 129 Wn. App. 1024, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3002 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County Docket No: 99-5-01764-8. Judgment or order under review Date filed: 11/22/2002. Judge signing: Hon. Stephanie a Arend.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After blood tests showed that appellant alleged father was the child's biological father, the alleged father petitioned the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington) for an order establishing paternity and granting him residential visitation. The trial court essentially ruled for respondent presumptive father and dismissed the alleged father's paternity and visitation actions. The alleged father appealed.


OVERVIEW: When the child was born, respondent mother was involved in an 11-year cohabitation relationship with the presumptive father. The child's birth certificate identified him as the child's father, and the presumptive father filed an acknowledgment of paternity with the State Department of Vital Statistics (Washington). The trial court concluded that the stability of the present home environment would be better maintained by denying the alleged father's paternity action. That conclusion was supported by the unchallenged findings that the presumptive father provided consistency for the child and that the child had lived with the presumptive father most of his life. Also, the trial court concluded that there was no uncertainty of parentage in the child's mind as the presumptive father was the only father he had ever known. Further, the trial court concluded that the continuity of established family relationships would be better maintained if the alleged father's parentage action was denied. Thus, the trial court properly determined that the child's best interests were served by dismissing the alleged father's paternity action in favor of continuing the presumptive father's paternity.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment and declined to award attorney fees to either party.

State v. Walker


No. 31174-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2408



September 15, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Cowlitz County Docket No: 03-1-01222-7. Date filed: 11/19/2003. Judge signing: Hon. James E Warme.
State v. Walker, 129 Wn. App. 1024, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3003 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Cowlitz County, Washington, convicting him of unlawful possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: While on routine patrol, the officer observed that the passenger in defendant's vehicle was not wearing his seat belt. The officer ran a check of the vehicle's license plate and learned that the vehicle had been sold more than 45 days before but had not been re-registered, a misdemeanor. The officer stopped the vehicle, and the passenger was arrested on outstanding warrants. The officer conducted a search of defendant's vehicle incident to the passenger's arrest and found a baggie of methamphetamine. Defendant argued that his counsel was ineffective for failing to bring a motion to suppress evidence that was seized from his vehicle in a search incident to the arrest of the passenger. The appellate court ruled that defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claim failed. As a result of the passenger's seat belt violation, the officer had a legal basis to stop defendant's vehicle and obtain the passenger's information. The passenger's arrest provided a valid reason for the incidental search of defendant's vehicle. Because the search of defendant's vehicle was lawful, defense counsel was not deficient for failing to bring a suppression motion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Potter


No: 23371-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


129 Wn. App. 494; 119 P.3d 877; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2347



September 13, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by State v. Potter, 156 Wn.2d 1001, 128 P.3d 1239, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 7 (2006)
Affirmed by, Remanded by State v. Potter, 156 Wn.2d 835, 132 P.3d 1089, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 351 (Wash., Apr. 27, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State charged defendant with possession of a controlled substance. Defendant moved to suppress the drug evidence. The Superior Court of Spokane County, Washington, granted defendant's motion and dismissed the prosecution. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer stopped defendant while driving his vehicle. The officer checked the status of defendant's license; it was suspended. The officer arrested defendant, searched him incident to the arrest, and found methamphetamine. The trial court granted defendant's motion to suppress because the law under which defendant's license had been suspended had been determined to be unconstitutional. Thus, the trial court held that the subsequent search incident to an arrest was unconstitutional. The appellate court reversed the trial court's ruling and remanded the matter back for prosecution. The appellate court held that the trial court should not have suppressed the evidence because the police had probable cause to arrest defendant and therefore search him. The procedural provisions in Wash. Rev. Code §§ 46.20.289 and 46.20.324(1), although later found to be unconstitutional, were valid at the time of arrest, and were not so "flagrantly unconstitutional" as to require notice by the officer. The arrest was lawful, and therefore the search was lawful.


OUTCOME: The dismissal was reversed, and the matter was remanded for prosecution.

In re Fuel Tax or Prorate Assessment


No. 32421-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


129 Wn. App. 556; 119 P.3d 889; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2376



September 13, 2005, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant dump truck business challenged a decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington affirming a final order by the department of licensing (DOL) determining that the business was not eligible for a credit for taxes erroneously or illegally collected or paid under Wash. Rev. Code § 82.38.180(3) of the Special Fuel Tax Act (SFTA), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 82.38.


OVERVIEW: The business used "special fuel" for its operations. An auditor determined that the business had not received power take-off (PTO) tax credits to which it was entitled. The credit was calculated for the 21-month audit period, but the DOL's assessment limited the credit to a 13-month period. The business claimed that Wash. Rev. Code §§ 82.38.180(3) and 82.38.190(3)(b) granted it five years to pursue PTO refunds, but the court held that the up front payment of the special fuel tax was not an erroneously or illegally paid tax. Section 82.38.190(3)(b) precluded a refund without a timely claim. However, the business was entitled to a refund under Wash. Rev. Code § 82.38.180(1) because the audit included recalculating the business's initial tax obligation. The court also held that the business failed to present its equal protection argument for review because the business assumed that the DOL and it were similarly situated, but it cited no authority or argument for this proposition. Nor did the business cite authority for the proposition that a party's lack of knowledge of a statutorily established procedure demonstrated the constitutional deficiency of that procedure.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision and remanded for recalculation.

State v. Shipman


No. 23059-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2378



September 13, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Shipman, 129 Wn. App. 1024, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 3001 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: BENTON. Docket No(s): 03-1-00517-1. Judge signing: VIC L. VANDER SCHOOR. Date filed: June 18, 2004.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment and orders of the Superior Court, Benton County (Washington), that denied his motions to withdraw his guilty plea and his motion for resentencing for the offenses of second-degree trafficking in stolen property under former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.82.050(1) (2001) and misdemeanor bail jumping under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.76.170(1). Defendant sold a rented television.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that the trial court erred in denying his motion to withdraw his plea and in calculating his offender score and that he received ineffective assistance of counsel when he pleaded guilty. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying the motion to withdraw the plea without a hearing under Wash. Super. Ct. Crim. R. 7.8(c)(2) as the motion did not establish grounds for relief where the record showed he had proper notice of the charge to which he was pleading and that there was a factual basis for the plea. The court found that the record showed defendant not only obtained wrongful control over the television from the rental company by theft but that he also traded it to another person, which supported the additional element of trafficking of stolen property found in former Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.82.050. The court rejected defendant's claims regarding his offender score because his prior forgery convictions were committed on three different dates and involved three different victims; thus they did not qualify as the same criminal conduct as defined in Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.589(1)(a). The court rejected defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

Sakkarapope v. Board of Regents


No. 22708-1-III Consolidated with No. 22732-4-III and No. 22817-7-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL FIVE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2190



September 8, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals January 5, 2006.   [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court. County: WHITMAN. Docket No(s): 03-2-00168-4. Judge signing: JOHN DAVID FRAZIER. Date filed: January 16, 2004 (22708-1-III), January 29, 2004 (22732-4-III), March 5, 2004 (22817-7-III).
Sakkarapope v. Bd. of Regents of Wash. State Univ., 129 Wn. App. 1017, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2975 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff claimant challenged the judgment of the Whitman County Superior Court, Washington, dismissing his suit filed against defendant Washington State University, stemming from the University's dismissal of the claimant from the University's graduate program.


OVERVIEW: The University approved the claimant's petition to pursue entry into its Individual Interdisciplinary Doctoral Program; however, the claimant failed the required preliminary examination and was dismissed from the program. The trial court summarily dismissed the claimant's petition for review because it concluded it lacked jurisdiction due to the claimant's failure to file within the 30-day limit set by the Administrative Procedure Act (APA), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 34.05. The appellate court ruled that the trial court did not err. The University's actions were final when it denied the claimant the opportunity to continue his graduate degree on January 31, 2003. The claimant was dismissed from the doctoral program after failing a required entrance examination. On February 1, 2002, the University sent the claimant a letter affirming his dismissal; thus, the University's action was final for purposes of the APA on February 1, 2002. The claimant was allowed 30 days to seek judicial review, under Wash. Rev. Code § 34.05.542(2), and when the claimant filed for judicial review on July 23, 2003, the trial court lacked jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Rickert v. Pub. Disclosure Comm'n


No. 32274-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


129 Wn. App. 450; 119 P.3d 379; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2186; 34 Media L. Rep. 1502



September 7, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by Rickert v. State, 156 Wn.2d 1035, 134 P.3d 1170, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 398 (2006)
Affirmed by Rickert v. Pub. Disclosure Comm'n, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 716 (Wash., Oct. 4, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant political opponent challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington) that affirmed a decision of respondent Washington Public Disclosure Commission (PDC) that held she violated Wash. Rev. Code § 42.17.530(1)(a) when she made false statements about a senator's voting record in the 2002 general election and that upheld the constitutionality of § 42.17.530(1)(a).


OVERVIEW: The PDC found that the senator's political opponent violated § 42.17.530(1)(a) in that she acted with "actual malice or reckless disregard" in sponsoring a brochure that stated the senator had voted to reduce funds for and to close a facility for the developmentally challenged because the opponent had actual knowledge that the senator had not voted to close the facility and she failed to make even a cursory check of the senator's voting record. On appeal, the opponent claimed that § 42.17.530(1)(a) was unconstitutional on its face and as it was applied to her. The court held that § 42.17.530(1)(a) was unconstitutional because it was not narrowly tailored to the PDC's interest in promoting integrity and honesty in the elections process and chilled protected political speech. The court found that § 42.17.530(1)(a) was unconstitutionally overbroad in that it covered every false statement of material fact made with actual malice--regardless of whether it was defamatory-- and that it was not limited to defamatory speech in that it did not require that the candidate be damaged by the false statements.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court judgment and held that the false political advertising statute was unconstitutional.

Parsons v. DSHS


No. 55702-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


129 Wn. App. 293; 118 P.3d 930; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2165



August 29, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by Parsons v. State, 157 Wn.2d 1004, 136 P.3d 759, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 493 (Wash., May 31, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of King County, Washington, dismissed appellants', school residents, suit against respondent, Washington Department of Social and Health Services, challenging the department's actions to downsize the school, after the residents argued that the department's actions were steps toward closure, not just downsizing. The residents appealed.


OVERVIEW: The residents argued that the department had only the power the legislature gave it, and that nothing in the budget bills specifically directed it to implement downsizing. The appellate court noted that the legislature expected that the school would be downsized. The department had the authority to downsize the school without express legislative directive. Nothing in the statutes required that the school be maintained in a static condition. The legislature had greater latitude under Wash. Const. art. II, § 19 in appropriations bills, because budget bills allocated funds to a number of state needs. The budget bills were not substantive. The school's size was not the subject of separate legislation, did not effect changes beyond the two-year budget period, and did not define rights or eligibility for services. The budget bills did not change the scope of effect of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 71A.20.020 or 71.16.010(1). They did not require the department to close the school or affect the ability of persons with developmental disabilities to exercise choice as to where they live. The trial court did not err in allowing the Washington Protection and Advocacy System to participate as amicus.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

In re Det. of Albrecht


No. 22651-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


129 Wn. App. 243; 118 P.3d 909; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2153



August 25, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by Albrecht v. State (In re Albrecht), 157 Wn.2d 1003, 136 P.3d 758, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 487 (Wash., May 31, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: In re Det. of Albrecht, 147 Wn.2d 1, 51 P.3d 73, 2002 Wash. LEXIS 484 (2002)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant patient appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Spokane County (Washington) that ordered him committed as a sexually violent predator (SVP).


OVERVIEW: The patient argued, inter alia, that the evidence was insufficient to sustain the commitment. The court of appeals disagreed. Sufficient evidence existed to support the finding of a recent overt act. The patient approached a child and offered him a small amount of money to follow him. When the boy hesitated, the patient attempted to grab the boy's arm. The patient was a diagnosed pedophile with a 20-year history of sexually molesting prepubescent children using a grooming technique where he offered his victims candy and money to promote their contact with him. The grooming of the victims permitted the patient to commit a "sexually violent offense" as defined in Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.020(15). The patient's contact with the child was consistent with that pattern of obtaining the contact with his victims except for the fact that the contact occurred in an alley, not an apartment. However, that deviation was explained by the patient's housing difficulties on the day of the incident.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1751 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Keen


No. 32282-0-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2100



August 23, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Keen, 129 Wn. App. 1008, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2819 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Lewis County. Docket No: 04-1-00393-2. Date filed: 08/31/2004. Judge signing: Hon. H John Hall.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Lewis County, Washington, for possession of methamphetamine. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Following defendant's conviction, the Washington Supreme Court issued City of Redmond v. Moore, holding that statutes providing for mandatory suspension of a driver's license without an administrative hearing violated procedural due process rights. Defendant argued that the trial court erred in denying her motion to suppress because her arrest and the resulting search and seizure were not lawful based upon Moore. The trial court denied the motion, ruling that police had probable cause at the time of her arrest and that Moore did not apply retroactively to render defendant's arrest unconstitutional. The appellate court noted that the record did not specify under which statutory section of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c) defendant's license was suspended; therefore, she had not shown that her license was suspended under one of the unconstitutional license suspension provisions. The appellate court concluded that defendant had failed to show that the police unlawfully stopped and arrested her, unlawfully searched her incident to that arrest, and unlawfully seized the methamphetamine in her possession; therefore, the trial court did not err in denying her motion to suppress.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1752 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Regan v. Dep't of Licensing


No. 31848-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


130 Wn. App. 39; 121 P.3d 731; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2109



August 23, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Order Granting Respondent's Motion to Publish October 25, 2005.  [***1]
Reported at Regan v. Dep't of Licensing, 129 Wn. App. 1008, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2817 (2005)
Review denied by Regan v. State, 157 Wn.2d 1013, 139 P.3d 350, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 553 (2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant bail bondsman challenged an order of the Superior Court of Clark County (Washington) affirming appellee Washington Department of Licensing's (DOL) finding that the bondsman aided and abetted unlicensed bail bond activity and was in violation of former Wash. Rev. Code § 18.185.110(10) and revoking his bond individual agent and agency licenses for five years.


OVERVIEW: The bondsman's employee failed to renew her license, and the bail bonds program manager informed the bondsman that he could not have the employee working in the office. An undercover DOL investigator discovered that the employee was handling bond business at the office with a licensed bondsman executing the bond. The court held that Wash. Rev. Code § 18.185.010(6)'s definition of "bail bond agent" was plain and that common knowledge and understanding of the bail bond profession clearly encompassed the employee's actions. Therefore, § 18.185.010(6) was not vague as applied to the employee's actions. Reports showed that the employee was the sole negotiator on multiple bonds involving deeds of trust. It was unnecessary to read into former Wash. Rev. Code § 18.185.110(10) the criminal standard of accomplice liability as the DOL did not charge the bondsman with violating a criminal statute. He knew that the employee was selling bonds without a license. While the five-year license revocation was harsh, the Director of the DOL took the action with due consideration in that the bondsman received a hearing and the Director carefully reviewed the testimony.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the DOL's order.

 

1753 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



In re Pers. Restraint of Martin


No. 54558-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


129 Wn. App. 135; 118 P.3d 387; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2092



August 22, 2005, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a personal restraint petition challenging the authority of the Washington Department of Corrections (DOC) to seize money for the purpose of paying his legal financial obligations, restitution.


OVERVIEW: After the petitioner was convicted in 1994 of attempted robbery in the first degree and attempted murder in the second degree and sentenced to 300 months' confinement, the sentencing court ordered the petitioner to pay restitution. Since the petitioner was still incarcerated, he did not yet have a community corrections officer, and no payment schedule was set. The petitioner argued that because his restitution order required restitution to be paid on a schedule established by his community corrections officer, collection was to be deferred until he was released. The appellate court ruled that the DOC was permitted to start collecting restitution even though the petitioner remained incarcerated, had no community corrections officer, and no payment schedule had ever been set. The petitioner had no vested rights to the contrary. Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.772 changed the Sentencing Reform Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 9-94A, to specifically allow for collection of legal financial obligations during incarceration despite language in a judgment and sentence that would direct otherwise.


OUTCOME: The personal restraint petition was dismissed.

 

1754 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. N.M.K.


No. 54767-4-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


129 Wn. App. 155; 118 P.3d 368; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2095



August 22, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review granted by State v. Kirkpatrick, 157 Wn.2d 1001, 136 P.3d 758, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 441 (2006)
Affirmed by Wash. v. Nathan Michael Kirkpatrick, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 477 (Wash., July 12, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant juvenile was adjudicated as guilty of driving without a valid operator's license and reckless driving in the King County Superior Court, Washington. He appealed, asserting that the arresting officer did not have reasonable suspicion to detain him. He also asserted that the admission of a certified letter from a state agency, stating that no driver's license had been issued to him, was hearsay and violated the Confrontation Clause.


OVERVIEW: Police quickly located appellant's parked vehicle after a reckless driving report. Appellant gave his name and date of birth. He admitted that he did not have a driver's license and that he had been driving the vehicle. In the hearing on the admissibility of appellant's statements, the State offered a certification from the Washington Department of Licensing (DOL), indicating that there was no record of a driver's license for appellant. The defense had objected, claiming the certification was hearsay. The appellate court held: (1) there was no seizure at the point of encounter between appellant and the officer, and because there was an independent cause to question appellant, his state constitutional rights were not violated when the officer asked him to identify himself; (2) appellant was not in custody before his confession, and he was not entitled to Miranda warnings; (3) the certified copy of the absence of a driver's license was admissible because the document was not testimonial and thus unavailability of an agency custodian of same was irrelevant; and (4) a public record was the functional equivalent of a business record for purposes of the Confrontation Clause.


OUTCOME: The trial court's disposition order imposing a sentence upon appellant was affirmed.

 

1755 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



City of Yakima v. Skov


No. 23063-5-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


129 Wn. App. 91; 118 P.3d 366; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2069



August 16, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by City of Yakima v. Skov, 156 Wn.2d 1029, 133 P.3d 473, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 291 (Wash., Apr. 4, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's conviction for driving under the influence (DUI) was affirmed by the Superior Court of Yakima County. Defendant sought further review.


OVERVIEW: Prior to sentencing, defendant unsuccessfully moved to strike any sentencing enhancement based on his prior deferred prosecution for DUI. He argued that using an unproven charge to enhance a sentence violates due process. The court sentenced defendant as a prior offender under Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.5055(11)(a)(vii). Defendant appealed and claimed that the trial court erred in using defendant's prior deferred prosecution to enhance his sentence in violation of his due process rights and the principles established in Blakely v. Washington. The appellate court affirmed the sentence imposed and held that (1) defendant was not deprived of due process because defendant stipulated to the admissibility and sufficiency of the facts in the police report for the prior DUI in order to receive the deferred prosecution, and (2) the United States Supreme Court in deciding Blakely noted that its decision did not implicate earlier decisions upholding judicial fact-finding to establish mandatory minimums. Consistent with Blakely, the lower court used the fact of defendant's prior deferred prosecution to establish a minimum sentence. Thus, it properly sentenced him within the standard range.


OUTCOME: Defendant's sentence was affirmed.

Legacy Roofing, Inc. v. Labor & Indus.


No. 31722-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


129 Wn. App. 356; 119 P.3d 366; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1981



August 9, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 13, 2005.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 02-2-04217-3. Date filed: 03/30/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Theodore F Spearman.
Legacy Roofing, Inc. v. Dep't of Labor & Indus., 128 Wn. App. 1069, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2690 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee department of labor and industries cited appellant roofing contractor for its employee's failure to wear fall protection gear while on a roof at a job site. An industrial appeals judge found that the violation was the result of unavoidable employee misconduct and vacated the citation and penalty. The industrial insurance appeals board reversed, and the Superior Court of Kitsap County, Washington, affirmed. The contractor sought review.


OVERVIEW: On review, the contractor contended, inter alia, that the department failed to establish a prima facie violation of the Washington Industrial Safety and Health Act, Wash. Rev. Code ch. 49.17, and that the board erred in rejecting its statutory affirmative "unpreventable employee misconduct" defense. The appellate court found that the contractor did not argue that extraordinary circumstances excused its failure to timely object, and that its counsel conceded that the violation occurred. Further, substantial evidence supported the board's finding that the contractor did not effectively communicate the safety rules to its employees, that the contractor's unannounced inspections were infrequent, and that the employees caught violating the rules were not consistently counseled or fined. As such, the board properly determined that the contractor did not prove each element of its statutory affirmative "unpreventable employee misconduct" defense under Wash. Rev. Code § 49.17.120.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Holmes


No. 54965-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


129 Wn. App. 24; 117 P.3d 360; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1955



August 8, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Holmes, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2572 (Wash. Ct. App., Sept. 22, 2005)
Review granted by State v. Holmes, 156 Wn.2d 1001, 128 P.3d 1239, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 6 (2006)
Affirmed by, Remanded by, Sub nomine at State v. Potter, 156 Wn.2d 835, 132 P.3d 1089, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 351 (Wash., Apr. 27, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Superior Court County: Snohomish. Superior Court Cause No: 04-1-01035-1. Date filed in Superior Court: September 16, 2004. Superior Court Judge Signing: The Honorable James Allendoerfer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Snohomish County Superior Court (Washington) with possession of a controlled substance. Defendant moved to suppress the evidence seized from his vehicle. The superior court granted the motion, suppressed the evidence, and dismissed the charge against defendant. The State of Washington appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was stopped for a traffic infraction. The police officer checked the licensing records, which showed that defendant's license had been suspended in the third degree. The officer arrested defendant for violating Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c). In searching defendant incident to the arrest, the officer found a pipe of the type used to smoke drugs, pills, heroin, and cocaine. After being read his Miranda rights, defendant told the police that there was cocaine, heroin, and syringes in his car. The police then searched the car and found heroin, cocaine, and drug paraphernalia. Defendant argued that as his license suspension was unconstitutional, his arrest was thereby invalid, and evidence seized as a result of the unlawful arrest was inadmissible under the exclusionary rule of U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wash. Const. art. I, § 7. On appeal, the court found that the evidence was admissible under Wash. Rev. Code § 10.31.100(3)(e) as the police were not required to know whether defendant was afforded due process when his license was suspended to have probable cause to arrest him for driving while license suspended, and then conduct a search subsequent to the arrest.


OUTCOME: The superior court's suppression order was reversed.

 

1760 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Am. Discount Corp. v. Shepherd


No. 54017-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


129 Wn. App. 345; 120 P.3d 96; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1962



August 8, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication September 8, 2005.
Reported at Am. Disc. Corp. v. Shepherd, 128 Wn. App. 1065, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2640 (2005)
Reconsideration denied by Am. Disc. Corp. v. Shepherd, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2723 (Wash. Ct. App., Oct. 14, 2005)
Review granted by Am. Disc. Corp. v. Shepherd, 157 Wn.2d 1012, 139 P.3d 350, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 506 (2006)
Affirmed by Am. Disc. Corp. v. Shepherd, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 292 (Wash., Apr. 19, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant judgment debtors moved to vacate respondent assignee's 1996 extension of the judgment, contending it was void ab initio under former Wash. Rev. Code § 6.17.020(3) (1996). The Superior Court of King County, Washington, denied appellants' motion to vacate the order extending the judgment, from which they appealed.


OVERVIEW: A judgment was entered against appellants in 1986. The judgment creditor assigned it to the assignee; in 1996, prior to its expiration date, the assignee obtained an order extending the judgment for 10 years. In 2001, the court of appeals held that under then-existing statutory law, only judgment creditors could seek extension orders; assignees could not. Former Wash. Rev. Code § 6.17.020(3) (1996) was amended in 2002 to allow assignees to seek extension orders, and § 6.17.020(8) (2002) provided that the amendment applied to all judgments extended after June 9, 1994. The assignee argued that the 2002 amendments retroactively validated the 1996 extension. The appellate court disagreed. Under Wash. Rev. Code § 4.56.210 (a nonclaim statute, not a statute of limitations), when the 10-year period to execute on the judgment expired, the judgment lien ceased to exist and no action could be taken under the judgment. The legislature's attempt to substantively change Wash. Rev. Code § 6.17.020(3) and to apply the amendment retroactively violated the separation of powers doctrine. Therefore, the 2002 amendment to § 6.17.020(3) had only prospective application.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed.

 

1761 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lugo


No. 30845-2-II (consolidated with) No. 30849-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1941



August 3, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Lugo, 128 Wn. App. 1061, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2624 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 03-1-01186-3. Date filed: 09/10/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Daniel J Berschauer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After denying defendants' motion to suppress in a joint trial, the Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington, convicted defendants for unlawful possession of methamphetamine with intent to deliver and unlawful manufacture of methamphetamine. They were sentenced within the standard range, including a 24-month sentence enhancement for unlawful manufacture in the presence of a minor. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, defendants contended, inter alia, that the trial court erred in denying their motion to suppress as the arresting officer did not have an articulable suspicion to perform an investigatory stop. The appellate court found that because defendant driver did not specify under which statutory section his license was suspended, defendants did not show that defendant driver's license was suspended under one of the unconstitutional provisions of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342. Further, the officer had probable cause to arrest defendant driver for driving with a suspended license based on a department of licensing report he received. Thus, the subsequent investigatory stop incident to arrest was proper where evidence of drug possession, intent to sell, and manufacture was found. As defendant driver failed to show that his license was suspended under one of the unconstitutional provisions of § 46.20.342, he could not show that his counsel was ineffective for failing to argue the point. The extensive methamphetamine and manufacturing equipment, coupled with defendants' close relationship, was sufficient evidence to support their convictions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Thiefault


NO. 53214-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1896



August 1, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 01-1-00167-6. Date filed: 10/01/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Ronald X Castleberry.
State v. Thiefault, 128 Wn. App. 1056, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2603 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington), which gave assessed a life sentence under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA) for his conviction for attempted second degree rape. It was determined that defendant's prior Montana attempted robbery conviction and prior federal aggravated assault convictions counted as "strikes" for purposes of the POAA.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed his convictions were facially invalid. The court affirmed, and held that neither the Montana attempted robbery conviction nor the federal conviction were facially invalid because the convictions indicated that defendant was represented by counsel. Also, the POAA did not violate the single subject requirement of Wash. Const. art. II, § 19. The court also held that Wash. R. App. P. 16.4(c)(4) and Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73(6) applied to changes in the law that occurred after a petitioner's conviction and/or sentence. Counsel's waiver of a challenge to the comparability of the offenses was not ineffective assistance because Montana's attempt statute was narrower than Washington's, and while the Montana robbery statute was broader than Washington's, and the information was not included in the record so the court could not conclude that defendant's conduct violated the comparable Washington statute, defendant did not show that if his counsel had argued that the crimes were not comparable and that the sentencing court was not entitled to rely on the included materials, the court likely would not have given the State the opportunity to procure the information.


OUTCOME: The remanded for correction of a scrivenor's error, and affirmed on all other claims.

 

1763 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Tubbs


NO. 53482-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1908



August 1, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON COURT RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Tubbs, 128 Wn. App. 1056, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2604 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Whatcom County. Docket No: 01-1-00612-9. Judgment or order under review. Date filed: 09/26/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Michael F Moynihan.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Whatcom County (Washington) denied defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea to two counts of second degree child rape. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court's findings were not supported by the evidence and that the trial court erred in not having him present for the hearing on his motion. However, as the State pointed out, the motion to withdraw was barred by Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090 because it was filed more than one year after the judgment was final. Because the motion to withdraw was not filed within the time allowed by § 10.73.090, it was barred. Furthermore, Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.100(1) did not exempt defendant's motion to withdraw from the one year limit of Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090 because (1) defendant's claim that the confession was the only evidence against him and should have been suppressed or that counsel should have pursued suppression was not newly discovered evidence; it might have been a newly discovered argument but it was not evidence; and (2) the confession was not the only evidence against defendant because his daughter reported the abuse to the police and that fact was set out in the certificate of probable cause. Because defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty plea was untimely, it was barred. Therefore, defendant's motion was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

1764 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


Northwest Educ. Loan Ass'n v. Wash. State Grange


No. 31851-2-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1868



July 26, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Northwest Educ. Loan Ass'n v. Wash. State Grange, 128 Wn. App. 1053, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2525 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 03-2-00282-5. Date filed: 05/28/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Richard a Strophy.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff private guaranty agency sued defendant employer for failing to respond to a wage-withholding order arising from its employee's default on student loans obtained under the Federal Higher Education Act of 1965 (HEA), 20 U.S.C.S. §§ 1070-99. The Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington, denied the employer's motion for dismissal and ordered it to comply with the wage-withholding order. The employer appealed.


OVERVIEW: On review, the employer argued, inter alia, that the wage-withholding order was defective. The appellate court found that the employer did not assert any injury to its own personal rights. The property at risk was the employee's, and any injury resulting from its deprivation inured to her alone. Instead, the employer asserted the employee's personal rights, purportedly in an attempt to avoid a speculative wrongful-withholding lawsuit by the employee. But the employee was neither a party to this action nor had she successfully assigned her personal rights to the employer to act on her behalf in this matter. Moreover, the employer did not show how its interests as an employer, potentially subject to suit, were within the zone of interests to be protected or regulated by the laws it cited. Therefore, the employer lacked standing to raise its claims of unlawful delegations of authority, due process, and statutory notice, and the trial court properly dismissed the employer's claims. The agency was entitled to attorney fees and costs under 20 U.S.C.S. § 1095a(a)(6) as the employer refused to order the garnishment order.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.
