State v. Buchanan


54922-7-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1791



July 25, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Buchanan, 128 Wn. App. 1051, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2516 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Skagit County. Docket No: 03-1-00474-9. Date filed: 08/13/2004. Judge signing: Hon. John M Meyer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Skagit County, Washington, convicted defendant of misdemeanor harassment but found that she did not threaten to kill the victim, thus acquitting her of the felony harassment charge. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that there was insufficient evidence to sustain the misdemeanor harassment conviction, that there was reversible instructional error, and that the trial court erred in admitting irrelevant evidence of a prior incident. The appellate court found that the conduct and demeanor of defendant as testified to by the victim was sufficient for a rational trier of fact to find that the victim was placed in reasonable fear and that defendant would carry out her threats of bodily injury to him. The facts of the incident suggested that a reasonable person in defendant's position would foresee that her comments could be interpreted seriously. However, the jury was erroneously instructed that it could convict defendant under a subsection of the harassment statute that had been declared unconstitutionally vague and overbroad. The jury was erroneously instructed it could convict defendant under a statutory alternative, not charged in the information, that was not a lesser alternative. The errors could not be deemed harmless. The evidence of the seven-year-old incident admitted by the trial court was not relevant as there was no evidence that defendant had anything to do with it.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded.

 

1767 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Spencer


No. 30987-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1709



July 19, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 99-1-05040-3. Date filed: 10/16/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Katherine M Stolz.
State v. Spencer, 128 Wn. App. 1044, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2486 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, for the offenses of drive-by shooting and tampering with a witness. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The testimony at trial established that a shooter discharged a firearm and shot at a residence. Witnesses testified that they observed the shooter standing near a vehicle and flee in the vehicle following the shooting. When that vehicle was traced to defendant, further evidence suggested that he told the owner of the car to lie to police about when he returned it to her. The primary question on appeal was whether the evidence showed beyond a reasonable doubt that defendant discharged a firearm from the immediate area of a motor vehicle under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.36.045(1). The appellate court held that there was no evidence that the firearm had been discharged from the immediate area of a motor vehicle; therefore, it could only discern that shots were fired outside the residence during either a walk-by or a drive-by shooting and that a rational trier of fact could not have found beyond a reasonable doubt that a firearm was discharged from the immediate area of a motor vehicle. However, the appellate court concluded that defendant's failure to object to the allegedly improper hearsay evidence waived that issue on appellate review.


OUTCOME: Defendant's drive-by shooting conviction was reversed; however, his tampering with a witness conviction was affirmed.

 

1768 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Olinger


No. 23217-4-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


130 Wn. App. 22; 121 P.3d 724; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1728



July 19, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Granting Respondent's Motion to Publish October 18, 2005.
Reported at State v. Olinger, 128 Wn. App. 1045, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2492 (2005).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court for Spokane County, Washington, convicting him of one count of possession of a controlled substance, methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: The officer stopped defendant because he ran a red light. Defendant's driver's license had been suspended, and the officer arrested defendant and searched him incident to that arrest. The officer found two small baggies of methamphetamine in defendant's waistband. Defendant argued that the Washington Supreme Court held Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c) to be unconstitutional. Defendant challenged his conviction based solely on the argument that his initial arrest under the statute and the search incident to that arrest were unlawful. The appellate court ruled that the arrest was supported by probable cause and the subsequent search was also justified. Driving with a suspended license was still a crime, as Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.342(1)(c) was not declared unconstitutional. Also, defendant failed to satisfy his burden that his possession was unwitting. The baggies were found in defendant's waistband, and the manner in which the baggies were concealed indicated that there was some effort to conceal or otherwise not make the methamphetamine readily apparent.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. M.K.


No. 53304-5-I, Consolidated w/ No. 54780-1, 53304-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1695



July 18, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. M.K., 128 Wn. App. 1038, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2466 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 03-8-01277-7. Date filed: 09/25/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Gerald L Knight.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington, found defendant juvenile guilty of taking a motor vehicle without permission and imposed a 86 to 108 week manifest injustice disposition. The instant court granted accelerated review and reversed because the trial court failed to consider mitigating factors. On remand, the trial court applied mitigating and aggravating factors but imposed the same sentence. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: On remand, the trial court concluded that the aggravating factors outweighed the mitigating factors. In that respect, defendant was 15 at the time of the instant offense, which was committed in 2003. However, in 1999, he had received manifest injustice disposition for second degree assault, when he set a boy's hair on fire and attempted to set a girl's hair on fire. In 2001, he had received manifest injustice dispositions for second degree malicious mischief and third degree theft. In two cases, after he was released from custody, he "went on the run." He also committed all but the first offense while on probation. Based on Washington precedent, the appellate court rejected defendant's constitutional challenge to Wash. Rev. Code § 13.04.021(2), the statute that allowed juvenile offenders to be tried without a jury, and his argument that either Crawford v. Washington and Blakely v. Washington implied a right to a jury trial for juvenile offenses or required changing the burden of proof for a manifest injustice disposition from the "clear and convincing" standard to proof "beyond a reasonable doubt." The appellate court also rejected his argument that his disposition was excessive.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and his manifest injustice disposition were affirmed.

 

1770 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Austin


No. 54278-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1699



July 18, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Austin, 128 Wn. App. 1040, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2473 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-1-09014-6. Judgment or order under review. Date filed: 04/16/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Robert H Alsdorf.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father was convicted in the Superior Court of King County, Washington, of the domestic assault of the mother in the fourth degree. As a result, a no-contact order (NCO) was imposed pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 10.99.050 prohibiting the father from contacting the mother, but the NCO did not prohibit him from having contact with his children. The father appealed.


OVERVIEW: The father argued that order prohibiting his contact with the mother had a consequence of precluding contact with his children. Thus, he argued that it impermissibly interfered with his fundamental right to parent, and claimed that the statute authorizing the order was unconstitutional on its face and that the resulting order was invalid. The appellate court noted that Wash. Rev. Code § 10.99.050(1) authorized the issuance of no-contact orders in cases of domestic violence. The appellate court held that the NCO did not prohibit the father from having contact with his children, it only prohibited contact with the mother of his children; therefore, the father could not show that the statute interfered with his right to parent, at least as constitutionally recognized. The appellate court further held that while the NCO as imposed might have been an inconvenience, any interference was not substantial or beyond that which was justified by the need to protect the mother of the children.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Schimelpfenig


No. 31012-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


128 Wn. App. 224; 115 P.3d 338; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1538



June 29, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [***1] PUBLISHED IN PART


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Superior Court of Grays Harbor County (Washington), which convicted him of first degree murder and entered a lifetime banishment order. Defendant also challenged the sentence imposed.


OVERVIEW: After defendant was convicted of first degree murder, a lifetime banishment order was entered. Defendant then sought review. On appeal, the court determined that the banishment order was not valid because it impermissibly infringed on defendant's right to travel. The court used the strict scrutiny standard of review. Even if the interest advanced by the order were compelling, the order was not narrowly tailored. Defendant posed no threat to the victim's family upon his release, he did not desire continued contact, and the family did not frequent the entire county.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the banishment order and the exceptional sentence imposed. The case was remanded for resentencing. The conviction was affirmed.

State v. Greer


No. 53752-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1518



June 27, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Greer, 128 Wn. App. 1016, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2257 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 03-1-01909-1. Date filed: 01/28/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Charles S French.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington, convicting him of robbery in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: At sentencing, the State asked the trial court to find that the crime constituted a crime of harassment for purposes of entering a no-contact order. The trial court made its finding and ordered no contact with the victim, and defendant was sentenced to the middle of the standard range. Defendant argued that a jury was required to make the determination of whether robbery in the first degree was a crime of harassment. Defendant argued that in order to be convicted of the crime of harassment, a jury would have to find beyond a reasonable doubt that his actions fit the statutory definition of harassment. The appellate court ruled that the harassment finding had no impact on defendant's sentence for his current offense. No contact with the victim was a permissible crime-related prohibition, whether or not the trial court found the offense was a crime of harassment, and in the event that defendant ever harassed the victim again, he would be punished for that crime, not for the instant one. Also, defendant failed to show he received ineffective assistance of counsel, and failed to demonstrate that the prosecution committed misconduct.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Moore


NO. 54334-2-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1523



June 27, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Moore, 128 Wn. App. 1017, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2261 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 03-1-01007-8. Date filed: 05/20/2004. Judge signing: Hon. James H Allendoerfer.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Snohomish County (Washington) denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence obtained in a search incident to his arrest. Defendant was found guilty of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court found that while the officer mistakenly arrested him for refusing to give his correct name in connection with her investigation of violation of a dangerous dog ordinance, the officer could have arrested him for failing to give his correct name in connection with an investigation of a traffic infraction: failure to wear a seatbelt. The appellate court found that the fact that defendant was not wearing a seatbelt in a car required by law to have a seatbelt was within the officer's knowledge. Also, the appellate court found that the fact that defendant was giving the officer a false name was within her knowledge. Thus, the appellate court found that the facts within the officer's knowledge would lead a reasonable person to believe that defendant had refused to give his name in connection with the investigation of a traffic infraction, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 46.61.021(3) and .022. Therefore, the officer could have arrested him. Accordingly, the search incident to defendant's arrest was lawful. In addition, the appellate court found that Wash. Rev. Code § 46.61.688 - the seatbelt law - was not unconstitutionally vague.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Score LLC v. City of Shoreline


No. 55359-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1531



June 27, 2005, Decided


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Score L.L.C. v. City of Shoreline, 128 Wn. App. 1019, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2269 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 02-2-30555-5. Date filed: 03/29/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Nicole K MacInnes.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant adult cabaret challenged a decision from the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which affirmed respondent city's decision to suspend the cabaret's operating license.


OVERVIEW: Undercover officers observed employees at the cabaret engaging in unlawful sexual conduct. The city then entered an order suspending the cabaret's license. The superior court affirmed this decision, and the cabaret sought review. In affirming, the court determined that the cabaret's right to an objective and disinterested adjudicator was not contravened. Due process was not violated because the hearing examiner did not have a direct, personal, and substantial pecuniary interest due to an at-will termination clause. Next, the court rejected the contention that the cabaret was not responsible for the acts of its employees under Shoreline, Wash., Mun. Code § 5.10.070 (1997). Even though owners were not held responsible under ordinance, the license could have been suspended under Shoreline, Wash., Mun. Code § 5.10.120 as a public nuisance. Case law also put the cabaret on notice that it could have lost its right to do business based on the acts of employees. Finally, Shoreline, Wash., Mun. Code § 5.10.090 was not unconstitutional as vague, overbroad, or a prior restraint on free express under the First Amendment, Fourteenth Amendment, and Wash. Const. art. I, § 5.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

1775 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



State v. Stevenson


No. 30933-5-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


128 Wn. App. 179; 114 P.3d 699; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1484



June 21, 2005, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Skamania County Superior Court, Washington, which convicted him in a bench trial of one count of voyeurism involving domestic violence in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.115.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that: (1) the voyeurism statute was unconstitutionally vague and overbroad, and (2) the evidence was insufficient to support his conviction. Defendant could not mount a facial challenge because the statute did not punish thought, but instead regulated conduct. The statute was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to defendant's actions, nor was it overbroad. The court concluded that sufficient evidence supported defendant's conviction. Defendant admitted he became sexually aroused after his daughter walked through the kitchen in a t-shirt. Defendant "felt drawn" to the utility room, intending to masturbate while watching his daughter shower. Defendant admitted that he saw her arm or shoulder when looking between the blinds and the wall. He then moved to the center of the blinds, which he separated to see more of her body. The daughter testified that she saw defendant's hands on the blinds for several seconds and that he acted without her consent. Substantial evidence showed that defendant knowingly viewed his daughter for purposes of sexual arousal and gratification, without her knowledge or consent, in a place where she had a reasonable expectation of privacy.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hallman


No. 29726-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1496



June 21, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Hallman, 128 Wn. App. 1013, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2243 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 02-1-01019-2. Judgment or order under review Date filed: 11/15/2002. Judge signing: Hon. Paula K Casey JUDGES.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which convicted her of felony harassment in violation of Wash. Rev. Code §§ 9A.46.020(1)(b) and 10.99.020.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed her conviction for felony harassment, arguing that the evidence was insufficient and that her counsel was ineffective. The court stated that her counsel proposed instructions that incorrectly laid out the elements of felony harassment. As a result, it was probable that the jury convicted her of felony harassment without having found all of the essential elements of that crime, denying her due process and a fair trial. The court further stated that the trial court did not err in admitting evidence that defendant had previously pulled a gun on her daughter's ex-husband pursuant to Wash. R. Evid. 404(b). The State offered evidence of the earlier gun incident to show that her daughter, the victim, was reasonably frightened by defendant's current threats. Because the evidence showed that defendant was capable of using a gun to enforce her threats, and that the daughter knew this, the evidence was relevant to show the daughter's fear during the current incident.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment and remanded for retrial.

State v. Douglas


No. 33059-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Grays Harbor County (Washington), which convicted him of three counts of persistent prison misbehavior in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94.070.


OVERVIEW: While in the custody of the Department of Corrections following a conviction on a 2002 harassment charge, defendant committed a series of prison disciplinary infractions and was eventually placed in the intensive management unit at a correctional center. On December 13, 2002, and January 21 and 22, 2003, he committed several additional serious infractions. Further, the statute was not vague because the definitions in Wash. Admin. Code § 137-28-260(1) defined the prohibited conduct such that persons of common intelligence would understand their meaning and that there was no risk that a person would have to guess at their meaning.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, mother and father, sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which found in favor of respondent, the State of Washington Department of Social and Health Services, Division of Child and Family Services (department), and terminated the mother and father's parental rights to their child.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Lewis County (Washington), which convicted him of four counts of child molestation and sentenced him under the Persistent Offender Accountability Act (POAA), Wash. Rev. Code ch. 9.94A.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of four counts of child molestation and had two previous convictions for first degree statutory rape. The trial court reviewed defendant's previous convictions and found them to be "strikes" under the POAA. He currently appealed his sentence of life without the possibility of release. McCuistion v. State (In re Det. of McCuistion)


No. 30729-4-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1341



June 7, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No: 98-2-11149-1. Judge signing: Hon. James R Orlando. Date filed: 07/23/2003.
In re Det. of McCuistion, 127 Wn. App. 1054, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2134 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, committed appellant detainee as a sexually violent predator (SVP). Appellant challenged the commitment.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was previously convicted for attempted indecent liberties, which, according to Wash. Rev. Code § 71.09.020(15), was a sexually violent offense. At the time the petition was filed, appellant was incarcerated for third degree rape. Appellant argued that the county lacked authority to file an SVP petition while he was incarcerated for a crime that was not a sexually violent offense under Wash. Rev. Code ch. 71.09. Appellant also argued, inter alia, that chapter 71.09 violated ex post facto, due process, and equal protection; that the evidence was insufficient to support findings of mental abnormality and serious inability to control his sexually violent behavior. The appellate court rejected appellant's arguments. Third degree rape qualified as a recent "overt act," as that term was statutorily defined. Appellant had a history of criminal sexual acts. A psychologist opined that appellant had a serious lack of control such that he was likely to engage in predatory acts of sexual violence if not confined to a secure facility. In committing appellant, the trial court did not abuse its discretion.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Britannia Holdings Ltd. v. Greer


No. 55149-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


127 Wn. App. 926; 113 P.3d 1041; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1342



June 6, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by, Request denied by Britannia Holdings, Ltd. v. Greer, 156 Wn.2d 1032, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 419 (2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Britannia Holdings Ltd. v. Greer, 116 Wn. App. 1029, 2003 Wash. App. LEXIS 1633 (2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a holding company, obtained an $ 11 million judgment against defendants, a couple who ran an investment company, for securities fraud, and initiated proceedings to collect the judgment. In 2004, the Superior Court of King County, Washington, held the couple in contempt for disobeying multiple orders to deliver assets. The trial court gave the couple four months to deliver monies, or be jailed for contempt. The couple appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had also ruled that a trust created by the husband's father had lost its character as a spendthrift trust, and ordered execution on the trust assets. The couple also appealed that order. On appeal, the couple claimed that imprisonment as a contempt sanction was unconstitutional. They further claimed the order violated due process because they did not have the present ability to purge the contempt. The appellate court found that although there was evidence to support the court's finding that the couple were contumacious, the trial court failed to make a finding that they had a present ability to pay the purge amount. Instead, the trial court found they had, in 2002, possessed $ 635,000, and had "transferred the money away." That was not a finding that at the time of the contempt order in 2004, they could purge the contempt. Therefore, a reversal was in order because without said finding, the contempt was not coercive (to enforce compliance with a court order and allowed under the Washington Constitution), but impermissibly penal (disallowed under the Washington Constitution). However, the appellate court agreed that the trust had lost its protected character.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order of execution on the spendthrift trust because the trust had lost its protected character. The appellate court held the contempt order did not violate the constitutional prohibition against imprisonment for debt. But it reversed the contempt order, because the contemnor had to hold the keys to his release, and the trial court made no finding that the couple had the present ability to pay the purge amount.

Erickson v. Dep't of Labor & Indus.


No. 54781-0-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1206



May 31, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at Erickson v. Dep't of Labor & Indus., 127 Wn. App. 1049, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2043 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-2-08469-7. Date filed: 07/14/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Deborah Fleck.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant claimant challenged a judgment of the Superior Court of King County (Washington) that affirmed a decision of the Board of Industrial Appeals (BIA) that found the claimant had fraudulently induced respondent Labor Department to pay widow's benefits under Wash. Rev. Code § 51.32.050(2) of the Industrial Insurance Act (IIA) and that directed her to repay the benefits with penalties pursuant to Wash. Rev. Code § 51.32.240(5) (1999).


OVERVIEW: The claimant received benefits under the IIA as the widow of the decedent, but was later ordered to repay the benefits on the ground they were fraudulently induced because her marriage to the decedent was void since she never divorced her prior husband. The BIA and the trial court affirmed the Department's orders. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The court held that the trial court did not err in admitting the affidavit of the claimant's husband because it was admissible under the family history hearsay exception, Wash. R. Evid. 804(b)(4). The court also held that the BIA had jurisdiction to determine the claimant's eligibility under the IIA because the BIA's determination pertained to benefit eligibility and not the validity of the claimant's marriage. The court found that the Department was not barred from challenging the claimant's eligibility under the doctrine of res judicata and that the Department had proven the elements of fraud because the Department presented evidence to show that the claimant's divorce petition had been dismissed, and that she knew she was still married to her prior husband, which prevented her from legally marrying the decedent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court judgment.

In re Petersen v. King County Superior Court ( In re Pers. Restraint of Petersen)


No. 54065-3-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1212



May 31, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from Superior Court of Pierce County. Docket No:01-2-07997-8. Date filed: 12/07/2001. Judge signing: Hon. D Gary Steiner.
In re Pers. Restraint of Petersen, 127 Wn. App. 1047, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 2036 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner individual, a sexually violent predator (SVP) sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Pierce County (Washington), which dismissed his habeas corpus petition. He also brought a personal restraint petition (PRP).


OVERVIEW: The individual appealed the dismissal of a habeas corpus petition filed in the trial court and brought a PRP. Both challenged his commitment as an SVP. The court affirmed the dismissal of the habeas corpus petition and dismissed the PRP, stating that he failed to carry the burden placed on habeas and personal restraint petitioners. Further, there was no requirement of a response in 30 days for habeas corpus petitions. The 30-day rule of Wash. R. App. P. 16.9 did not apply to petitions filed in superior court, Wash. R. App. P. 16.3(b). In addition, his SVP hearing met the process of due process and his bare, unsupported, and conclusory allegations failed to show actual and substantial prejudice arising from constitutional error or non-constitutional error resulting in a complete miscarriage of justice. The fact that the State argued that he was not insane in his criminal trial did not preclude it from arguing that he had a mental abnormality because insanity and mental abnormality were not equivalent, Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.12.010. Rather, they required very different proof.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the habeas corpus petition and dismissed the PRP.

State v. Rosales


No. 22734-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1192



May 26, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.

PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: YAKIMA. Docket No(s): 97-1-01723-3. Judge signing: ROBERT N. HACKETT, JR. Date filed: January 12, 2004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Yakima County (Washington), which denied his petition for a writ of habeas corpus.


OVERVIEW: The inmate pled guilty to first-degree assault while armed with a firearm. Five years later, he filed a petition for writ of habeas corpus seeking to withdraw his plea, arguing that the plea was equivocal and lacked a factual basis, and that he was denied effective assistance of counsel. On appeal, he challenged the superior court's decision to deny his petition. In his brief, the inmate failed to discuss the one-year limitation on collateral attacks to criminal convictions set forth in Wash. Rev. Code § 10.73.090, or to reconfigure his arguments to fit within the exceptions to the provision. Thus, the court affirmed the order denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Further, far from being equivocal, the inmate's written statement described his conduct and expressly waived any claim of self-defense, except for purposes of sentencing. The inmate stated that he believed that he was acting in self-defense, but there was no indication that he also believed that the evidence was insufficient to convict him of the charged crime.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Gersema v. Allstate Ins. Co.


No. 31734-6-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


127 Wn. App. 687; 112 P.3d 552; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1175



May 24, 2005, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Pierce County, Washington, affirmed a decision by the Board of Industrial Insurance Appeals and held that respondent, a self-insured employer (the insurer), could offset his potential future industrial insurance benefits against his "excess recovery" from a third party tortfeasor responsible for his industrial injury. The employee appealed, asserting an unconstitutional taking of his property.


OVERVIEW: Specifically, the employee argued that because the insurer recovered all industrial insurance benefits it had paid him, the Department unconstitutionally took his property when it allowed the insurer to offset his potential future industrial insurance benefits against his statutorily defined excess recovery. The appellate court noted the employee received an undifferentiated settlement award for which it was impossible to determine from the record what portion was attributable to general damages, such as pain and suffering, and what portion was attributable to special damages, for which the insurer had already paid the employee industrial insurance benefits or might have to pay as future benefits arising from the same neck injury. The appellate court held that under Wash. Rev. Code § 51.24.060(1)(e) and (2), the insurer was entitled to a lien on the entire remainder of the employee's excess recovery from the third-party-tortfeasor settlement because the parties failed to differentiate general damages from special damages. The appellate court also held that Wash. Rev. Code § 51.24.060 was constitutional and that application did not result in a taking of the employee's property.


OUTCOME: The decision of the trial court was affirmed.

 

1786 of 2278 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davison


No. 54071-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1162



May 23, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 00-1-08720-5. Date filed: 03/26/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Catherine D Shaffer.
State v. Davison, 127 Wn. App. 1035, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1990 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of King County, Washington, convicting him of first degree assault and sentencing him to life in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was found guilty of first degree assault for shooting the victim in both knees. Defendant argued that he was deprived of his right to effective assistance of counsel. The appellate court ruled that defendant had not overcome the strong presumption that trial counsel's representation was effective. Defendant did not established that trial counsel's representation fell below an objective standard of reasonableness. Trial counsel presented a plausible defense. Trial counsel's questioning suggested that the victim implicated defendant in the shooting because he feared retribution from the true shooter. Trial counsel also appropriately and successfully challenged the admission of evidence before and during trial. Also, defendant failed to show that the trial court erred when it found him to be a persistent offender and sentenced him to life in prison without the possibility of parole. Defendant did not present affirmative evidence that constitutional safeguards were not provided when he pled guilty to his earlier crimes, thus, the trial court properly considered the prior convictions when it sentenced him as a persistent offender.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Sansone


No. 53584-6-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


127 Wn. App. 630; 111 P.3d 1251; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1142



May 23, 2005, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1]
State v. Sansone, 123 Wn. App. 1011, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 2868 (2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which sentenced him for violating a condition of his community placement.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his sentence for violating a condition of his community placement. The condition required that he not possess or peruse pornography without prior approval of his probation officer, and that the term "pornography" was to be defined by his probation officer. His probation officer found him in possession of photographs that she deemed inappropriate but defendant claimed that the condition prohibiting pornography was unconstitutionally vague. The State conceded that the condition was improperly applied to defendant's conduct in that instance, and the court accepted the concession. The term "pornography" was unconstitutionally vague because it was not defined with sufficient definiteness such that ordinary people could understand what it encompassed. Although delegation to the probation officer or treatment provider to define a term in a community placement condition could have been permissible in some circumstances, the vagueness was not cured by the delegation here.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded to the sentencing court for imposition of a condition on defendant's possession of materials that contained the necessary specificity.

State v. Betschart

State v. Hawkins


No. 31330-8-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1038



May 17, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Hawkins, 127 Wn. App. 1030, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1818 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Kitsap County. Docket No: 03-1-01382-8. Date filed: 01/05/2004. Judge signing: Hon. M Karlynn Haberly.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of Kitsap County (Washington), which convicted him of possession of methamphetamine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for possession of methamphetamine, but the court affirmed, stating that community custody in Washington was equivalent to parole. A person presently on community custody, placement, or supervision had a privacy interest that was diminished rather than absolute and, by the same token, a liberty interest that was conditional rather than absolute. Thus, the court rejected his constitutional challenge against Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.740(1) pursuant to U.S. Const. amend. IV and Wash. Const. art. I, § 7. Further, the entry into his home was lawful because that was the first time the officers were at defendant's house and they had no reason to believe that he would not be at home. They reasonably suspected that he was in the apartment. Defendant did not show that he failed to act knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently when he agreed to a stipulated facts trial, or that his attorney rendered ineffective assistance. In addition, the record did not show that his speedy trial rights were violated.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Young


No. 52529-8-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1009



May 16, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Young, 127 Wn. App. 1026, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1827 (2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Snohomish County. Docket No: 03-1-00981-9. Date filed: 06/13/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Gerald L Knight.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged in the Superior Court of Snohomish County, Washington, for first-degree unlawful possession of a firearm. He moved to suppress evidence of a gun found during the search, arguing that the initial stop was unconstitutional. The trial court granted the motion, and the case was dismissed. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: A police officer ran a registration check on a vehicle and determined that the vehicle's owner, defendant, had a suspended license. The officer saw that two people were in the car, but could not determine the driver's gender. The officer stopped the car and saw both occupants make furtive movements consistent with putting on their seat belts. As the officer approached the car, she noticed that the driver was a female and the passenger was a male. The driver was arrested on an outstanding warrant and defendant was arrested after the driver indicated that he had a weapon in the vehicle. The trial court suppressed the weapon on the basis that the officer did not have an articulable suspicion because she did not attempt to ascertain the physical characteristics of the driver and compare them with the information known about the registered owner of the vehicle. The appellate court held that the occupant's movements consistent with putting on seat belts provided for a substantial likelihood that wrongful activity occurred and was sufficient to justify further inquiry under an investigatory stop and that the trial court erred in suppressing the evidence obtained in the subsequent search.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and remanded.

City of Pasco v. Shaw


No. 22884-3-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


127 Wn. App. 417; 110 P.3d 1200; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 969



May 5, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review pending at City of Pasco v. Shaw, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 163 (Wash., Jan. 31, 2006)
Review granted by City of Pasco v. Shaw, 156 Wn.2d 1016, 132 P.3d 734, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 184 (2006)
Affirmed by City of Pasco v. Shaw, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 697 (Wash., Sept. 13, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: Columbia Basin Apt. Ass'n v. City of Pasco, 268 F.3d 791, 2001 U.S. App. LEXIS 20922 (9th Cir. Wash., 2001)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court of Franklin County, Washington, granted summary judgment to appellee city where it successfully enforced City of Pasco, Wash., Ordinance 3231 against appellant landlords, intervenor tenants, and intervenor corporation. The ordinance required residential landlords to obtain a business license conditioned upon presenting an inspection certificate showing compliance with health and safety standards. The landlords appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landlords argued that the trial court erred in concluding that the ordinance did not violate search or privacy principles established in the Fourth Amendment or Wash. Const. art. I, § 7 and granting summary judgment dismissal of those claims. Since the city's ordinance required a landlord to provide a certificate of inspection and did not authorize the city to search for code violations, the landlords had to prove governmental action by showing that the landlord was a state actor. The appellate court found that they failed because their authority concerned actions by a city building inspector and school officials, government employees acting within the scope of their employment. The landlords' preexisting private inspection right was consonant with the ordinance's regulatory goals. The landlords had the legal means to gain entry under Wash. Rev. Code § 59.18.150. The ordinance was not so vague that it could not be understood by an ordinary person. The appellate court focused on the facts and found that appalling dwelling conditions were well supported by the record.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

1792 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Nw. Motorcycle Ass'n v. Interagency Comm. for Outdoor Recreation


No. 22854-1-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE


127 Wn. App. 408; 110 P.3d 1196; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 970



May 5, 2005, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Review denied by Northwest Motorcycle Ass'n v. State Interagency Comm. for Outdoor Rec., 156 Wn.2d 1008, 132 P.3d 146, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 26 (Wash., Jan. 11, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from SUPERIOR COURT KITTITAS COUNTY. No: 03-2-00252-9. Judge signing: MICHAEL E. COOPER. Date Filed: 2/13/04.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff motorcycle association sued defendants, state agencies and environmental groups, and claimed that Wash. Rev. Code § 46.09.170, which authorized expenditures of state motor vehicle license and fuel tax revenues on recreational trails that could not be used by motorized vehicles violated Wash. Const. art. II, § 40. The Superior Court of Kittitas County, Washington, dismissed the association's suit, and the association appealed.


OVERVIEW: Wash. Rev. Code § 46.09.170 provided that at least annually the state treasurer had to "refund" one percent of the gasoline tax revenues for use in off-road vehicle (ORV) and nonhighway projects, including recreation facilities. The association claimed that § 46.09.170 violated Wash. Const. art. II, § 40 because refunds authorized by article II, § 40 did not justify use of funds from the gasoline excise tax to finance construction and maintenance of nonmotorized recreation trails and facilities. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's summary dismissal of the association's claim. The appellate court noted that the framers' intent in drafting art. II, § 40 was to return the share of those taxes paid by drivers who expended fuel driving on roadways other than public highways, roads, and streets. Thus, the refund was paradoxically a "highway purpose" for taxes levied on nonhighway driving. The legislature's dispersal of the refund came within its plenary powers of taxation, and the court found nothing in art. II, § 40 that prohibited the legislature from dispersing the funds as it saw fit.


OUTCOME: The summary dismissal of the association's claim was affirmed.

State v. Chaten


No. 52721-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 932



May 2, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 02-1-01597-9. Date filed: 07/25/2003. Judge signing: Hon. George T Mattson.
State v. Chaten, 127 Wn. App. 1013, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1883 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which convicted him of three counts of rape in the first degree after denying his motion to suppress DNA evidence. A $500 victim penalty assessment was imposed.


OVERVIEW: A jury convicted defendant on three counts of rape in the first degree and he appealed. The court affirmed however, stating that the trial court did not err in denying his motion to suppress DNA evidence and did not abuse its discretion in excluding other suspect evidence. Further, the determination of whether multiple serious violent offenses were "separate and distinct" criminal conduct under Wash. Rev. Code § 9.94A.589(1)(b) was not a decision that had to be proved beyond a reasonable doubt and decided by a jury. Thus, the court affirmed the trial court's decision that the three convictions for rape in the first degree were "separate and distinct" conduct under § 9.94A.589(1)(b). But, based on the State's concession that the victim penalty assessment should have been $ 100 rather than $ 500, the court remanded to correct the judgment and sentence accordingly. The court further stated that Wash. Rev. Code § 43.43.754 was not unconstitutional because a previous version of the statute was held not to violate the Fourth Amendment and those case law determinations were persuasive and controlling.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed and remanded for the victim penalty assessment to be $100 rather than $500.

State v. Vezzoni


No. 22361-2-III


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION THREE, PANEL SEVEN


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 864



April 28, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Vezzoni, 127 Wn. App. 1012, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1686 (Wash. Ct. App., Apr. 28, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Superior Court County: KITTITAS. Docket No(s): 03-8-00032-3. Judge signing: SCOTT R. SPARKS. Date filed: August 25, 2003.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court, Kittitas County (Washington), of dealing in depictions of a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.050, and possession of depictions of a minor engaged in sexually explicit conduct, Wash. Rev. Code § 9.68A.070. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant took photographs of his 16-year-old girlfriend's breasts and genitals and showed them to friends. Defendant argued, inter alia, that the convictions violated his First Amendment rights because the photographs did not show the girlfriend engaging in any sexual conduct or performing any sexual activity. The court of appeals disagreed. The photographs showed the actual exhibition of the girlfriend's genitals, unclothed pubic areas, and breasts. A reasonable trier of fact could have inferred that the photos were taken for the purpose of sexually stimulating the viewer. The photos showed the girlfriend engaged in sexual conduct and therefore constituted child pornography. In addition, it was not constitutionally necessary for prosecution under child pornography statutes that defendant knew the actual age of the person depicted. Thus, the statutes were not overly broad.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Biggers v. City of Bainbridge Island


No. 30752-9-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


124 Wn. App. 858; 103 P.3d 244; 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3708



December 21, 2004, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals April 27, 2005.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by, Amended by Biggers v. City of Bainbridge Island, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 862 (Wash. Ct. App., Apr. 27, 2005)
Review granted by Biggers v. City of Bainbridge Island, 156 Wn.2d 1005, 132 P.3d 146, 2006 Wash. LEXIS 9 (2006)
Affirmed by Biggers v. City of Bainbridge Island, 2007 Wash. LEXIS 784 (Wash., Oct. 11, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY:   [***1]
Biggers v. City of Bainbridge Island, 2004 Wash. App. LEXIS 3075 (Wash. Ct. App., Dec. 21, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Acting under the Washington Shoreline Management Act of 1971 (SMA), appellant city adopted a Shoreline Management Master Program (SMP), and ultimately placed restrictions on applications for new overwater construction and new shoreline armoring to preserve shoreline habitat. Respondents, a citizens group contested the SMP. The Superior Court of Kitsap County, Washington, granted summary judgment for the citizen's group. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the city first contended that two of the citizens, (a building company and a homebuilders association), lacked standing. However, the appellate court found that the latter two parties had interests within the ordinance ambit because the subject moratorium controlled said parties' island-based business opportunities. Thus, said parties did have standing. In addition, one of those parties had standing under Washington's "association" three-prong test. Secondly, the appellate court rejected the city's argument that the trial court erred in deciding it had no express or implied authority to impose the moratorium and that the moratorium conflicted with the state's general laws in violation of the Washington Constitution. In that respect, Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70A.390 was limited to growth management in selected counties and cities; it did not apply to shoreline management. Thus, neither Wash. Rev. Code § 36.70A.390 nor Wash. Rev. Code § 35A.63.220 granted a city the authority to enact shoreline management regulations under the Washington Shoreline Management Act of 1971. Finally, the Washington Growth Management Act (GMA) did not apply to shoreline development.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

State v. Gibson


No. 31017-1-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 841



April 26, 2005, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Superior Court of Thurston County, Washington, convicting him of failing to register as a sex offender.

State v. Wiatt


No. 30168-7-II


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION TWO


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 849



April 26, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Wiatt, 127 Wn. App. 1008, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1674 (Wash. Ct. App., Apr. 26, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of Thurston County. Docket No: 01-1-01136-1. Date filed: 03/31/2003. Judge signing: Hon. Gary R Tabor.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision of the Superior Court of Thurston County (Washington), which convicted him of 18 charges that included second degree rape under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.050(1)(b), third degree rape under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.44.060(1)(a), sexual exploitation of a minor, voyeurism, and furnishing liquor to a minor. Defendant also appealed his exceptional sentence.


OVERVIEW: Two of the second degree rape charges stemmed from charges that defendant provided alcohol to a minor, victim number one, had intercourse with her, and videotaped it. There was testimony and charges of similar incidents involving different victims. The court held that (1) the information was insufficient to demonstrate that the informants had a basis of knowledge that a videotape existed in that defendant told the informants about it, and the affidavit used to obtain the search warrant for defendant's residence contained no facts showing how a detached magistrate could have concluded that each level of hearsay was reliable; (2) while there was probable cause to search for evidence of rape, the videotapes and camera did not fall under the plain view doctrine because they did not give probable cause to believe that they were evidence of a crime; (3) defendant invited the jury to consider the possibility of date-rape drugs; (4) sufficient evidence existed to support both the convictions of second degree rape and third degree rape; and (5) nothing in the language of the instructions defining second and third degree rape suggested that the jury should assume that a crime was committed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the convictions as to second degree rape, sexual exploitation of a minor, sexual motivation, and voyeurism involving victim number one. The court affirmed as to all other counts.

State v. Earl


No. 54318-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 833



April 25, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:  [*1] RULES OF THE WASHINGTON COURT OF APPEALS MAY LIMIT CITATION TO UNPUBLISHED OPINIONS. PLEASE REFER TO THE WASHINGTON RULES OF COURT.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State v. Earl, 127 Wn. App. 1007, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1668 (Wash. Ct. App., Apr. 25, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Superior Court of King County. Docket No: 03-1-09466-4. Date filed: 05/03/2004. Judge signing: Hon. Carol A Schapira.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Superior Court of King County (Washington) of felony harassment in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.020(2)(b), (ii). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant told a woman that he was going to kill a police officer, his wife, and his children. Defendant was convicted of felony harassment and the court affirmed. The trial court's instruction defining a true threat tracked the definition approved in case law. It informed the jury of the applicable law and was not misleading. The trial court properly admitted evidence that defendant was angry about an officer's treatment of defendant during a prior arrest because it showed defendant's motive for making the threat against the officer. The fact that defendant harbored anger toward the officer was relevant because it made the existence of a material fact, whether defendant actually made the threat, more likely. Assuming the evidence of prior bad acts that the trial court agreed to admit was prejudicial to defendant, the court found no abuse of discretion. Under Wash. Rev. Code § 9A.46.020(1)(b), the State had to prove that defendant's words or actions placed the person threatened in reasonable fear of the threat, and the court rejected defendant's claim that the information learned after the officer perceived the threat could not have contributed to the reasonableness of his fear.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Exendine v. City of Sammamish


No. 54570-1-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


127 Wn. App. 574; 113 P.3d 494; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 684



April 18, 2005, Filed


NOTICE:

As amended by order of the Court of Appeals May 31, 2005.


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Reported at Exendine v. City of Sammamish, 126 Wn. App. 1067, 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 1451 (2005)
Related proceeding at Exendine v. City of Sammamish, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 61034 (W.D. Wash., Aug. 25, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owners challenged a district court's jurisdiction to issue search warrants to search their property for alleged violations of respondent city's code. Affirming a hearing examiner's decision upholding notice and orders issued to the owners, the King County Superior Court, Washington, ruled that the district court had jurisdiction to issue the search warrants. The owners appealed.


OVERVIEW: The owners contended the search warrants issued by the district court violated their rights under the Fourth Amendment and Wash. Const. art. I, § 7, because the district court did not have jurisdiction to issue search warrants for city code violations. The instant court concluded the district court had authority to issue the search warrants to search the owners' property. The search warrants were issued on probable cause for alleged criminal violations of the city's code, and the district court had jurisdiction for criminal violations of the city's code under Wash. Rev. Code § 3.66.060. The district court did not abuse its discretion in denying the owners' request to supplement the record with new evidence to challenge an interlocal agreement between the city and the county for court services. The owners did not challenge the validity of the interlocal agreement before the hearing examiner and provided no explanation as to why the evidence could not have been discovered and the argument made earlier. The hearing examiner correctly decided he did not have authority to rule on the constitutional validity of the criminal search warrants in this code enforcement proceeding.


OUTCOME: The instant court affirmed the hearing examiner's decisions upholding the notice and orders issued to the owners by the city.

 

1800 of 2278 DOCUMENTS



Devine v. Dep't of Licensing


No. 52380-5-I


COURT OF APPEALS OF WASHINGTON, DIVISION ONE


126 Wn. App. 941; 110 P.3d 237; 2005 Wash. App. LEXIS 645



April 18, 2005, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of the decision of the Superior Court of King County (Washington), which found in favor of respondent, the Department of Licensing (Department), denied his request for a writ of review, and refused to dismiss the revocation of his driver's license.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Licensing failed to provide the individual a hearing before the revocation of his driver's license took effect, even though he timely requested one. The court held that the failure to do so was a violation of his statutory right to due process. The Department offered a hearing more than four months after the license revocation went into effect. Because a belated hearing was not an adequate remedy at law, the trial court should have granted the individual's request for a writ of review and dismissed the revocation. The Department's failure to offer the individual a hearing until after the revocation of his license conflicted with Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.329. And, the Department, in violation of Wash. Rev. Code § 46.20.308, counted the 30-day deadline for requesting hearing from the date of arrest, rather than the date the individual received notice of his right to a hearing. That error deprived him from obtaining a hearing before his license was revoked, and therefore, it came within the class of errors that violated due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for further proceedings.
